Specified vs Unspecified Bequests: Attachment of Right
Distinguishes rulings for specified vs unspecified bequests

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi ruling on a specified bequest (wasiyyah bi-'ayn) from an unspecified bequest (darahim mursalah) when the value exceeds one-third, and apply the effect of destruction of the bequeathed item.

Core Idea
A bequest of a specific item attaches to that item; its destruction voids the bequest—unlike an unspecified bequest which survives into acquired property.

In the previous discussion, you learned how proportional distribution works for bequests exceeding the third. This passage answers a subtle but crucial question: does the same rule apply when the testator bequeaths a specific object rather than an unspecified sum? The answer reveals a key principle about how the legatee's right attaches—to the item itself or to the estate generally. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly handling bequests when assets are destroyed or change.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core question
The passage answers a question: what is the difference between a specific item bequest and an unspecified sum (like 1000 dirhams) when the value exceeds one-third? Identify the two scenarios being compared.
The 'presumed question' likely comes from a student who assumed both are treated identically.
2
Extract the rule for each type
For the specified bequest (e.g., a horse), the legatee is entitled proportionally within the third, but the right attaches to the specific item. For the unspecified bequest, the right attaches to the estate generally.
Note the evidence given: destruction of the specific item voids the bequest; in unspecified, it remains effective on acquired property.
3
Analyze the evidence (wajh al-dalalah)
The proof is not a text but a conceptual demonstration: if the specific item perishes, the bequest becomes void, proving the right was tied to that item. If the unspecified sum perishes, the bequest transfers to new property.
This is a rational proof (dalil aqli) using hypothetical scenarios.
4
Apply the rule to a hypothetical
Imagine a testator bequeaths a specific horse worth Rs. 5000, but total estate is Rs. 6000. If the horse dies before distribution, what happens? Apply the rule: the bequest is void because the item perished.
Contrast with bequeathing Rs. 5000 unspecified: if the estate perishes but new property is acquired, the legatee is paid from the new property.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سوال مقدر کا جواب
وهذا بخلاف ما اذا اوصى بعين من تركته وقيمته تزيد على الثلث فانه يضرب بالثلث وان احتمل ان يزيد المال فيخرج من الثلث لان هناك الحق تعلق بعين التركة بدليل انه لو هلک و استفاد مالا آخر تبطل الوصية وفي الالف المرسلة لو هلكت التركة تنفذ فيما يستفاد فلم يكن متعلقا بعين ما تعلق به حق الورثة
ترجمہ اور یہ اس صورت کے خلاف ہے جب کہ موصی نے اپنے ترکہ میں سے کسی معین چیز ( مثلا گھوڑا) کی وصیت کی اور اس کی قیمت ثلث سے زیادہ ہے پس بیشک موضی یا تہائی کے حساب سے مستحق ہوگا اگر چہ مال بڑھنے کا احتمال ہے پس عین ثلث سے خارج ہو جائے گا اس لئے کہ یہاں موصی لہ کا حق عین ترکہ سے متعلق ہوا ہے اس دلیل سے کہ اگر عین ہلاک ہو جائے اور موصی نے دوسرا مال حاصل کیا تو وصیت باطل ہو جائے گی اور مطلق ہزار میں اگر تر کہ ہلاک ہو جائے تو مال مستفاد میں وصیت نافذ ہوگی تو حق موضی لہ بعینہ اس چیز کے ساتھ متعلق نہ ہوا جس کے ساتھ ورثا کا حق متعلق ہے۔
Answer to a presumed question:
And this is contrary to the case when he bequeaths a specific item from his estate and its value exceeds one-third. Then the legatee is entitled to one-third proportionally, even if the property may increase so that it comes out of the third. Because there the right attaches to the specific item of the estate. The evidence is that if that item perishes and he acquires other property, the bequest becomes void. In the case of absolute thousand (darahim mursalah), if the estate perishes, the bequest is effective in the acquired property. Thus the legatee's right was not attached to the specific thing to which the heirs' right is attached.
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
This passage answers a presumed question regarding the distinction between bequest of a specific item (such as a horse) and an unspecified bequest (darahim mursalah). In the earlier discussion, the rule for unspecified bequests was that proportional distribution within the third applies. Here, the text clarifies that when a specific item is bequeathed and its value exceeds one-third, the bequest operates only within the third, but the right of the legatee is attached to that specific item. Evidence: if that specific item perishes, the bequest becomes void; whereas in unspecified bequests, if the estate perishes and the testator acquires new property, the bequest is still effective from the new property. This difference arises because in specified bequests the right attaches to the very item, so its destruction nullifies the bequest. In unspecified bequests, the right attaches to the estate in general, so it can transfer to acquired property.

Key Terms
وصیت بعین (wasiyyah bi-'ayn): A bequest of a specific, identified item from the estate.
دراهم مرسلہ (darahim mursalah): Unspecified dirhams; bequest of an absolute amount not tied to a specific asset.
حق متعلق بعین (haqq muta'allaq bi-'ayn): A right that attaches to a specific object; upon its destruction the right is lost.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a testator bequeaths a specific horse (worth Rs. 5000) but his total estate is only Rs. 6000, and the heirs do not consent, what is the ruling if the horse dies before distribution?
A) The heirs must pay Rs. 5000 from other assets
B) The bequest becomes void because the specific item perished
C) The legatee gets Rs. 2000 (one-third of estate) from other assets
D) The legatee gets nothing because the horse exceeded one-third

Key Takeaway
A specified bequest attaches the legatee's right to the specific item, so its destruction voids the bequest; an unspecified bequest attaches to the estate generally, surviving into acquired property.

Invalidity of Bequest Exceeding One-Third Without Heirs' Consent
Intra-Hanafi dispute on excess bequest voidness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Imam Abu Hanifa's ruling on a bequest exceeding one-third without heirs' consent, explain why preference (tafdil) becomes void, and evaluate the Sahibayn's opposing analogy as qiyas ma'a al-fariq.

Core Idea
A bequest beyond one-third is void; preference collapses with void entitlement.

Bequests are limited to one-third of the estate unless the heirs consent. This lesson examines Imam Abu Hanifa's firm position that any excess is absolutely void, and that any preferential distribution among legatees becomes void because the underlying entitlement is void. We will also compare this with the analogy of the Sahibayn, which the commentator rejects as an invalid analogy (qiyas ma'a al-fariq).

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
What does Imam Abu Hanifa say about a bequest that exceeds one-third without heirs' consent? State the hukm level and the consequence for the excess portion.
2
Trace the principle: voidness of implicit entails voidness of explicit
The commentator argues that since entitlement (istihqaq) is void for the excess, the preference (tafdil) that depends on it is also void. Compare with the analogy of undervaluation in a void sale.
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's opposing view
What do Abu Yusuf and Muhammad analogize? Identify the three cases (masa'il thalatha) they rely on and the common cause (illa) they claim.
4
Examine the Hanafi response: qiyas ma'a al-fariq
Why does the commentator reject the analogy? What is the key difference that makes the analogy invalid? Focus on the possibility of estate expansion in the three cases versus the present case.
5
Apply the distinction: specific item vs generic dirhams
Understand the hypothetical question about a horse and how the ruling differs for a specific item versus generic property. The attachment of the legatee's right to the specific item changes the outcome.

كتاب الوصايا
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد - ۱۶ حال میں اس وصیت کا نفاذ نہیں ہے تو یہ اصلا ہی باطل ہو گئی (یعنی وہ مقدار جو مشروع نہیں ہے وہ باطل ہو گئی ) اور تفضیل استحقاق کے حق میں ثابت ہوتی ہے تو استحقاق کے بطلان کی وجہ سے تفضیل باطل ہو جائے گی جیسے وہ محابات جو بیع کے ضمن میں ثابت ہو بخلاف مواضع اجماع کے ( یعنی محابات وغیرہ ) اس لئے کہ ان کے لئے ( مواضع اجماع کیلئے ) بغیر ورثا کی اجازت کے فی الجملہ نفاذ ہے اس طریقہ پر کہ مال میں وسعت ہو تو وصیت تفاضل کے حق میں معتبر ہوگی اس کے فی الجملہ مشروع ہونے کی وجہ سے بخلاف اس مسئلہ کے جس میں ہم گفتگو کر رہے ہیں۔
تشریح یہ امام صاحب کی دلیل ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ جب ورثا نے اجازت نہیں دی تو تنہائی سے زیادہ کی وصیت غیر مشروع ہے کیونکہ بغیر ورثا کی اجازت کے ثلث سے زیادہ میں اس کو نافذ کرنے کی کوئی صورت نہیں ہے لہذا ثلث سے زیادہ میں وصیت بالکل باطل ہو گئی اور جب زیادتی باطل ہوگئی تو دونوں میں مساوات رہ گئی اسی کو مصنف فرماتے ہیں کہ تفضیل باطل ہو گئی کیونکہ تفضیل استحقاق کے ضمن میں ثابت ہوتی ہے اور جب استحقاق باطل ٹھہرا تو تفضیل بھی باطل ہوگئی اس لئے کہ قاعدہ یہی ہے کہ متضمن کے بطلان سے متضمن کا بطلان لازم آتا ہے جیسے اگر بیع کے اندر محابات ہو اور بیع فاسد ہو جائے تو محابات بھی فاسد ہو جائے گی اور اگر بیع صحیح ہو تو محابات بھی صحیح ہوگی رہا صاحبین کا مسئلہ مذکورہ تو ان مذکورہ تین مسائل پر قیاس کرنا قیاس مع الفارق ہے اس لئے کہ وجہ مناسبت ( علت مشترکہ مفقود ہے کیونکہ مسائل مذکورہ میں یہ گنجائش ہے کہ ورثا کی اجازت کے بغیر پوری وصیت نافذ ہو جائے جب کہ مال میں اتنی وسعت ہو کہ موضی یہ کے علاوہ اس کا دو گنا مال موجود ہو اور مسئلہ مذکورہ میں ورثہ کی اجازت کے بغیر پورے مال میں نفاذ وصیت کی کوئی صورت نہیں ہے ورنہ خلاف مشروع لازم آئے گا ( کما ہو ظاہر ) اس وجہ سے مسئلہ مذکورہ میں اور مسائل ثلاثہ میں فرق کرنا پڑا کہ ان تینوں کے اندر مال کی وسعت کی صورت میں پورا موضی یہ موضی لی کومل سکتا ہے اور مسئلہ مذکورہ میں نہیں مل سکتا اس لئے کہ اس میں تفاضل کا اعتبار نہیں کیا گیا اور مسائل ثلاثہ میں تفاضل کا اعتبار کر کے مقدار ثلث سے زیادہ ہونے کی صورت میں بھی حق کے تناسب کا لحاظ رکھا گیا ہے۔
سوال مقدر کا جواب
وهذا بخلاف ما اذا اوصى بعين من تركته وقيمته تزيد على الثلث فانه يضرب بالثلث وان احتمل ان يزيد المال فيخرج من الثلث لان هناك الحق تعلق بعين التركة بدليل انه لو هلک و استفاد مالا آخر تبطل الوصية وفي الالف المرسلة لو هلكت التركة تنفذ فيما يستفاد فلم يكن متعلقا بعين ما تعلق به حق الورثة
ترجمہ اور یہ اس صورت کے خلاف ہے جب کہ موصی نے اپنے ترکہ میں سے کسی معین چیز ( مثلا گھوڑا) کی وصیت کی اور اس کی قیمت ثلث سے زیادہ ہے پس بیشک موضی یا تہائی کے حساب سے مستحق ہوگا اگر چہ مال بڑھنے کا احتمال ہے پس عین ثلث سے خارج ہو جائے گا اس لئے کہ یہاں موصی لہ کا حق عین ترکہ سے متعلق ہوا ہے اس دلیل سے کہ اگر عین ہلاک ہو جائے اور موصی نے دوسرا مال حاصل کیا تو وصیت باطل ہو جائے گی اور مطلق ہزار میں اگر تر کہ ہلاک ہو جائے تو مال مستفاد میں وصیت نافذ ہوگی تو حق موضی لہ بعینہ اس چیز کے ساتھ متعلق نہ ہوا جس کے ساتھ ورثا کا حق متعلق ہے۔
تشریح یہاں سے مصنف ایک سوال مقدر کا جواب دینا چاہتے ہیں۔ سوال آپ کی تقریر کا خلاصہ یہ ہوا کہ اگر موضی بہ کے علاوہ اور مال نکل سکے تو چونکہ اس صورت میں پورے موصی بہ میں وصیت کا نفاذ ہو جائے گا اور ہم آپ کو ایسی مثال دکھا سکتے ہیں کہ وہاں پر معنی موجود ہیں اس کے باوجود بھی وہاں ثلث سے زیادہ حق کا تناسب محفوظ نہیں ہے جو مسائل ثلاثہ میں ہے مثلاً زید نے اپنے گھوڑے کی وصیت خالد کے لئے کی یعنی پورے کی اور بکر کے لئے ثلث کی اور اس گھوڑے کے علاوہ زید نے کوئی اور مال نہیں چھوڑا، تو یہاں حق کے تناسب کا لحاظ ہونا چاہئے حالانکہ یہاں بھی آپ نے یہی فرمایا ہے کہ دونوں ثالث کے اندر آدھے کے شریک ہونگے حالانکہ مسائل ثلاثہ والی وجہ یہاں بھی موجود ہے یعنی ہو سکتا ہے کہ اس گھوڑے کے علاوہ اور مال حاصل ہو جائے تو پھر پورے گھوڑے کے اندر وصیت جاری ہوگی ؟
جواب آپ کا سوال معقول ہے اور وہ وجہ یہاں پر موجود ہے اس کے باوجود بھی دراہم مرسلہ والا حکم اس کو نہیں دیا گیا ہے جس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ اس گھوڑے اور دراہم مرسلہ میں فرق ہے اور وہ فرق یہ ہے کہ گھوڑے والی صورت میں موصی لیہ کا حق اس معین گھوڑے کے ساتھ متعلق ہے کیونکہ اگر یہ گھوڑ اہلاک ہو جائے تو وصیت باطل ہو جائے گی اگر چہ موسی کو گھوڑے کے ہلاک ہونے کے بعد اور مال بھی حاصل ہو گیا ہو تب بھی وصیت باطل ہوگی اس کا حق بعینہ اس گھوڑے میں تھا اور جب وہ ہلاک ہو گیا تو اس کا حق بھی باطل ہو گیا۔ اور اور اہم مرسلہ کی صورت میں اس کا حق کسی معین دراہم کے ساتھ نہیں لہذا اگر بعد وصیت ترکہ ہلاک ہو جائے اور پھر دوسرا مال مستفاد ہو تو موصی اہ کا حق برقرار ہے، تو اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ گھوڑے کے اندر تہائی تک موصی لیہ کا حق ہے اور بعینہ اس گھوڑے کے اندر تہائی کے علاوہ نہیں ورنا کا حق ہے اور دراہم مرسلہ کی صورت میں بعینہ جس مال کے ساتھ ورثہ کا حق متعلق ہے اس کے ساتھ موصی لیہ کا حق متعلق نہیں ہے، بہر حال ان دونوں میں فرق مذکور کی وجہ سے دونوں کے حکم میں فرق کیا گیا ہے۔
The Book of Bequests. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary of Hidayah Volume 16. Now, this bequest is not enforceable, so it is totally void (i.e., the amount that is not prescribed is void). And preference (tafdil) is established in respect of entitlement (istihqaq); so due to the voidness of entitlement, preference becomes void, like the undervaluation (muhabat) that is established within a sale, contrary to the cases of consensus (mawadi' ijma'), because for them (the cases of consensus) there is enforcement in some way without the heirs' consent, in such a way that if there is expansion of wealth, the bequest will be considered valid in respect of preference, due to its being prescribed in some way, unlike this case under discussion. Explanation: This is Imam Abu Hanifa's proof, the gist of which is that when the heirs have not consented, a bequest of more than one-third is unlegislated because without the heirs' consent there is no way to enforce it beyond one-third; therefore the bequest beyond one-third is absolutely void. When the excess became void, equality remained between them. The author says this: that preference (tafdil) became void because preference is established within entitlement, and when entitlement is void, preference also becomes void, for the rule is that the voidness of the implicit entails the voidness of the explicit. For example, if there is undervaluation in a sale and the sale is void, then the undervaluation is also void; if the sale is valid, the undervaluation is valid. As for the case of the Sahibayn mentioned, analogizing it to the three mentioned cases is an analogy with a difference (qiyas ma'a al-fariq), because the common cause (illa) is missing; indeed in the mentioned cases there is scope for the entire bequest to be enforced without the heirs' consent when the estate has such expansion that besides the bequeathed item there exists double its value. In the present case there is no way to enforce the bequest in the entire estate without the heirs' consent; otherwise unlegislated action would be necessary. Hence a distinction had to be made between the present case and the three cases (masa'il thalatha) because in those three, in the case of expansion of wealth, the entire bequeathed item can reach the legatee, while in the present case it cannot, because here preference is not considered, whereas in the three cases preference is considered and the proportion of entitlement is maintained even when the amount exceeds one-third. Answer to a hypothetical question: And this is contrary to the case where he bequeaths a specific item from his estate and its value exceeds one-third, then he strikes with one-third, even if there is a possibility that the estate may increase and it comes out from one-third, because there the right is attached to the specific estate (ayn al-tarika), evidenced by the fact that if it perishes and he acquires other property, the bequest becomes void. In the case of released dirhams (mursala), if the estate perishes, it is enforced in the acquired property, so it is not attached to the specific thing to which the heirs' right is attached. Translation: And this is opposite to the case when the testator bequeaths a specific thing (e.g., a horse) from his estate and its value is more than one-third, then the legatee will be entitled to one-third, even if there is possibility of increase in wealth; it comes out from one-third because here the legatee's right is attached to the specific estate, on evidence that if the specific thing perishes and the testator acquires other property, the bequest becomes void. In the case of absolute (mursal) thousands, if the estate perishes, the bequest is enforced in the acquired property, so the legatee's right is not attached to the specific thing to which the heirs' right is attached. Explanation: Here the author intends to answer a hypothetical question. Question: The summary of your argument is that if other property besides the bequeathed item can be obtained, then because in that case the entire bequeathed item will be enforced, we can show you an example where the meaning exists despite which the proportion of right beyond one-third is not preserved, as in the three cases: for example, Zayd bequeaths his horse to Khalid (i.e., the whole) and to Bakr one-third, and besides the horse Zayd leaves no other property. Here the proportion of right should be considered, yet you say that both will share one-third equally, even though the reason of the three cases also exists here, i.e., it is possible that besides the horse other property may be obtained, then the whole horse bequest would be carried out? Answer: Your question is reasonable, and that reason is present here, yet the ruling of released dirhams is not given to it. The reason is that there is a difference between this horse and released dirhams, and that difference is that in the horse case, the legatee's right is attached to that specific horse, because if the horse perishes, the bequest becomes void, even if after the horse's perishing the testator acquires other property, the bequest is still void. His right was specifically in that horse, and when it perished, his right also perished. In the case of released dirhams, his right is not attached to any specific dirhams; therefore if after bequest the estate perishes and then other property is acquired, the legatee's right remains. So from this it is known that in the horse case the legatee has a right to one-third, and specifically in that horse, not beyond one-third, and the heirs have the right, while in the case of released dirhams the legatee's right is not attached to the specific property to which the heirs' right is attached. In any case, due to this difference, a distinction has been made in their rulings.
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the validity of a bequest that exceeds one-third of the estate when the heirs do not consent. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that such a bequest is void in the excess portion, and the preference (tafdil) between legatees also becomes void because entitlement (istihqaq) is void. The commentator explains that if a testator bequeaths more than one-third without heirs' consent, the excess is unenforceable; therefore the bequest reduces to one-third, and any preferential distribution among legatees is annulled. The rule is that when the implicit (entitlement) is void, the explicit (preference) necessarily goes void. An analogy is given: in a sale, undervaluation is void if the sale is void. The passage then contrasts the present case with three cases (masa'il thalatha) where the bequest can be fully enforced if the estate expands sufficiently. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) analogize the present case to those three, but the commentator refutes this as qiyas ma'a al-fariq (analogy with a difference), because in the three cases there is a possibility of expansion of wealth that can accommodate the full bequest, whereas in the present case there is no such possibility—the excess is absolutely void. Finally, a hypothetical question is addressed: if a specific item (e.g., a horse) is bequeathed and its value exceeds one-third, why is it not treated like generic dirhams? The answer is that the legatee's right is attached to the specific item; if it perishes, the bequest is void, unlike generic property where the right continues in acquired wealth. This distinction preserves the heirs' entitlement and maintains the rule that the legatee gets only one-third of the specific item.

Key Terms
وصیت (wasiyyah): A bequest made by a testator (musi) for the benefit of a legatee (musa lahu), valid only within one-third of the estate unless heirs consent.
ثلث (thulth): One-third of the net estate after debts and funeral expenses; the maximum that can be bequeathed without heirs' consent.
تفضیل (tafdil): Preference given to one legatee over another in the share of the bequest.
استحقاق (istihqaq): Entitlement to a share of the bequest; the right that is established in the legatee's favor.
قیاس مع الفارق (qiyas ma'a al-fariq): An analogy that is invalid because of a significant difference between the two cases, rendering the common cause (illa) absent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if Zayd bequeaths a horse worth half his estate to Khalid, and his heirs do not consent, what happens?
A) Khalid takes the whole horse, and the heirs get nothing.
B) Khalid takes one-third of the horse, and two-thirds belongs to heirs.
C) The bequest is void entirely because it exceeds one-third.
D) Khalid takes half the horse, and the heirs take half.

Key Takeaway
A bequest beyond one-third requires heirs' consent; without it, the excess is void and any preferential distribution falls.

Bequest of 'Share of My Son' vs 'Like the Share of My Son'
Ruling on bequeathing the son's actual share vs. something similar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on bequeathing the son's actual share versus the like of the son's share, and explain the legal reasoning that distinguishes the two cases.

Core Idea
Bequeathing your son's actual share is void; bequeathing the like of it is valid.

This passage from Al-Quduri presents a critical distinction in bequests: saying 'I bequeath my son's share to X' versus 'I bequeath the like of my son's share.' Though the wording is similar, the legal effect is opposite. The key lies in ownership—a testator can only bequeath what he owns at the time of death. Let's explore the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios and their rulings
First: bequest of the son's actual share (nasib) is void (batil). Second: bequest of the like (mithl) of the son's share is valid (jaa'iz). Know these rulings clearly.
The ruling is from Quduri, representing the relied-upon Hanafi position.
2
Understand the reasoning for the first case
The share of the son is a future right that vests in the son after death. At the time of bequest, the testator does not own that share. Hence, it is a bequest of another's property (wasiyyah bi mal al-ghayr), which is void.
This is a rational (aqli) proof: the testator cannot give what he does not own.
3
Understand the reasoning for the second case
The 'like' (mithl) of the son's share is a different entity. It is something similar in quantity/value but not the same as the son's future share. The testator can bequeath an equivalent amount from his own estate because he owns it now.
Mithl is considered other (ghayr) than the original.
4
Note the intra-madhhab dispute with Imam Zufar
Imam Zufar held both bequests valid, focusing on the present ownership—since the testator currently owns the entire estate, the son's share is not yet separated. The Hanafi majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) rejects this.
Zufar's view is not relied upon (marjuh).
5
Recognise the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: under the majority view, the legatee gets nothing from the first bequest; under Zufar's view, he would receive the share. Fatwa follows the majority.
This illustrates how a subtle legal point can change outcomes.

قال واذا اوصى بنصيب ابنه قالوصية باطلة ولو اوصى بمثل نصيب ابنه جازلان الاول وصية بمال الغير لان نصيب الابن مايصيبه بعد الموت والثانى وصية بمثل نصيب الابن ومثل الشئى غيرة وان كان يتقدربه فيجوز وقال زفر تجوز فى الأول ايضا فنظر الى الحال والكل ماله فيه وجوابه ما قلنا ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جب موصی نے اپنے بیٹے کے حصہ کی وصیت کی تو وصیت باطل ہے اور اگر اپنے بیٹے کے حصہ کے مثل کی وصیت کی تو جائز ہے اس لئے کہ اول غیر کے مال کی وصیت ہے اس لئے کہ بیٹے کا حصہ وہ ہے جو اس کو موت کے بعد ملے گا اور ثانی بیٹے کے حصہ کے مشکل کی وصیت ہے اور شئی کا مثل اس کا غیر ہوتا ہے اگر چہ اس مثل کا انداز بھٹی کے ساتھ ہوتا ہے تو یہ صورت جائز ہے اور زقر نے فرمایا کہ اول میں بھی جائز ہے تو زقر نے فی الحال کا لحاظ کیا ہے اور فی الحال تمام مال موصی کا مال ہے اور اس کا جواب وہی ہے جو کہ ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں ۔ تشریح اگر موجی نے اس طرح وصیت کی کہ میرے بیٹے کا حصہ فلاں کیلئے وصیت ہے تو یہ وصیت جائز نہ ہوگی کیونکہ بیٹے کا حصہ بیٹے کی ملکیت ہوگا تو موصی کو یہ حق نہ ہوگا کہ وہ دوسرے کے مال کی وصیت کرے اور اگر موجی نے اس طرح وصیت کی کہ میرے بیٹے کا جتنا
Ruling on a person making a bequest from his own estate for someone of the share of his son. He said: And when he bequeaths the share of his son, the bequest is void. And if he bequeaths like the share of his son, it is permissible. Because the first is a bequest of another's property, because the share of the son is what he will receive after death. And the second is a bequest of something similar to the share of the son, and the like of a thing is other than it, even though it is estimated by it, so it is permissible. And Zufar said: It is permissible in the first as well, for he considered the present situation, and at present all the property is the testator's property. And its answer is what we have stated. Translation: Quduri said: And when the testator bequeaths the share of his son, the bequest is void. And if he bequeaths like the share of his son, it is permissible. Because the first is a bequest of another's property, because the son's share is what he will receive after death. And the second is a bequest of something similar to the son's share, and the like of a thing is other than it, even though it is estimated by it, so this case is permissible. And Zufar said: The first is also permissible, for he considered the present situation, and at present all the property is the testator's property. And its answer is what we have stated. Explanation: If the testator makes a bequest like this: 'My son's share is bequeathed to so-and-so,' this bequest will not be valid because the son's share will be the son's property, so the testator has no right to bequeath another's property. And if the testator makes a bequest like this: 'As much as my son's share...'
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage states a clear ruling from Al-Quduri's matn regarding bequests involving the son's share. The rule: If a testator says 'I bequeath my son's share to X,' the bequest is void. The reason is that the son's share is not yet owned by the testator at the time of death; it is a future entitlement of the son. Therefore, this constitutes a bequest of another's property (wasiyyah bi mal al-ghayr), which is invalid. However, if the testator says 'I bequeath the like of my son's share to X,' it is valid. The phrase 'like' refers to something similar, which is different from the son's actual share, and the testator can bequeath an equivalent amount from his own estate. Imam Zufar disagreed, arguing that at the moment of bequest, all property belongs to the testator, so bequeathing the son's share should be permissible. The commentator rejects this, stating that the son's share is future property that will belong to the son after death; the testator cannot bequeath it. The relied-upon position is the Hanafi view as stated by Imam Muhammad and Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms
نصیب (nasib): The share of inheritance that a son is entitled to receive from the testator's estate after death.
مثل (mithl): Something similar or equivalent in quantity or value, but not identical; a different entity.
وصیت بمال الغیر (wasiyyah bi mal al-ghayr): A bequest of property that belongs to someone else; such a bequest is invalid because the testator lacks ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A testator says: 'I bequeath my son's share to Zayd.' What is the ruling according to the Hanafi school?
A) Valid, because the testator owns all property at the time of bequest.
B) Valid, but limited to one-third of the estate.
C) Void, because it is a bequest of another's property.
D) Valid, with the son's consent.

Key Takeaway
Bequeathing the son's actual share is void as a bequest of another's property; bequeathing the like of it is valid as a bequest of one's own property.

Wasiyyah — Bequest

6 min
Bequest of a Son's Share vs. Like His Share
Ruling on bequest of son's share versus like with Zufar's dissent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling regarding bequest of a son's specific share versus its like and explain the legal basis for the distinction using the principle of bequest of another's property.

Core Idea
Bequeathing your son's specific share is void; bequeathing its like is valid.

In this lesson, we examine a critical distinction in Hanafi wasiyyah law. According to the matn of Al-Quduri, if a testator bequeaths the specific share of his son, the bequest is invalid because it effectively disposes of property that will belong to the son after death. However, if he bequeaths 'the like of my son's share,' it is valid because the 'like' is a legal measure, not another's property. The passage also presents the dissenting view of Imam Zufar, who considered current ownership, and the Hanafi response.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases
The testator either bequeaths 'my son's share' (specific) or 'the like of my son's share' (measured). Note the Arabic phrasing: نصيب الابن vs مثل نصيب الابن.
2
State the ruling for each
Specific share: batil (void). Like: sahih (valid). This is the mufta bihi position.
The ruling is from Al-Quduri, which is Zahir al-Riwayah.
3
Analyze the legal reasoning (illah)
The specific share is invalid because it is a bequest of property that will become the son's property after death. The like is valid because it is merely a quantification using another's property as a yardstick; the like is not the property itself.
The Hanafi maxim: 'The like of a thing is other than it' (مثل الشيء غيره).
4
Examine Zufar's dissent
Imam Zufar argues that at the time of bequest, all property belongs to the testator, so it is not a bequest of another's property. He focuses on the present state.
Zufar's view is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school but is marjuh.
5
Apply the Hanafi response
Although the property is currently owned by the testator, the son's right vests at the moment of death, making it in effect a bequest of another's property. Therefore, the bequest is void.
This is a case of considering future ownership (malikiyyah mustaqbaliyyah).

قال واذا اوصى بنصيب ابنه فَالوصية باطلة ولو أوصى بمثل نصيب ابنه جاز لأن الاول وصية بمال الغير لان نصيب الابن مايصيبه بعد الموت والثانى وصية بمثل نصيب الابن ومثل الشئ غيره وان كان يتقدر به فيجوز وقال زفر تجوز فى الأول ايضا فنظر الى الحال والكل ماله فيه وجوابه ما قلنا

Ruling on bequest from one's estate for a person from his son's share: He said: And when he bequeaths his son's share, the bequest is void; but if he bequeaths the like of his son's share, it is valid. Because the first is a bequest of another's property, for the son's share is what he receives after death. The second is a bequest of the like of his son's share, and the like of a thing is other than it, even though it is estimated by it; so it is valid. And Zufar said: It is valid in the first case as well; he considered the present state, and currently all the property is his. The answer is what we said. Commentary: Al-Quduri said... Explanation: If the testator says: 'My son's share is for so-and-so,' the bequest is invalid because the son's share will become the son's property, so the testator has no right to bequeath another's property. If he says: 'I bequeath for so-and-so the amount equal to my son's share,' it is valid because here the testator did not bequeath another's property, but rather measured the bequeathed property by another's property, and there is no harm in that, for the well-known principle is that the like of a thing is other than it. Thus it is clear that the testator did not bequeath another's right but measured the bequeathed property by the son's right and estimated the bequeathed object. Imam Zufar says that just as the second case is valid, so too the first case is valid. His view is that currently this property is not the son's property but still all is the testator's property, so it is not a bequest of another's property. But the answer is what we stated earlier, which is that although it is not currently the son's property, after the testator's death when the legatee becomes owner, at that time it will be the son's property. So where does the testator have the right to bequeath others' property? Therefore this bequest is void.
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from Al-Quduri's matn on bequests of a son's share versus the like of a son's share, along with an intra-Hanafi dispute with Imam Zufar. The passage type is a ruling with proof, as it gives rational reasoning. The author begins by stating the ruling: if a testator bequeaths the specific share of his son (i.e., 'my son's share is for so-and-so'), the bequest is invalid. The reason given is that the son's share is property that will belong to the son after the testator's death, so the testator is bequeathing another's property, which is not permissible. However, if the testator bequeaths 'the like of my son's share,' it is valid because the 'like' of a thing is considered something else, even if it is estimated by that thing. Imam Zufar disagreed and held that even the first case is valid because at the time of bequest, the property still belongs to the testator. The Hanafi response, as stated, is that although the property is currently owned by the testator, the son's right to that share will vest at the moment of death, making it a bequest of another's property in effect. The commentary then elaborates with an explanation in Urdu: the testator cannot bequeath what will become the son's property, but he can bequeath an amount equal to the son's share as a measure. The dispute highlights the Hanafi principle that future ownership is considered.

Key Terms
نصيب الابن (nasīb al-ibn): The share of the son from the testator's inheritance, which he would receive after the testator's death.
مثل (mithl): The 'like' of a thing, considered legally different from the thing itself, even if measured by it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The bequest is valid if the son agrees.

Key Takeaway
Bequeathing a specific share of an heir is invalid because it is a bequest of another's property; bequeathing its like is valid as a measurement.

Bequest of an Unspecified Share: Sahm Dispute Between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn
Ruling on bequest of an unspecified 'sahm' (share) with Imam Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the difference between Abu Hanifa's and the Sahibayn's rulings on bequest of an unspecified 'sahm' and apply the thamarah al-khilaf to a concrete scenario.

Core Idea
A bequest of 'a sahm' is valid, but the amount splits the school: smallest share vs. one heir's share, capped at one-third.

What happens when a testator says 'I give a sahm to Zaid' without saying how much? The bequest is valid, but its precise amount becomes a matter of juristic interpretation. In this lesson, we dissect the intra-Hanafi disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two foremost disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Understanding their different approaches to custom (urf) and minimal certainty will sharpen your ability to resolve ambiguous bequests.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa)
Identify the ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa from the passage: the legatee receives the smallest share among the heirs (akhass siham al-warathah), with a floor of one-sixth and a ceiling of one-third (since no bequest can exceed one-third without heirs' consent).
The smallest share might be 1/6, 1/8, etc., depending on the heir set.
2
State the Sahibayn position
Identify the ruling of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: the legatee receives the like of the share of any one heir (mithl nasib ahad al-warathah), but not exceeding one-third unless the heirs allow.
This gives the legatee a full heir's share, e.g., if there is one son, the legatee gets like the son's share (but capped at 1/3).
3
Analyse the proof (dalil) of each side
Abu Hanifa relies on the Kufan custom where 'sahm' often meant one-sixth, and the principle of giving the minimum certain. The Sahibayn rely on the general custom ('urf) that 'sahm' means one of the heirs' shares, and the least is certain only as a fallback.
The Sahibayn's argument prioritises the literal meaning over the local custom.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Consider a testator with one heir (a son) who bequeaths 'a sahm' to a stranger. Under Abu Hanifa, the legatee gets 1/6 (the smallest share, since 1/6 < son's share). Under the Sahibayn, the legatee gets 1/3 (like the son's share, but capped at 1/3).
The difference matters when the smallest share is less than the share of one heir.
5
Identify the tarjih (preferred view) in later fatwa
Though the passage does not give a tarjih, later Hanafi works (like Radd al-Muhtar) often prefer the Sahibayn's view as more aligned with the apparent meaning of 'sahm' and easier to apply.
In practice, many muftis adopt the Sahibayn position unless local custom dictates otherwise.

Source Text

لفظ ہم ( حصہ ) اور جز سے کسی کیلئے وصیت کرنے کا حکم، اقوال فقہاء ، صاحبین کی دلیل
قال ومن أوصى بسهم من ماله فله اخس سهام الورثة الا ان ينقص عن السدس فيتم له السدس ولا يزاد عليه وهذا عند ابي حنيفة وقالا له مثل نصيب احد الورثة ولا يزاد على الثلث الا ان تجيز الورثة لا ان السهم يراد به احدسهام الورثة عرفا لا سيما فى الوصية والاقل متيقن به فيصرف اليه الا اذا زاد على الثلث فير دعليه لانه لا مزيد عليه عدم اجازة الورثة -
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جس نے اپنے مال میں سے ایک سہم کی وصیت کی تو موصی لہ کیلئے ورثہ کے سہام میں سے اخس ( گھٹیا ) ہے مگر یہ کہ اخس سدس سے کم ہو جائے تو اس کیلئے سدس کو پورا کر دیا جائے گا اور سدس سے بڑھایا نہ جائے گا اور یہ ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ہے اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ موصی لہ کیلئے ورثاء میں سے ایک کے حصہ کے مثل ہوگا اور ثلث پر بڑھایا نہیں جائے گا مگر یہ کہ ورثا اجازت دے دیں۔ اسلئے کہ سہم سے عرف کے اندر ورثہ کے سہام میں سے ایک مراد لیا جاتا ہے۔ خصوصا وصیت میں اور اقل یقینی ہے تو اقل کی جانب پھیرا جائے گا۔ مگر جبکہ اقل ثلث سے بڑھ جائے تو زیادتی کو ورثا پر پھیر دیا جائے گا۔ اسلئے کہ ورثا کی اجازت نہ ہونے کے وقت ثلث پر زیادتی نہیں ہوتی ۔
تشریح اگر موصی نے وصیت ان الفاظ میں کی کہ میرے مال کا ایک سہم (حصہ) فلاں کے لئے ہے، یا میرے مال کا ایک جز فلاں کیلئے ہے تو سہم اور جز دونوں ہم معنی ہیں اور دونوں کے اندر جہالت وصیت کیلئے مضر نہیں تو وصیت تو جائز و درست ہوگئی مگر یہ ابہام اس میں رہ گیا کہ کس کو کتنا ملے گا تو یہ فیصلہ موصی کی وضاحت پر موقوف ہے اور اگر موصی وضاحت نہ کر سکا یہاں تک کہ موصی کا انتقال ہو گیا تو اب اس کے ورثا موصی کے قائم مقام ہو گئے لہذ اور نہ اس کی وضاحت کریں گے کہ سہم اور جز سے کیا مراد ہے۔ ورنہ جو بھی وضاحت کردیں خواہ وہ قلیل ہو یا کثیر اسی پر عمل کیا جائے گا یہ ہے اصل مسئلہ مگر اہل کوفہ کی اصلاح میں سہم بمعنی سدس مستعمل ہوتا تھا اس وجہ سے امام صاحب اور صاحبین کے نزدیک سہم بولنے کی صورت میں اختلاف ہو گیا جو کتاب میں مذکور ہے۔ یعنی صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر سہم بولا تو موصی کے ورثا کے سہام کو دیکھا جائیگا، ان میں سے جو سہم سب سے کم ہو اتنا ہی حصہ موصی لہ کو دیا جائے گا۔
Ruling on bequest using the word 'sahm' (share) and 'juz' (part), statements of jurists, proof of the two companions. He said: And whoever bequeaths a sahm from his wealth, then for the legatee is the lowest of the shares of the heirs, unless it is less than one-sixth, then one-sixth is completed for him, and it is not increased beyond that. This is according to Abu Hanifa. And they (the two companions) said: For him is the like of the share of one of the heirs, and it is not increased beyond one-third unless the heirs permit. Because 'sahm' customarily refers to one of the shares of the heirs, especially in bequests, and the least is certain, so it is directed to it. But if the least exceeds one-third, then the excess is returned to the heirs because there is no increase beyond one-third without the heirs' permission. Translation: Al-Quduri said... Commentary: If the testator bequeaths saying 'a sahm of my wealth is for so-and-so' or 'a juz of my wealth is for so-and-so', both words are synonymous, and ignorance of the amount does not harm the bequest, so the bequest is valid. But ambiguity remains as to how much he will receive. This is resolved by the testator's clarification. If he dies without clarifying, his heirs stand in his place and will clarify what is meant. The original ruling is that the smallest share of the heirs is given to the legatee, as per the custom of Kufa where sahm means one-sixth. Hence the difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions.
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage deals with the ruling when a testator bequeaths 'a sahm' (a share) from his wealth without specifying the exact amount. The passage type is an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani). The text first states the ruling from Al-Quduri: according to Abu Hanifa, the legatee receives the smallest share among the heirs (akhass siham al-warathah), which is understood as the minimum share any heir could get. If that minimum is less than one-sixth, it is raised to one-sixth, but not more. According to the Sahibayn, the legatee receives the like of the share of any one heir (mithl nasib ahad al-warathah), but no more than one-third without the heirs' consent. The reasoning for Abu Hanifa's view is based on the custom (urf) that 'sahm' typically refers to one of the heirs' shares, and the least is certain. For the Sahibayn, it is equal to one heir's share. The commentary explains that both 'sahm' and 'juz' are ambiguous but valid, and the resolution is through the testator's clarification or the heirs' interpretation. The difference arose because in Kufan usage, 'sahm' often meant one-sixth, hence Abu Hanifa's default to one-sixth. The practical application: if the testator says 'a sahm,' the legatee gets the smallest heir's share (Abu Hanifa) or one heir's share (Sahibayn), but capped at one-third without permission.

Key Terms
سهم (sahm): An undefined share or portion of the testator's wealth; ambiguous in amount.
اخس سهام الورثة (akhass siham al-warathah): The smallest (lowest) share among the heirs in the inheritance division.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) One-sixth of the estate
C) One-third of the estate
D) The share of one specific heir chosen by the testator

Key Takeaway
A bequest of an unspecified 'sahm' is valid; Hanafi imams differ on its amount, with Abu Hanifa favouring the smallest heir's share (minimum 1/6) and the Sahibayn favouring the share of one heir (capped at 1/3).

Wasiyyah — Bequest

The Meaning of 'Sahm' in Bequests: Imam Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the meaning of 'sahm' in bequests

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the meaning of 'sahm' in bequests, identify each side's evidence, and explain the later Hanafi tarjih based on custom.

Core Idea
'Sahm' in a bequest: one-sixth (Abu Hanifa), smallest heir share (Sahibayn), or ambiguous (later custom)?

When a testator uses the word 'sahm' in a bequest without specifying a number, what should the legatee receive? This ambiguity triggered a well-known intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn). The passage you will study lays out each side's evidence and ultimately shows that the ruling may change with custom.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested term and its legal significance
The word 'sahm' (share) appears in bequests without a fraction. Determine what 'sahm' means here because it directly affects the amount the legatee receives.
2
State the Sahibayn's position and their proof
The Sahibayn argue that 'sahm' refers to a share from among the heirs' shares. Since inheritance shares vary, the least certain (aqueel mutayaqqin) is the smallest share. Thus, the legatee gets the smallest heir share (capped at one-third without heirs' permission). Their proof is qiyas with inheritance.
Their analogy: bequest is a 'sister' of inheritance.
3
State Imam Abu Hanifa's position and his proof
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that 'sahm' means one-sixth (sudus). His evidence is textual: a marfu' hadith from Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) that 'sahm' is sudus, and the linguist Iyas ibn Mu'awiya stating that 'sahm' in Arabic means sudus.
Textual proof overrides qiyas in Hanafi usul.
4
Analyze the praktical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Abu Hanifa, the legatee gets a fixed 1/6 regardless of heirs. Under Sahibayn, the amount varies: if the smallest heir share is, say, 1/3, the legatee gets 1/3 (but capped at 1/3 even if smallest share is larger). The difference can be significant.
Example: if one daughter (share=1/2), Abu Hanifa gives 1/6; Sahibayn would give 1/2 but capped at 1/3 without permission.
5
Note the later Hanafi tarjih based on custom
The commentator (author of Ashraf al-Hidayah) states that the earlier positions were based on the custom of Kufa. In his own custom (and ours), 'sahm' is synonymous with 'juz'' (ambiguous part), so the heirs have the discretion to decide the amount. This is the mufta bihi.
Thus the ruling is not fixed but context-dependent.

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد - ۱۶ اس پر مصنف فرماتے ہیں کہ یہ ساری تفصیلات اہل کوفہ کے عرف کے مطابق ہیں ورنہ ہمارے عرف میں سہم جز کے معنی میں مستعمل ہے اور جز کے بارے میں جو حکم ہے وہ ہم شروع میں بیان کر چکے ہیں اور آگے بھی اس کو بیان کیا جارہا ہے۔
Book of Bequests. Page 126. Ashraf al-Bidaya Sharh Urdu Hidayah Volume 16. ... [full literal translation of the Arabic portion:] 'And the argument is that the sahm is the sudus, it is narrated from Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) and he raised it to the Prophet (peace be upon him) in what is narrated, and because it is mentioned and by it is intended sudus, for Iyas said: 'sahm' in language is an expression for sudus, and it is mentioned and by it is intended a share from the shares of the heirs, so he is given what we mentioned. They said: This was in their custom, but in our custom 'sahm' is like a part.'
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the meaning of 'sahm' when a testator bequeaths 'a sahm of my property'. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) argue that 'sahm' refers to the smallest share among the heirs, based on qiyas with inheritance where the term is used for shares. Imam Abu Hanifa, however, argues that 'sahm' means one-sixth (sudus), relying on a marfu' hadith from Ibn Mas'ud and the linguistic opinion of Iyas ibn Mu'awiya that 'sahm' in Arabic means sudus. The commentator (author of Ashraf al-Hidayah) notes that this interpretation was according to the custom of the people of Kufa; in the commentator's own custom, 'sahm' is synonymous with 'juz' (part), which is ambiguous and thus the heirs may decide the amount.

Key Terms
سهم (sahm): In this passage, the term is contested: Imam Abu Hanifa defines it as one-sixth (sudus); Sahibayn define it as a share from among the heirs' shares, specifically the smallest share.
سدس (sudus): One-sixth, a fixed Quranic share for certain heirs (e.g., one child of the deceased).
جزء (juz'): An ambiguous part; the text states that when a testator bequeaths a 'juz'', the heirs have the right to decide the amount because it is vague.
موصی لہ (musa lahu): The beneficiary of the bequest (legatee).
ورثہ (warathah): The heirs of the deceased who are entitled to the estate under inheritance law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It is given a fixed meaning of one-sixth.
B) It is interpreted as the smallest share among the heirs.
C) It is considered ambiguous, like 'juz', and the heirs decide the amount.
D) It is always interpreted as one-third.

Key Takeaway
The meaning of 'sahm' in a bequest is not fixed in the Hanafi school; the operative ruling depends on custom, with the later view treating it as ambiguous like 'juz'.

Bequest of Sudus Then Thulth: Inclusion and Linguistic Rule
Ruling on bequest inclusion and linguistic interpretation of definite noun repetition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of tadakhul (inclusion) when a testator bequeaths a larger share after a smaller one, and derive the outcome for repeated definite nouns using the linguistic principle al-ma'rifah idha u'idat tu'id bi 'aynihi.

Core Idea
A larger bequest includes a smaller one; a repeated definite noun refers back to the same entity.

In this lesson, we examine a key principle in Hanafi inheritance law: when a testator makes two bequests to the same person, the second may either supersede or confirm the first. The ruling hinges on whether the bequest is a different share (e.g., sudus then thulth) or the same share repeated. The Hanafi school applies a linguistic rule from Arabic grammar: a definite noun, when repeated, refers to the same entity, not a new one. This has direct consequences for the legatee's entitlement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the bequests and their order
Determine whether the testator gave a different share (sudus then thulth) or the same share (sudus twice).
The order matters: first bequest then second bequest.
2
Apply the rule of tadakhul (inclusion)
If the second bequest is a larger share and the heirs permit, the larger includes the smaller. The legatee only gets the larger share.
Tadakhul means the smaller is subsumed.
3
Apply the linguistic rule for repeated definite nouns
When the same definite noun (e.g., 'sudus') is repeated, the second refers to the same entity as the first, not an additional one. Thus, only one share is given.
The noun is definite due to idafah (construct state) to 'al-mal'.
4
Determine the final share
For sudus then thulth: thulth (one-third). For sudus twice: one sudus (one-sixth).
This assumes heirs permit the bequest (up to one-third).
5
Note the condition of heirs’ permission
Both scenarios presuppose that the heirs permit the bequest, as it is within the one-third limit.
If heirs do not permit, the bequest lapses.

موصی کہے کہ میر اسدس مال فلاں کیلئے وصیت پھر اسی مجلس یا دوسری مجلس میں کہا ثلث مال اس کیلئے ہے کا حکم
قال ومن قال سدس مالى لفلان ثم قال فى ذلك المجلس او فى مجلس اخر له ثلث مالى واجازت الورثة فله ثلث المال ويدخل السدس فيه ومن قال سدس مالى لفلان ثم قال فى ذلك المجلس اوفی غیره سدس مالی لفلان فله سدس واحد لان السدس ذكر معرفا بالاضافة الى المال والمعرفة اذا اعيدت يراد بالثاني عين الاول هو المعهود في اللغة
ترجمہ اور جس نے کہا کہ میر اسدس مال فلاں کیلئے ہے پھر اس مجلس میں یا دوسری مجلس میں کہا کہ فلاں کیلئے میر انلث مال ہے اور ورثا نے اجازت دیدی تو اس کیلئے ثلث مال ہے اور سندس اس ٹکٹ میں داخل ہو جائے گا اور جس نے کہا کہ میر اسدس مال فلاں کیلئے ہے پھر اسی مجلس میں یا اس کے غیر میں کہا کہ میرا اسدس فلاں کیلئے ہے تو اس کیلئے ایک سدس ہے اس لئے کہ ساس معرفہ ذکر کیا گیا ہے مال کی
جانب اضافت کرنے کی وجہ سے اور معرفہ کا جب اعادہ کیا جاتا ہے تو ثانی سے عین اول مراد لیا جاتا ہے، لغت میں یہی معہود ہے۔ تشریح موصی نے کہا کہ میر اسدس مال فلاں کیلئے وصیت ہے اور پھر اسی مجلس میں یا اس کے علاوہ دوسری مجلس میں کہتا ہے کہ اس کے لئے میراثلث مال وصیت ہے تو ان دونوں کا مجموعہ نصف ہوتا ہے اور در خا بھی اس کے نفاذ پر راضی ہیں اور نصف کے نفاذ کی اجازت دیتے ہیں، پھر بھی موصی لہ کو فقط ثلث ملے گا اور پہلا سدس بھی اسی میں مدغم ہو جائے گا اور اگر اس نے اولاً کہا کہ میر اسدس مال فلاں کیلئے وصیت ہے اور پھر اسی مجلس میں یا دوسری میں پھر کہتا ہے کہ میر اسدس مال فلاں کیلئے وصیت ہے تو قاعدہ میں اس کو ثلث ہو جانا چاہئے ، اس لئے کہ سد سان مل کر ٹکٹ بن جاتا ہے ، مگر اس کو صرف سدس ہی ملے گا۔ اس لئے کہ قاعدہ یہ مقرر ہے کہ جب معرفہ کے بعد پھر دوبارہ معرفہ آئے تو ثانی اور اول معرفہ دونوں سے مراد ایک ہوتا ہے اور یہاں سدس معرفہ ہے اس لئے کہ اس کی اضافت مال کی جانب ہے
The ruling when the testator says 'my sudus to so-and-so' then says in the same or another session 'he has my thulth' and the heirs permit: He receives the thulth and the sudus is included in it. And who says 'my sudus to so-and-so' then says in the same or another session 'my sudus to so-and-so': He receives one sudus, because sudus is mentioned as definite by addition to property, and when a definite is repeated, the second refers to the same as the first, according to established linguistic custom. Translation: ... He who first says 'my sudus is for so-and-so' then in the same assembly or another says 'my thulth is for so-and-so' and the heirs permit, he receives the thulth and the sudus is included in it. And he who first says 'my sudus is for so-and-so' then in the same assembly or another says 'my sudus is for so-and-so', he receives only one sudus, because 'sudus' is definite due to its idafah to property, and when a definite is repeated, the second refers to the same entity as the first; this is the established rule in language.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage from Al-Hidayah (via Al-Quduri) explains two scenarios: First, if a testator bequeaths 'sudus' (one-sixth) to someone, then later bequeaths 'thulth' (one-third) to the same person, and the heirs permit the bequest, the legatee receives only the thulth, and the earlier sudus is merged into it. The total would be half if combined, but since the second bequest overrides the first as a larger share, only the thulth is given. Second, if the testator bequeaths 'sudus' twice to the same person (whether in the same session or different), the legatee receives only one sudus, not a third (which would be two-sixths). This is because 'sudus' is a definite noun (ma'rifah) due to its idafah to 'al-mal', and when a definite is repeated, the second refers to the same entity as the first, not an additional one. Thus the two statements are considered a confirmation, not a new bequest.

Key Terms
معرفہ (ma'rifah): A definite noun; here, 'al-sudsu' is definite due to its idafah to 'al-mal' (my property).
اعادہ (i'adah): Repetition of a definite noun; in Arabic, repeating a definite noun refers back to the same entity.
تداخل (tadakhul): Inclusion or merging; when the testator says 'thulth' after 'sudus', the sudus is included in the thulth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a testator says 'my sudus for Zaid' twice, how much does Zaid receive?
A) One-third
B) One-sixth
C) One-fourth
D) Two-sixths

Key Takeaway
When a testator bequeaths a larger share after a smaller one to the same person, the larger includes the smaller; repeating the same share yields no increase due to the linguistic rule for definite nouns.

Bequest of an Unspecified Part (Juz') and Heirs' Discretion
States ruling that heirs determine quantity of ambiguous bequest

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a bequest of an unspecified part (juz') and explain why the heirs have the right to determine the amount.

Core Idea
An ambiguous bequest is valid; the heirs, as the testator's successors, decide the quantity.

When a testator uses the vague term 'juz' (a part) in their will, the Hanafi school provides a practical solution: the ambiguity does not invalidate the will, and the heirs, stepping into the testator's role, have the authority to specify the amount. This reflects the school's emphasis on fulfilling the testator's intention while avoiding invalidation due to vagueness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? A bequest of an unspecified part (juz' min malihi). Determine the hukm: the bequest is valid (sahih) and the heirs decide the amount.
The term 'juz' is ambiguous, but validity is preserved.
2
Understand why ambiguity does not invalidate
Why does uncertainty not nullify the will? Because the testator's intent to give is clear, and ignorance (jahalah) does not inherently invalidate a bequest in Hanafi law.
Contrast with sales, where uncertainty can invalidate.
3
Analyze the heirs' authority
Why do the heirs have the right to specify? They stand in the place of the testator (qa'imun maqam al-musi) after his death, so they complete what he left open.
This is a unique Hanafi extension of the concept of succession.
4
Note the custom variation
The passage notes that the term 'sahm' (share) is commonly used instead of 'juz', but both carry the same ruling. The earlier details were based on Kufan custom.
Flexibility based on local custom ('urf) is evident.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, if a will says 'I give a part of my estate to my nephew,' the heirs can give any amount they choose, even a minimal sum, acting in good faith.
The legatee cannot demand more than what the heirs decide.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اس پر مصنف فرماتے ہیں کہ یہ ساری تفصیلات اہل کوفہ کے عرف کے مطابق ہیں ورنہ ہمارے عرف میں سہم جز کے معنی میں مستعمل ہے اور جز کے بارے میں جو حکم ہے وہ ہم شروع میں بیان کر چکے ہیں اور آگے بھی اس کو بیان کیا جارہا ہے۔ جزء مجہول کی وصیت کرنے کی صورت میں تفصیل کرنے کا حق ورثا کو ہوگا

قال ولواوصى بجزء من ماله قيل للورثة اعطوه ما شئتم لانه مجهول يتناول القليل والكثير غيران الجهالة صحة الوصية والورثة قائمون مقام الموصى فاليهم البيان

ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور اگر اپنے مال میں سے ایک جز کی وصیت کی تو ورثا سے کہا جائے گا کہ موصی لہ کو جو تم چاہوں دو اس لئے کہ جز مجہول ہے جو قلیل و کثیر کو شامل ہے علاوہ اس بات کے کہ جہالت وصیت کی صحت کو مانع نہیں ہے اور ورثا موصی کے قائم مقام ہیں تو بیان ورثا کی جانب ہے۔ تشریح اس کی تشریح ہم پہلے ہی بیان کر چکے ہیں اور یہ بھی بتا چکے ہیں کہ ہم اور جز دونوں کا حکم ایک ہے۔
The author says: All these details are according to the custom of the people of Kufa; otherwise in our custom, 'sahm' is used in the meaning of 'juz', and the ruling about 'juz' we have already mentioned at the beginning and will mention later. In the case of bequest of an unknown part (juz), the heirs have the right to specify. He said: And if one makes a bequest of a part of his wealth, the heirs are told: give him whatever you wish, because it is unknown encompassing little and much, except that ignorance does not prevent the validity of the will, and the heirs stand in place of the testator, so clarification is up to them. Translation: Quduri said: And if one makes a bequest of a part of his wealth, the heirs will be told: give the legatee whatever you wish, because 'juz' is unknown, including little and much, and moreover ignorance does not prevent the validity of the will, and the heirs are the successors of the testator, so the statement is up to the heirs. Commentary: We have already explained its commentary and also stated that the ruling for 'sahm' and 'juz' is the same.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah explains the ruling on a bequest of an ambiguous 'juz' (part). The author first notes that the detailed rules given earlier are based on the custom of the people of Kufa, whereas in the common custom 'sahm' is used instead of 'juz', but the ruling is the same. The core ruling from Quduri states that if a testator bequeaths a 'juz' of his wealth, the heirs have the authority to determine how much to give. This is because 'juz' is ambiguous (mujmal) and can mean a little or a lot. Nevertheless, such ambiguity does not invalidate the will. Since the heirs stand in the place of the testator after his death, they have the right to specify the amount. This is a clear Hanafi position that gives flexibility when the testator uses vague terms.

Key Terms
جزء (juz'): An unspecified part or portion of something; in this context, a part of the testator's estate.
موصی (musi): The testator who makes a bequest (wasiyyah).
ورثہ (warathah): The heirs who inherit the estate and, in this case, have the authority to determine the quantity of the ambiguous bequest.
مجہول (majhul): Unknown or ambiguous; here, refers to the term 'juz' which does not specify a fixed quantity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a testator bequeaths 'a part' (juz) of his wealth, what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) The bequest is invalid because the term is ambiguous.
B) The heirs must give exactly one-third of the estate.
C) The heirs may give whatever amount they wish, because the testator's ambiguity does not invalidate the will and they stand in his place.
D) The bequest is interpreted as one share equal to that of an heir.

Key Takeaway
A bequest of an unspecified part is valid in Hanafi law, and the heirs, as the testator's successors, have the right to decide the amount.

Rulings on Repeated and Successive Fractional Bequests
Dictates that a later bequest of a third includes an earlier sixth; repeated sixth refers to the same.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi linguistic rule of definite noun repetition to determine the legatee's share when bequests of fractions are repeated or followed by a larger fraction.

Core Idea
A later bequest of a third absorbs an earlier sixth; a repeated sixth grants only one sixth due to linguistic definiteness.

This lesson examines two common scenarios in Islamic estate planning where a testator makes multiple bequests of fractions to the same person. The Hanafi school employs a rigorous linguistic principle to resolve these cases: when a definite noun is repeated, it refers to the same entity, not a second one. We will see how this principle determines whether the legatee receives a third, a sixth, or something else.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The text presents two cases: (a) a bequest of a sixth followed by a third, and (b) a bequest of a sixth followed by another sixth. Note that the testator may be in the same session or a different one.
These are distinct situations with different rulings.
2
Analyze the first scenario: sixth then third with heirs' permission
The legatee receives only the third. The later bequest of a third is considered to absorb the earlier sixth. The heirs' permission is required for the bequest to be effective, but here they permit.
The total would be half, but the ruling gives only a third.
3
Analyze the second scenario: sixth then another sixth
The legatee receives only one sixth, not two. This is because the second 'sixth' is a definite noun referring to the same sixth as the first.
Mathematically two sixths make a third, but the linguistic rule overrides.
4
Understand the linguistic proof
The proof is based on the nature of 'my sixth' as a definite noun (ma'rifah) due to idafa. In Arabic, when a definite noun is repeated, it refers to the same entity (al-ma'rifah idha u'idat fa-hiya li-ayn al-awwal). This is a well-established principle in the language.
This is a rational proof (dalil aqli) from linguistic usage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
موصی کہے کہ میر اسدس مال فلاں کیلئے وصیت پھر اسی مجلس یا دوسری مجلس میں کہا ثلث مال اس کیلئے ہے کا حکم

قال ومن قال سدس مالى لفلان ثم قال فى ذلك المجلس او فى مجلس اخر له ثلث مالى واجازت الورثة فله ثلث المال ويدخل السدس فيه ومن قال سدس مالى لفلان ثم قال فى ذلك المجلس اوفی غیره سدس مالی لفلان فله سدس واحد لان السدس ذكر معرفا بالاضافة الى المال والمعرفة اذا اعيدت يراد بالثاني عين الاول هو المعهود في اللغة

ترجمہ اور جس نے کہا کہ میر اسدس مال فلاں کیلئے ہے پھر اس مجلس میں یا دوسری مجلس میں کہا کہ فلاں کیلئے میر انلث مال ہے اور ورثا نے اجازت دیدی تو اس کیلئے ثلث مال ہے اور سندس اس ٹکٹ میں داخل ہو جائے گا اور جس نے کہا کہ میر اسدس مال فلاں کیلئے ہے پھر اسی مجلس میں یا اس کے غیر میں کہا کہ میرا اسدس فلاں کیلئے ہے تو اس کیلئے ایک سدس ہے اس لئے کہ ساس معرفہ ذکر کیا گیا ہے مال کی جانب اضافت کرنے کی وجہ سے اور معرفہ کا جب اعادہ کیا جاتا ہے تو ثانی سے عین اول مراد لیا جاتا ہے، لغت میں یہی معہود ہے۔ تشریح موصی نے کہا کہ میر اسدس مال فلاں کیلئے وصیت ہے اور پھر اسی مجلس میں یا اس کے علاوہ دوسری مجلس میں کہتا ہے کہ اس کے لئے میراثلث مال وصیت ہے تو ان دونوں کا مجموعہ نصف ہوتا ہے اور ورثا بھی اس کے نفاذ پر راضی ہیں اور نصف کے نفاذ کی اجازت دیتے ہیں، پھر بھی موصی لہ کو فقط ثلث ملے گا اور پہلا سدس بھی اسی میں مدغم ہو جائے گا اور اگر اس نے اولاً کہا کہ میر اسدس مال فلاں کیلئے وصیت ہے اور پھر اسی مجلس میں یا دوسری میں پھر کہتا ہے کہ میر اسدس مال فلاں کیلئے وصیت ہے تو قاعدہ میں اس کو ثلث ہو جانا چاہئے ، اس لئے کہ سد سان مل کر ٹکٹ بن جاتا ہے ، مگر اس کو صرف سدس ہی ملے گا۔ اس لئے کہ قاعدہ یہ مقرر ہے کہ جب معرفہ کے بعد پھر دوبارہ معرفہ آئے تو ثانی اور اول معرفہ دونوں سے مراد ایک ہوتا ہے اور یہاں سدس معرفہ ہے اس لئے کہ اس کی اضافت مال کی جانب ہے اور وہ یا متکلم کی جانب مضاف ہونے کی وجہ سے معرفہ ہے جس کی وجہ سے سدس بھی معرفہ ہو گیا تو معرفہ کے بعد دوسرا معرفہ بیان کیا گیا ہے تو ثانی سدس سے بھی اول مراد ہوگا اور صرف موصی لہ کو ایک سدس دیا جائے گا۔
The ruling if the testator says: 'My sixth of my wealth is for so-and-so,' then in the same gathering or another gathering says: 'His third of my wealth is for him,' and the heirs permit: He gets the third of the wealth, and the sixth is included in it. And whoever said: 'My sixth of my wealth is for so-and-so,' then in that same gathering or in another said: 'My sixth of my wealth is for so-and-so,' he gets one sixth, because the sixth was mentioned as definite by addition to the wealth, and when a definite noun is repeated, by the second the exact first is intended, which is established in the language. Translation: And whoever said: 'My sixth of my wealth is for so-and-so,' then in that gathering or another said: 'So-and-so has my third of my wealth,' and the heirs permitted, then he gets the third of the wealth, and the sixth enters into that third. And whoever said: 'My sixth of my wealth is for so-and-so,' then in that same gathering or in another said: 'My sixth is for so-and-so,' then he gets one sixth, because the sixth is mentioned as definite by addition to the wealth, and when a definite noun is repeated, by the second the exact first is intended, as is established in the language. Commentary: The testator said: 'My sixth of my wealth is bequeathed to so-and-so,' and then in the same gathering or another, says: 'My third of my wealth is bequeathed to him.' The total of both is half, and the heirs are satisfied with its execution and permit half. Nevertheless, the legatee gets only a third, and the first sixth is merged into that third. And if he initially said: 'My sixth of my wealth is for so-and-so,' and then in the same gathering or another says again: 'My sixth of my wealth is for so-and-so,' then by rule it should become a third, because two sixths together make a third. But he gets only one sixth. Because the rule is established: when a definite noun is followed by another definite noun, the second refers to the same as the first. Here, the sixth is definite because it is added to the wealth, and thus it becomes definite. So when the second definite noun is mentioned, it also refers to the first, so only one sixth is given to the legatee.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah discusses two scenarios of bequests involving fractions. First, if a testator bequeaths a sixth to someone, then later in the same session or another, bequeaths a third to the same person, and the heirs permit, the legatee receives only the third, and the sixth is absorbed into it. Even though the sum is half, the later bequest (third) is considered inclusive of the earlier one. This is because the testator's intention is likely to increase the bequest, and the heirs' permission makes it effective. Second, if the testator bequeaths a sixth, then again bequeaths a sixth, the legatee gets only one sixth, not two. The reasoning is linguistic: 'my sixth' is a definite noun (ma'rifah) due to the idafa (construct phrase) to the testator. When a definite noun is repeated, the second instance refers to the same entity as the first, not a different one. Therefore, the repetition does not create a second share; it merely confirms the first. The text also notes that if one calculated mathematically, two sixths make a third, but the legal ruling overrides that because of the linguistic principle.

Key Terms
سدس (sudus): One-sixth of the estate.
ثلث (thuluth): One-third of the estate.
معرفہ (ma'rifah): A definite noun; here, 'sudus' is made definite by idafa (addition) to the testator's wealth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a testator says 'my sixth is for Zaid' and later in the same session says again 'my sixth is for Zaid', how much does Zaid receive?
A) One-sixth
B) One-third
C) One-half
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a repeated definite bequest of the same fraction does not create multiple shares; the second refers to the first.

Bequest of a Third of Specific Property When Two-Thirds Perish
Presents Hanafi and Imam Zufar's dispute on legatee's share when two-thirds of specific bequest are lost

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the legatee's share when two-thirds of a specific bequeathed asset perish, and explain why Imam Zufar's opposing view is not followed.

Core Idea
A bequest of a specific third entitles the legatee to the surviving third in full, not a proportion.

This lesson examines a nuanced dispute within the Hanafi school regarding bequests of a specific fraction of a particular asset. When two-thirds of that asset are lost before distribution, does the legatee receive the entire remaining third, or only a part of it? We will study the Hanafi position, Imam Zufar's dissenting view, and the legal reasoning behind each.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The legatee gets the entire remaining third of the specific asset (e.g., 300 out of 900 dirhams).
This is the relied-upon view.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam Zufar holds that the legatee gets one-third of the remaining third (e.g., 100 out of 900).
Zufar's view is recorded but not followed.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Zufar argues from the principle of shared property (shirkah): loss and gain are proportionate for co-owners.
He uses qiyas to a multi-type estate bequest.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school distinguishes: the bequest is of a third of that specific property, not a share of the entire estate; the loss is external, and the bequest attaches to what remains.
The analogy does not hold.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: in the example, the legatee gets 300 dirhams (Hanafi) vs. 100 dirhams (Zufar).
This highlights the real-world impact of the dispute.

دراہم سے ایک تہائی یا بکریوں سے ایک تہائی کی وصیت کی اور اتفاقاً دو تہائی ضائع ہو جائے تو وصیت کا حکم ، اقوال فقہاء ، مذہب احناف، امام زفر کی دلیل

قال و من اوصى بثلث دراهمه او بثلث غنمه فهلک ثلثا ذلك وبقى ثلثه وهو يخرج من ثلث ما بقى من ماله فله ما بقى وقال زفر له ثلث ما بقى لان كل واحد منهما مشترك بينهم والمال المشترك يتوى ماتوى منه الشركة ويبقى مـــابـقـى عليها وصار كما اذا كانت التركة اجناسا مختلفة

ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جس نے وصیت کی اپنے دراہم میں سے ثلث کی یا اپنی بکریوں میں سے ثلث کی پس اس کے دو تہائی ہلاک ہو گئے اور اس کا ایک تہائی باقی رہ گیا اور ( جو تہائی باقی رہ گیا ہے ) اس کے ما بقی مال کے تہائی سے نکل جاتا ہے تو اس کے لئے تمام باقی ہے اور زفر نے فرمایا ہے کہ اس کیلئے ما بقی کا تہائی ہے اس لئے کہ ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک ان سب کے درمیان مشترک ہے اور مال مشترک ہلاک ہوتا ہے اس میں سے جو ہلاک ہوتا ہے شرکت پر اور باقی رہتا ہے جو باقی رہتا ہے شرکت پر اور ایسا ہو گیا جیسے جب کہ ترکہ مختلف اجناس ہوں۔

تشریح زید کے پاس کچھ درہم یا کچھ بکریاں اور اس کے پاس دراہم اور بکریوں کے علاوہ اور بھی مال ہے جو بکریوں یا دراہم کے مثلث سے دوگنا ہے۔ جب زید وصیت کرتا ہے کہ میرے دراہم کا ایک تہائی فلاں کیلئے وصیت ہے یا کہتا ہے کہ میری بکریوں کا ایک ثلث وصیت ہے تو وصیت صحیح ہے، مگر اب یہ واقعہ پیش آیا کہ دراہم اور بکریوں میں سے دو تہائی ہلاک ہو گیا اور صرف ایک تہائی باقی رہ گیا ہے اس تہائی کے علاوہ موصی کے پاس اتنا مال موجود ہے کہ وہ اس کے مقابلہ میں ثلثان یا اس سے زیادہ ہے، تو اب موصی لہ کو کتنا دیا جائے گا؟ تو اس میں ہمارا اور امام زفر کا اختلاف ہے۔ ہمارا مذہب یہ ہے دراہم میں سے اور بکریوں میں سے جو تہائی باقی ہے وہ پورا تہائی موصی لہ کو دیا جائے گا، اور امام زفر فرماتے ہیں کہ جو تہائی باقی ہے اس کا تہائی موصی لہ کو ملے گا۔ مثلا کل ۹۰۰ دراہم تھے، ان میں تہائی یعنی ۳۰۰، باقی رہے اور ۶۰۰ ہلاک ہو گئے تو امام زفر کے نزدیک ما بقی ۳۰۰ کا تہائی یعنی ۱۰۰ موصی لہ کو دیا جائے گا اور ہمارے نزدیک ۳۰۰ ما بقی موصی لہ کو دیئے جائیں گے۔ امام زفر کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ سارا مال یعنی دراہم اور بکریاں موصی لہ اور ورثہ کے درمیان مشترک ہیں تو جو مقدار ہلاک ہو گئی وہ بھی مشترک ہے اور جو باقی ہے وہ بھی مشترک اور اصول یہ ہے کہ جو مال مشترک ہوتا ہے اس کی ہلاکت بھی شرکت پر ہوتی ہے اور جو باقی بچتا ہے اس کی بقاء بھی شرکت پر باقی رہتی ہے۔ لہذا صورت مذکورہ میں جب یہ مال مشترک ہوا تو ہلاک اور باقی دونوں مشترک ہو گا اور اگر ترکہ اجناس مختلفہ ہوں اور وہاں موصی یہ طریقہ اختیار کرنا تو وہاں سب کے نزدیک یہی حکم ہے کہ ما بقی کا تہائی موصی لہ کو دیا جائے گا۔
The ruling on a bequest of a third of dirhams or a third of goats, and by chance two-thirds are lost: statements of jurists, Hanafi school, Imam Zufar's proof. He said: Whoever bequeaths a third of his dirhams or a third of his goats, then two-thirds of that perish and one-third remains, and that third comes out of the third of what remains of his wealth, so he gets what remains. Zufar said: He gets a third of what remains, because each of them is shared among them, and shared property perishes insofar as the partnership perishes, and remains insofar as it remains for the partnership. It becomes like when the estate consists of different genres. Translation: Quduri said: And whoever bequeathed a third of his dirhams or a third of his goats, then two-thirds of that perished and one-third remained, and that third comes out of a third of what remains of his wealth, so he gets all that remains. Zufar said: He gets a third of what remains, because each of them is shared among them, and shared property perishes as the partnership perishes, and remains as it remains for the partnership. It becomes like when the estate consists of different genres. Commentary: Zayd has some dirhams or some goats, and besides the dirhams and goats, he has other property that is twice the value of the like of the goats or dirhams. When Zayd bequeaths a third of his dirhams to so-and-so, or says a third of his goats is bequeathed, the bequest is valid. But it so happens that two-thirds of the dirhams and goats are lost, leaving only one-third. Besides this third, the testator has sufficient property that is two-thirds of that or more. How much will the legatee be given? There is a difference between us and Imam Zufar. Our school is that the remaining third of the dirhams and goats is given entirely to the legatee. Imam Zufar says: the legatee gets one-third of that remaining third. For example, total dirhams were 900, one-third (300) remains, 600 perished. According to Zufar, one-third of the remaining 300 (i.e., 100) is given to the legatee. According to us, the remaining 300 are given to the legatee. Zufar's proof: all the property (dirhams and goats) is shared between the legatee and the heirs. So the amount that perished is also shared, and what remains is also shared. The principle is that shared property perishes proportionally to the partnership, and remains proportionally. So in this case, since the property was shared, both the loss and the remainder are shared. If the estate consisted of different genres and the testator had taken this method, then all agree that the legatee gets one-third of what remains.
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah presents a dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam Zufar regarding a bequest of a specific third of a particular asset (like dirhams or goats) when two-thirds of that asset are lost. The testator has other property beyond that asset. The question is: does the legatee get the entire remaining third of that asset, or only a proportion? The Hanafi position (Imam Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) holds that the legatee receives the whole remaining third (e.g., if 900 dirhams were the asset and 600 are lost, the legatee gets the remaining 300). Imam Zufar argues that the legatee only gets one-third of the remaining third (i.e., 100), because the entire asset was shared between the legatee and the heirs from the moment of the testator's death. In a partnership, loss and gain are shared proportionally. Zufar uses analogy to a case where the estate has multiple types of property and a bequest is made of a third of each type; there, all agree that the legatee gets a third of what remains of each type. The Hanafi school, however, distinguishes: since the bequest was specifically of a third of that particular asset, the legatee is entitled to the surviving portion of that asset, up to the overall limit of one-third of the total estate (since the testator has other property, the remaining third does not exceed the one-third limit). The Hanafi view is that the loss is considered to have happened before the bequest takes effect, so the legatee's share is determined from what actually exists at the time of distribution.

Key Terms
ثلث (thuluth): One-third of the estate or of a specific asset.
مشترک (mushtarak): Shared; in this context, property that is owned jointly by the legatee and the heirs.
شرکت (shirkah): Partnership; the legal relationship between co-owners of property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a testator bequeaths one-third of his 900 dirhams, but 600 dirhams are lost before distribution, and he has sufficient other property, how much does the legatee receive?
A) 100 dirhams
B) 200 dirhams
C) 300 dirhams
D) 600 dirhams

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a bequest of a specific fraction of a particular asset entitles the legatee to the surviving portion of that asset in full, up to the one-third of the total estate limit.
