Wasiyyah — Bequest
intermediate
8 min
Bequest of a Fractional Share After Partial Destruction: The Single Genus Rule
Intra-Hanafi dispute on legatee's share after partial destruction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi majority position on a legatee's share when bequeathed property of a single genus is partially destroyed, and distinguish it from Imam Zufar's view, applying the distinction between jins wahid and ajnas mukhtalifa.

Core Idea
In a single genus, the legatee gets the entire remaining fractional share because the bequest takes precedence over inheritance and destruction falls on the subordinate.

When a testator bequeaths a fractional share of a specific type of property (e.g., one-third of his dirhams), and part of that property is destroyed before the bequest is executed, a critical question arises: how much does the legatee receive? The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement on this point. In this lesson, we examine the dispute between the majority (Abu Hanifa and the two companions) and Imam Zufar, and uncover the key distinction between single-genus and multi-genus property that determines the outcome.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi majority position
Identify the ruling from Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad: when two-thirds of a single-genus bequeathed item are destroyed, the legatee receives the entire remaining one-third.
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Identify Imam Zufar's opposing view
State Zufar's view: the legatee receives only one-third of the remaining one-third (proportional share).
Zufar argues based on common property principles.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Explain Zufar's dalil: the bequeathed property is common between legatee and heirs, so destruction and remaining are shared proportionally. He analogizes to multiple types where all agree the legatee gets a proportional share.
His proof relies on the nature of common ownership.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The majority rebuts by distinguishing single genus from multiple types. In a single genus, the judge can coerce division (jabr), and the bequest takes precedence over inheritance, making the legatee's right original (asl) and the heirs' right subordinate (taba'). Destruction is attributed to the subordinate.
The key distinction is the possibility of combining rights in a single item.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
State the practical difference: for a single genus, the legatee gets the full remaining share; for multiple types, he gets only a proportional share of each type.
This difference stems from the rules of division (qisma) and the precedence of bequest.

جنس کے مابھی ثلث کا ثلث دیا جائے گالہذا یہاں بھی ایسا ہی ہونا چاہئے ۔
امام زفر کی دلیل کا جواب
ولنا ان فى الجنس الواحد يمكن جمع حق احدهم فى الواحد ولهذا يجرى فيه الجبر على القسمة وفيه جمع والوصية مقدمة فجمعناها فى الواحد الباقى وصارت الدراهم كالدرهم بخلاف الاجناس المختلفة لانه لا يمكن الجمع فيها جبرا فكذا تقديما
ترجمہ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ جنس واحد میں ان میں سے ہر ایک کے حق کو ایک میں جمع کرناممکن ہے اس لئے جنس واحد میں تقسیم پر جبر جاری ہوتا ہے اور تقسیم میں جمع کرنا ہے اور وصیت مقدم ہے تو ہم نے اس کو ایک باقی میں جمع کر دیا اور دور اہم درہم کے مثل ہو گیا بخلاف اجناس مختلفہ کے اس لئے کہ اجناس مختلفہ میں تقسیم پر جبر کے اعتبار سے جمع کرنا ممکن نہیں ہے پس ایسے ہی باعتبار تقدیم کے۔ تشریح یہ ہماری طرف سے امام زفر کی دلیل کا جواب ہے ۔ جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ جنس واحد کو اجناس مختلفہ پر قیاس کرنا قیاس مع الفارق ہے اس لئے کہ کتاب القسمہ میں یہ بحث گزر چکی ہے۔ جنس واحد میں قسمت کی درخواست پر قاضی باقی شرکاء پر جبر کرے گا اور اجناس مختلفہ کی صورت میں قاضی جبر نہیں کرے گا اور اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ جنس واحد میں ایک چیز کے چند شر کا ء کو جمع کیا جا سکتا ہے یعنی اس کے اندر موصی لہ کا بھی حق ہو اور ورثا کا بھی حق ہو لہذا جب اجتماع ہو گیا یعنی جنس واحد کی صورت میں ۹۰۰ ر درا ہم میں تو موصی لہ کا حق مقدم ہوگا اسلئے کہ وصیت میراث سے مقدم ہوتی ہے تو اس میں موصی لہا کا حق اصالہ ہے اور دور خا کا حق سبعا ہے اور پھر اصول کلی یہ ہے کہ جب کوئی مال اصل اور تابع پر مشتمل ہو اور اس میں سے کچھ ہلاک ہو جائے تو ہلاکت کو تابع کی جانب پھیرا جاتا ہے اصل کی طرف نہیں جیسے مال مضاربت میں ایسا ہی ہوتا ہے لہذا یہاں ہلاکت کو اس ثلثان کی طرف پھیرا جائے گا جو دور تا کا حق تھا اور اصل ثلث باقی ہے لہذا وہ موصی لیہ کو دیا جائے گا۔ اور اگر اجناس مختلفہ ہوں تو وہاں نہ جبر ہو سکتا ہے اور نہ سب کو اکی واحد میں جمع کیا جا سکتا ہے اور جب یہ ساری چیزیں نہ ہوں گی تو وصیت کی میراث پر تقدیم بھی ثابت نہ ہو سکے گی اور نہ اصل اور تبع والا مسئلہ جاری ہو سکے گا یہ دلیل کا ماحصل ہو گیا۔
He said: Whoever bequeaths one-third of his dirhams or one-third of his goats, then two-thirds of that are destroyed and one-third remains, and it is taken from one-third of what remains of his wealth, so he (the legatee) gets what remains. Zufar said: He gets one-third of what remains, because each of them is common between them, and common property is lost as the partnership is lost, and remains as the partnership remains, and it becomes like when the estate consists of various types. Translation: Quduri said: And whoever bequeaths one-third of his dirhams or one-third of his goats, then two-thirds of that are destroyed and one-third remains, and it is taken from one-third of what remains of his wealth, so he gets all that remains. Zufar said: He gets one-third of what remains, because each of them is common between them, and common property is lost as the partnership is lost, and remains as the partnership remains, and it becomes like when the estate consists of various types. Explanation: Zayd has some dirhams or some goats, and besides the dirhams and goats he has other wealth which is double the value of the goats or dirhams. When Zayd bequeaths that one-third of his dirhams is for so-and-so, or says one-third of his goats is bequeathed, the bequest is valid. But now this incident occurs: two-thirds of the dirhams and goats are destroyed and only one-third remains. Besides this one-third, the testator has so much wealth that it is two-thirds or more in comparison. So how much will the legatee be given? There is a difference between us and Imam Zufar. Our madhhab is that the one-third that remains of the dirhams and goats will be given entirely to the legatee. Imam Zufar says that of what remains, only one-third goes to the legatee. For example, total dirhams were 900, one-third i.e. 300 remained, and 600 were destroyed. According to Imam Zufar, of the remaining 300, one-third i.e. 100 will be given to the legatee; according to us, the remaining 300 will be given to the legatee. Imam Zufar's proof is that the entire wealth, i.e. the dirhams and goats, is common between the legatee and the heirs. So the amount that was lost is also common, and what remains is also common. The principle is that when property is common, its destruction is also in proportion to the partnership, and what remains also remains in proportion to the partnership. Therefore in this case, when the wealth is common, both the lost and the remaining are common. And if the estate consists of various types, and the testator adopts this method, then all agree that one-third of what remains will be given to the legatee. For example, Zayd has a flock of goats, some camels, and some cows, and he bequeaths one-third of each, and by chance two-thirds of each are destroyed and only one-third remains. Then by consensus, for each type the legatee gets one-third of what remains of each type. So here also it should be the same.
Response to Imam Zufar's proof: And we have that in a single genus, it is possible to combine the right of one of them in the single item, and therefore coercion upon division is applied to it, and in it there is combination, and the bequest is given precedence, so we combined it in the single remaining item, and the dirhams became like a single dirham, unlike the various types, because in various types combination is not possible through coercion, so likewise in terms of precedence. Translation: And our proof is that in a single genus, it is possible to combine the right of each of them in one item. Therefore in a single genus, coercion upon division is applied, and in division there is combination, and the bequest is given precedence, so we combined it in the single remaining item, and the dirhams became like a dirham, unlike various types, because in various types it is not possible to combine through coercion, so similarly in terms of precedence. Explanation: This is our response to Imam Zufar's proof. Its summary is that comparing a single genus to various types is an analogy with a difference (qiyas ma'a al-fariq), because in the Book of Division this discussion has passed. In a single genus, upon request for division, the judge will coerce the remaining partners, but in the case of various types, the judge will not coerce. The reason is that in a single genus, several partners can be combined in one thing, i.e., it includes the right of the legatee and the right of the heirs. Therefore when combination occurs, i.e., in the case of a single genus like 900 dirhams, the right of the legatee is given precedence because the bequest takes precedence over inheritance. So in that, the legatee's right is the original (asl) and the heirs' right is the subordinate (taba'). Then the general principle is that when property consists of an original and a subordinate, and some of it is destroyed, the destruction is attributed to the subordinate, not the original, as in mudaraba property. Therefore here the destruction will be attributed to the two-thirds that was the right of the heirs, and the original one-third remains, so it is given to the legatee. If the types are various, then neither coercion is possible nor can all be combined in a single item, and when these things are not present, the precedence of the bequest over inheritance is not established, nor can the issue of original and subordinate apply. This is the summary of the proof.
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between the majority Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa and the two companions) and Imam Zufar regarding a bequest of a fractional share when part of the bequeathed property is destroyed. The case: A man bequeaths one-third of his dirhams or goats. Before execution, two-thirds of those dirhams/goats are destroyed, leaving only one-third. The testator also has other wealth sufficient to cover the bequest from the one-third of his total estate. The question: Does the legatee receive the entire remaining third, or only one-third of that remaining third? Imam Zufar argues the latter, based on the principle of common property: the bequeathed items are common between legatee and heirs, so destruction and remaining should be shared proportionally. He analogizes to the case of multiple types (e.g., goats, camels, cows) where by consensus the legatee gets only one-third of the remaining portion of each type. The Hanafi majority rejects this analogy, distinguishing between a single genus (jins wahid) and multiple types (ajnas mukhtalifa). In a single genus, the judge can coerce division among partners (jabr), and it is possible to combine all rights in one item. The bequest takes precedence over inheritance, making the legatee's right the original (asl) and the heirs' right subordinate (taba'). Applying the rule that destruction falls on the subordinate, the two-thirds destroyed is attributed to the heirs' share, so the remaining third goes entirely to the legatee. In multiple types, coercion is not possible, so the proportional approach applies, and the legatee gets only one-third of the remaining of each type. This distinction is rooted in the laws of division (qisma) as established in Kitab al-Qisma.

Key Terms
جنس واحد (jins wāḥid): Items of the same type or category, e.g., dirhams with dirhams, goats with goats.
اجناس مختلفة (ajnās mukhtalifa): Items of different types or categories, e.g., goats, camels, cows.
جبر (jabr): Coercion by the judge to force partners into dividing common property when one requests.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a Hanafi bequest of one-third of dirhams, if two-thirds of the dirhams are destroyed before execution, what does the legatee receive?
A) Nothing, because the property is destroyed.
B) One-third of the remaining one-third dirhams.
C) The entire remaining one-third dirhams.
D) Only one-third of the total original dirhams.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when a bequest of a fractional share in a single-genus property is partially destroyed, the legatee receives the entire remaining portion because the bequest is given precedence over inheritance and the destruction is attributed to the heirs' share.

Wasiyyah — Bequest

Bequest of One-Third of Clothes When Two-Thirds Destroyed
Ruling on legatee's share when bequeathed clothes partially destroyed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule for a legatee's share when bequeathed property is partially destroyed, and distinguish between single-genus and multi-genus property.

Core Idea
When bequeathed property is partly destroyed, the legatee's entitlement depends on whether the property is one type or multiple types.

In this lesson, we examine a scenario where a testator bequeaths one-third of his clothes, but two-thirds of the clothes are destroyed before distribution. The key question is whether the legatee receives one-third of the remaining clothes or the entire remaining third. The Hanafi ruling turns on a subtle but crucial distinction: whether the clothes are all of the same type or of different types. This ruling also draws an analogy with bequests of dirhams, which we will explore first.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic rule for a specific number
If the testator bequeaths a specific number of items (e.g., one dirham) and some are destroyed, the legatee gets that specific item if it remains intact, not a fraction of the remaining.
This is the first part of the passage, clarifying the principle.
2
Apply the rule to clothes of different types
When the bequest is one-third of clothes, and the clothes are of different types (e.g., shirts, cloaks, turbans), the legatee receives only one-third of what remains. The destruction is attributed proportionally across types.
Because different types are treated as separate genera.
3
Apply the rule to clothes of the same type
If all clothes are of the same type (e.g., all shirts), the legatee receives the entire remaining third. This is analogous to the dirham case where the legatee gets the specific item.
Single genus property is treated as one unit; the bequest takes precedence over the destruction.
4
Connect to the one-third of estate condition
The passage mentions that the bequest is taken from the one-third of what remains of the testator's wealth. The legatee's share is subject to the overall limit of one-third of the estate.
This condition is assumed in the discussion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و ا گر موصی دراہم کے بجائے درہم کہتا مثلاً یوں کہتا کہ میں نے فلاں کو ایک درہم ہبہ کیا اول مثلا تین دراہم تھے ان میں سے دو ہلاک ہو گئے اور ایک باقی رہ گیا تو یہ ایک موصی لہ کو دیا جائے گا یعنی یہاں یہ نہیں کہا جائے گا کہ اس میں ایک ثلث موصی لہ کو دیا جائے گا۔ باقی بات واضح ہے۔ موصی اپنے کپڑوں کے ثلث کی وصیت کرے اور اتفاقا کپڑوں سے دو ثلث ختم ہو جائے اور صرف ایک ثلث باقی رہ جائے تو موصی لہ کو مابقی کا ثلث ملے گا یا پورا مابقی
قال ولو اوصى بثلث ثيابه فهلک ثلثاها وبقى ثلثها وهو يخرج من ثلث ما بقى من ماله لم يستحق الاثلث ما بقى من الثياب قالوا هذا اذا كانت الثياب من اجناس مختلفة ولو كانت من جنس واحد فهو بمنزلة الدراهم
ترجمہ اور اگر وصیت کی اپنے کپڑوں کے ثلث کی پس دو ثلث ہلاک ہو گئے اور صرف ایک ثلث باقی رہ گیا اور وہ اس کے مال کے ثلث سے نکلتا ہے جو استحقاق ثلث باقی کپڑوں کا نہیں ہے لوگوں نے فرمایا یہ حکم اس صورت میں ہے کہ جب کپڑے مختلف اجناس کے ہوں اور اگر ایک جنس کے ہوں تو وہ دراہم کی طرح ہے۔
And if the testator says 'dirham' instead of 'dirhams', for example says: I gave so-and-so one dirham as a gift, or such that there were three dirhams, two of them were destroyed and one remained, then that one will be given to the legatee, i.e., it will not be said that one-third of it is given to the legatee. The rest is clear. The testator bequeaths one-third of his clothes, and by chance two-thirds of the clothes are destroyed and only one-third remains, then will the legatee get one-third of what remains or the entire remaining? He said: And if he bequeaths one-third of his clothes, then two-thirds are destroyed and one-third remains, and it is taken from one-third of what remains of his wealth, he does not deserve the entire remaining portion of the clothes. They said: This is when the clothes are of different types; if they are of one type, then it is like the case of dirhams. Translation: And if he bequeaths one-third of his clothes, then two-thirds are destroyed and one-third remains, and it is taken from one-third of what remains of his wealth, he does not deserve the entire remaining portion of the clothes. They said: This ruling is when the clothes are of different types; if they are of one type, then it is like dirhams.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage extends the previous discussion to a bequest of one-third of clothes. It first clarifies a nuance: if the bequest is of a specific number (e.g., one dirham) rather than a fraction, then the legatee gets that specific item if it exists, not a proportion. Then it addresses the clothes case: if a person bequeaths one-third of his clothes, and two-thirds of the clothes are destroyed, the ruling depends on the nature of the clothes. If the clothes are of different types (e.g., shirts, turbans, cloaks), the legatee receives only one-third of what remains, because the types cannot be combined (as in multiple genera). If the clothes are all of the same type (e.g., all shirts), then the ruling is like that of dirhams: the legatee receives the entire remaining third. This is consistent with the earlier principle: in a single genus, the bequest takes precedence and the destruction is attributed to the heirs' share, so the legatee gets the full remaining one-third.

Key Terms
ثلث (thuluth): One-third; a fractional share commonly used in bequests.
ثیاب (thiyāb): Clothes; considered movable property subject to bequest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A testator bequeaths one-third of his clothes to Zaid. The clothes consist of 10 shirts and 10 trousers. Two-thirds of the shirts and two-thirds of the trousers are destroyed. What does Zaid receive?
A) The 3 remaining shirts and 3 remaining trousers (all remaining)
B) One shirt and one trouser (one from each type)
C) One-third of the remaining shirts (1 shirt) and one-third of the remaining trousers (1 trouser)
D) Nothing; the bequest fails because most is destroyed

Key Takeaway
When bequeathed property is partially destroyed, the legatee's entitlement depends on whether the property is a single genus or multiple genera: if single genus, the legatee takes all remaining; if multiple genera, only a proportional share.

Wasiyyah — Bequest
intermediate

Bequest of a Third of Dirhams and Rebuttal of Imam Zufar's Analogy
Establishes ruling and refutes intra-Hanafi dissent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why, in Hanafi fiqh, a legatee of a third of homogeneous property receives the entire remaining amount when part perishes, and evaluate Imam Zufar's analogy as invalid due to a material distinction.

Core Idea
In homogeneous property, bequest takes precedence and loss falls on heirs, so legatee gets the full remaining.

This passage addresses a specific dispute within the Hanafi school regarding the execution of a bequest when part of the bequeathed property perishes before distribution. The ruling depends on whether the property is of a single genus (jins wahid) or multiple genera. Understanding this illustrates the Hanafi method of istihsan and their careful distinction between analogous cases.

Guided Path
1
State the majority Hanafi ruling
Identify the ruling: when a testator bequeaths one-third of his dirhams (a single genus) and two-thirds perish, the legatee receives the entire remaining one-third, not just a third of that remainder.
This is the position of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
2
Explain the Hanafi proof
The proof is based on istihsan: in a single genus, the judge can coerce partition and combine rights. The bequest is given precedence over inheritance, so the legatee's right is the original (asl) and the heirs' right is subordinate (taba'). When loss occurs, it is attributed to the subordinate portion.
Reference: 'Our proof is that in a single genus, it is possible to combine each one's right into one...'
3
Present Imam Zufar's objection
Imam Zufar analogizes to heterogeneous property: if two-thirds of property from different genera perish, the legatee receives only one-third of the remaining (i.e., a fraction). He argues the same should apply here.
This analogy would give the legatee only 100 dirhams if the original bequest was 300 and 600 perished, instead of 300.
4
Refute the analogy
The rebuttal is qiyas ma'a al-fariq: the analogy is invalid because in heterogeneous property, coercion in partition is not possible, and rights cannot be combined into one item. Therefore, the precedence of bequest cannot operate the same way.
This distinction is established in Kitab al-Qisma.
5
Apply the principle to a specific dirham bequest
If the testator says 'I bequeath one dirham' instead of one-third, and three dirhams existed but two perished, the remaining single dirham goes entirely to the legatee. This reinforces the principle for specific (not fractional) bequests.
The logic is similar: the loss is attributed to the heirs' portion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

۱۲۹
كتاب الوصايا
اتفاق سے ہر ایک کے دو ثلث ہلاک ہو گئے اور صرف ایک ثلث باقی رہ گیا تو وہاں بالاتفاق موصی لہ کو ہر جنس کے مابھی ثلث کا ثلث دیا جائے گالہذا یہاں بھی ایسا ہی ہونا چاہئے ۔
امام زفر کی دلیل کا جواب
ولنا ان فى الجنس الواحد يمكن جمع حق احدهم فى الواحد ولهذا يجرى فيه الجبر على القسمة وفيه جمع والوصية مقدمة فجمعناها فى الواحد الباقى وصارت الدراهم كالدرهم بخلاف الاجناس المختلفة لانه لا يمكن الجمع فيها جبرا فكذا تقديما
ترجمہ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ جنس واحد میں ان میں سے ہر ایک کے حق کو ایک میں جمع کرناممکن ہے اس لئے جنس واحد میں تقسیم پر جبر جاری ہوتا ہے اور تقسیم میں جمع کرنا ہے اور وصیت مقدم ہے تو ہم نے اس کو ایک باقی میں جمع کر دیا اور دور اہم درہم کے مثل ہو گیا بخلاف اجناس مختلفہ کے اس لئے کہ اجناس مختلفہ میں تقسیم پر جبر کے اعتبار سے جمع کرنا ممکن نہیں ہے پس ایسے ہی باعتبار تقدیم کے۔ تشریح یہ ہماری طرف سے امام زفر کی دلیل کا جواب ہے ۔ جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ جنس واحد کو اجناس مختلفہ پر قیاس کرنا قیاس مع الفارق ہے اس لئے کہ کتاب القسمہ میں یہ بحث گزر چکی ہے۔ جنس واحد میں قسمت کی درخواست پر قاضی باقی شرکاء پر جبر کرے گا اور اجناس مختلفہ کی صورت میں قاضی جبر نہیں کرے گا اور اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ جنس واحد میں ایک چیز کے چند شر کا ء کو جمع کیا جا سکتا ہے یعنی اس کے اندر موصی لہ کا بھی حق ہو اور ورثا کا بھی حق ہو لہذا جب اجتماع ہو گیا یعنی جنس واحد کی صورت میں ۹۰۰ ر درا ہم میں تو موصی لہ کا حق مقدم ہوگا اسلئے کہ وصیت میراث سے مقدم ہوتی ہے تو اس میں موصی لہا کا حق اصالہ ہے اور دور خا کا حق سبعا ہے اور پھر اصول کلی یہ ہے کہ جب کوئی مال اصل اور تابع پر مشتمل ہو اور اس میں سے کچھ ہلاک ہو جائے تو ہلاکت کو تابع کی جانب پھیرا جاتا ہے اصل کی طرف نہیں جیسے مال مضاربت میں ایسا ہی ہوتا ہے لہذا یہاں ہلاکت کو اس ثلثان کی طرف پھیرا جائے گا جو دور تا کا حق تھا اور اصل ثلث باقی ہے لہذا وہ موصی لیہ کو دیا جائے گا۔ اور اگر اجناس مختلفہ ہوں تو وہاں نہ جبر ہو سکتا ہے اور نہ سب کوشی واحد میں جمع کیا جا سکتا ہے اور جب یہ ساری چیزیں نہ ہوں گی تو وصیت کی میراث پر تقدیم بھی ثابت نہ ہو سکے گی اور نہ اصل اور تبع والا مسئلہ جاری ہو سکے گا یہ دلیل کا ماحصل ہو گیا۔
اور اگر موصی دراہم کے بجائے درہم کہتا مثلاً یوں کہتا کہ میں نے فلاں کو ایک درہم ہبہ کیا اول مثلا تین دراہم تھے ان میں سے دو ہلاک ہو گئے اور ایک باقی رہ گیا تو یہ ایک موصی لہ کو دیا جائے گا یعنی یہاں یہ نہیں کہا جائے گا کہ اس میں ایک ثلث موصی لہ کو دیا جائے گا۔ باقی بات واضح ہے۔
From Ashraf al-Hidayah, Urdu commentary on al-Hidayah, volume 16, page 129, Book of Bequests. By agreement, if two-thirds of each (genus) perished and only one-third remained, unanimously the legatee is given a third of a third of each genus. So here it should be the same. Ruling: Our proof is that in a single genus, it is possible to combine each one's right into one, and for this reason coercion (jabr) on division applies, and there is combination (jama'), and the bequest is given precedence, so we combine it into the single remaining (item), and the dirhams become like a single dirham, unlike different genera because combination by coercion is not possible in them, and similarly in terms of precedence. Commentary: This is our response to Imam Zufar's proof. The gist is that analogizing a single genus to different genera is an analogy with a difference (qiyas ma'a al-fariq) because in the Book of Partition it has been discussed: for a single genus, the judge will coerce the remaining partners upon request for partition, but for different genera the judge will not coerce. The reason is that in a single genus, the rights of multiple parties can be combined in one thing, meaning both the legatee's right and the heirs' right can be in it. So when combination occurs, i.e., in the case of a single genus with 900 dirhams, the legatee's right is given precedence because bequest is given precedence over inheritance. Thus the legatee's right is the original (asl) and the heirs' right is subordinate (taba'). The general principle is: when property consists of an original and a subordinate, and part of it perishes, the loss is attributed to the subordinate not the original, as in mudarabah property. So here, the loss is attributed to the two-thirds that were the heirs' right, and the original third remains, so it is given to the legatee. But if there are different genera, neither coercion nor combination into one is possible, and since these factors are absent, the precedence of bequest over inheritance cannot be established, nor can the original-subordinate principle apply. This is the summary of the proof. And if the testator says 'a dirham' instead of 'dirhams', e.g., he says 'I gave him one dirham as a hibah', and originally there were three dirhams, two perished and one remains, then that one is given to the legatee, meaning it is not said that only one-third is given. The rest is clear.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute addressing a scenario where a testator bequeaths a third of his dirhams, and two-thirds of the dirhams perish before execution. The unanimous agreement among the Hanafi scholars (including Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) is that if the dirhams are of one genus, the entire remaining amount (the one-third that survived) is given to the legatee, not merely a third of that remainder. This is because the bequest is given precedence over inheritance, and the loss is attributed to the heirs' portion since their right is subordinate. Imam Zufar analogized this to the case of different genera, where the legatee only receives a third of the remainder. The author refutes this by explaining the distinction: in a single genus, the judge can coerce partition and combine rights, whereas in different genera this is not possible. Therefore, the analogy is invalid. The passage then gives a simpler case: if the testator bequeaths a specific dirham (not a third), and two of three dirhams perish, the remaining single dirham goes entirely to the legatee. This follows from the principle that a specific legacy takes priority.

Key Terms
جنس واحد (jins wahid): A single genus or type of property, e.g., all dirhams are of one genus.
جبر (jabr): Coercion by the judge to force partners to accept partition of jointly owned property.
قیاس مع الفارق (qiyas ma'a al-fariq): An invalid analogy because the two cases differ in a legally significant way.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A testator bequeaths one-third of his 900 dirhams (all of one genus). Before distribution, 300 dirhams are lost. How much does the legatee receive?
A) 200 dirhams
B) 300 dirhams
C) 600 dirhams
D) 100 dirhams

Key Takeaway
In homogeneous property, the legatee's right is original and loss falls on the heirs' subordinate portion, so the legatee receives the entire surviving amount up to his bequest.

Bequest of a Third When Property Perishes: Genus Condition and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling on bequest of a third when part perishes, with genus condition and intra-Hanafi dispute on jabar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rulings on bequest of a third when part of the property perishes, distinguishing between homogeneous and heterogeneous goods, and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding slaves and houses.

Core Idea
For bequest of a third, the legatee's share depends on whether the property is homogeneous (entire remainder) or heterogeneous (third of remainder), with a dispute for slaves and houses.

In this lesson, we explore a nuanced area of Hanafi inheritance law: what happens when the property subject to a bequest of a third partially perishes before distribution. The ruling hinges on the nature of the property—whether it is homogeneous or heterogeneous—and for certain assets like slaves and houses, there is a well-known intra-Hanafi disagreement. By the end, you will be able to navigate these scenarios with precision.

Guided Path
1
Identify the property type and genus condition for clothes
For clothes, if they are of different genera, the legatee receives only a third of the remaining clothes; if of one genus, he receives the entire remaining.
This is based on the principle that homogeneous goods are like dirhams.
2
Extend the ruling to makil and mawzun
Substances measured by volume or weight also follow the same rule because coercion in partition (jabr) applies to them.
Makil and mawzun items are considered like dirhams.
3
Apply the same logic to slaves and houses
For slaves and houses, there is a dispute among the Hanafi school. The text presents two views.
The dispute revolves around whether jabar applies to these items.
4
Recognize the intra-Hanafi dispute and its resolution
Abu Hanifa does not allow coercion for slaves/houses, so the legatee gets only a third of the remainder. The Sahibayn allow the judge to combine shares through ijtihad, potentially giving the entire remainder. The preferred view is Abu Hanifa's.
The text states 'al-awwal ashbah' (the first is more similar).

Source Text

موصی اپنے کپڑوں کے ثلث کی وصیت کرے اور اتفاقا کپڑوں سے دو ثلث ختم ہو جائے
اور صرف ایک ثلث باقی رہ جائے تو موصی لہ کو مابقی کا ثلث ملے گا یا پورا مابقی
قال ولو اوصى بثلث ثيابه فهلک ثلثاها وبقى ثلثها وهو يخرج من ثلث ما بقى من ماله لم يستحق الاثلث ما بقى من الثياب قالوا هذا اذا كانت الثياب من اجناس مختلفة ولو كانت من جنس واحد فهو بمنزلة الدراهم
وكذلك المكيل والموزون بمنزلتها لانه يجرى فيه الجمع جبرا با
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور اگر اپنے تہائی کپڑوں کی وصیت کی نپس ان کپڑوں میں سے دو ثلث ختم ہو گئے اور ان کا ثلث باقی رو گیا اور یہ ( ثلث باقی ) اس کے مابقی مال کے ثلث سے خارج ہو جاتا ہے تو موصی لا مستحق نہ ہوگا مگر مابقی کپڑوں کے ثالث کا ۔ مشائخ نے فرمایا ہے کہ یہ اس وقت ہے جبکہ کپڑے مختلف جنس کے ہوں اور اگر کپڑے ایک جنس کے ہوں تو کپڑے دراہم کے درجہ میں ہیں اور ایسے ہی ہر کیلی اور وزنی چیز دراہم کے درجہ میں ہے اسلئے کہ اس میں ( کیلی اور وزنی چیز میں ) جمع کرنا جاری ہو جاتا ہے تقسیم کے اندر جبر کے اعتبار سے ۔
تشریح اگر موسی نے اپنے کپڑوں کے ثالث کی وصیت کی ہو اور اتفاق سے ان کپڑوں میں سے دو ثلث ختم ہو جائیں اور صرف ایک ثلث باقی رہ جائے تو موصی لہ کو مابقی کا ثلث ملے گا یا پورا مابھی ملے گا۔؟
تو اس میں تفصیل ہے اگر کپڑے مختلف الجنس ہوں تو مابقی کپڑوں کا ثث ملے گا اور اگر ایک جنس کے ہوں تو پورا مابقی ملے گا اسلئے کہ اتحاد جنس کی صورت میں کپڑے دراہم کے مثل ہو گئے اور اسی طرح ہر کیلی اور وزنی چیز بھی دراہم کے درجہ میں ہے کیونکہ جس طرح دراہم میں تقسیم پر جبر جائز ہے اسی طرح کیلی اور روز نی اشیاء میں تقسیم پر جبر جائز ہے اور جیسے دراہم وغیرہ میں جمع کرنا ممکن ہے اسی طرح کیلی اور وزنی چیز میں جمع کرنا ممکن ہے۔ موصی تین غلاموں میں ایک ثات شکایت کرے اور پھر دوغلام مر گئے اور ایک باقی رہ گیا تو
موصی لہ کو اس ایک غلام کا ثلث ملے گا اور چند مختلف گھروں میں بھی یہی حکم ہے
ولو اوصى بثلث ثلثة من رقيقه فمات اثنان لم يكن له الاثلث الباقى وكذا الدور المختلفة وقيل هذا على قول ابي حنيفة وحده لانه لا يرى الجبر على القسمة فيها وقيل هو قول الكل لان عندهما للقاضى ان يجتهد ويجمع وبدون ذلك يتعذر الجمع والاول اشبه للفقه المذكور
ترجمہ اور اگر اس نے وصیت کی اپنے تین غلاموں میں سے ثالث کی پس دو مر گئے تو نہیں ہو گا موصی لہ کیلئے ، مگر ما بقی کا ثلث اور ایسے ہی مختلف گھر اور کہا گیا ہے کہ یہ ابو حنیفہ کے قول پر ہے اسلئے کہ وہ ان میں ( دور مختلفہ اور غلاموں میں) قسمت پر جبر کو جائز نہیں قرار دیتے اور کہا گیا ہے کہ یہ سب کا قول ہے اس لئے کہ صاحبین کے نزدیک قاضی کو حق ہے کہ وہ ایسا اجتہاد کرے اور جمع کرے اور قاضی کے اجتہاد کے بغیر جمع کرنا معذ رہے اور اول (یعنی اس میں اختلاف کا ہونا ) فقہ مذکور کے زیادہ مشابہ ہے۔ تشریح اگر زید نے اپنے تین غلاموں میں سے ثلث کی وصیت کی اور پھر دو غلام مر گئے اور ایک باقی رہ گیا تو موصی لہ کو اس ایک غلام کا ثلث دیا جائے گا اور چند مختلف گھر ہوں تو اس میں بھی یہی حکم ہے۔
پھڑی یہ بات کہ اس میں اختلاف ہے یا نہیں تو اس میں مشائخ کے دو قول ہیں۔
یہ فقط امام صاحب کا قول ہے اس لئے کہ ان کے نزدیک مذکورہ اشیاء میں تقسیم پر جبر جائز نہیں تو اس کا وہ حکم ہو گا جو اختلاف جنس کی صورت میں ہوتا ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک ان میں تقسیم پر جبر جائز ہے تو یہ دراہم کے درجہ میں ہوں گے۔
If a testator bequeaths a third of his clothes, and two-thirds of the clothes perish and only one-third remains, will the legatee receive a third of the remainder or the entire remainder? He said: 'And if he bequeaths a third of his clothes, and two-thirds of them perish and one-third remains, and it comes out of the third of the remainder of his wealth, he is not entitled except to a third of the remaining clothes.' They said: This is when the clothes are of different genera; but if they are of one genus, they are like dirhams. Similarly, measureable (makil) and weighable (mawzun) items are like them because combination by coercion in partition applies to them. Translation: Al-Quduri said: And if he bequeaths a third of his clothes, then two-thirds of those clothes perished and one-third remained, and it (the remaining third) comes out of the third of the remainder of his wealth, the legatee is not entitled except to a third of the remaining clothes. The mashayikh said: This is when the clothes are of different genera; if they are of one genus, clothes are like dirhams, and similarly every measureable and weighable item is like dirhams because combination by coercion in partition applies to them. Commentary: If a testator bequeaths a third of his clothes and two-thirds of them perish, and only one-third remains, does the legatee receive a third of the remainder or the entire remainder? Detail: If the clothes are of different genera, he receives a third of the remaining clothes; if they are of one genus, he receives the entire remainder because in case of unity of genus, clothes become like dirhams. Similarly, every measureable and weighable item is like dirhams because just as coercion in partition is permissible for dirhams, it is also permissible for measureable and weighable items, and just as combination is possible for dirhams, it is possible for them. If a testator bequeaths a third of three slaves, and two slaves die, leaving one, the legatee receives a third of that one slave. The same ruling applies to different houses. And if he bequeaths a third of three slaves, and two die, he is not entitled to a third of the remaining one; likewise for different houses. It is said that this is only the opinion of Abu Hanifa because he does not permit coercion in partition for such items. And it is said that it is the opinion of all because according to the Sahibayn, the judge has the right to exercise his ijtihad and combine, and without that, combination is difficult. The first opinion is more similar to the fiqh mentioned. Commentary: If Zaid bequeaths a third of three slaves, and two slaves die, leaving one, the legatee is given a third of that one slave. The same applies to several different houses. Then there is a dispute among the mashayikh: some say this is only Imam Abu Hanifa's view because he does not permit coercion in partition for these items, so the ruling is like that for different genera; others say it is the view of all because the Sahibayn permit coercion, so these items become like dirhams.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on bequest of a third of specific types of property when part of the property perishes. The first scenario concerns clothes: if the clothes are of different genera, the legatee receives only a third of the remaining clothes; if they are of one genus, he receives the entire remaining clothes because they are treated like dirhams. The same rule extends to measurable (makil) and weighable (mawzun) items because they allow coercion in partition. The second scenario involves slaves and houses: for three slaves, if two die, the legatee receives a third of the remaining one, not the whole. However, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: according to Abu Hanifa, this is the absolute ruling because he does not allow coercion in partition for slaves and houses; according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the judge may use ijtihad to combine shares, and if he does, the ruling would be like dirhams. The text notes that the first view (that there is a dispute) is more consistent with the previously mentioned fiqh principles.

Key Terms
مکیل (makil): Items measured by volume, like wheat or barley.
موزون (mawzun): Items weighed by weight, like gold or silver.
جبر على القسمة (jabr 'ala al-qisma): Coercion by the judge to force partners into accepting partition of jointly owned property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view in this passage, if a testator bequeaths a third of his three slaves and two die, what does the legatee receive?
A) The entire remaining slave.
B) One-third of the remaining slave.
C) Nothing, because the bequest fails.
D) Two-thirds of the remaining slave.

Key Takeaway
For bequest of a third when property perishes, homogeneous goods give the entire remainder, heterogeneous give a third of remainder, and for slaves/houses the preferred view is a third of remainder due to the absence of jabar.

Bequest of One-Third of Specific Items When Part Is Destroyed: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Forced Division
Ruling and intra-madhhab dispute on bequest of specific items partially destroyed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a bequest of one-third of specific items when part is destroyed and explain the dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding forced division (qisma jabr).

Core Idea
The legatee's entitlement to the remaining item depends on whether the items are fungible and whether qisma jabr is allowed.

When a testator bequeaths one-third of specific items (e.g., three slaves or a set of clothes) and some are destroyed before distribution, the legatee does not simply take everything left. The Hanafi school provides a nuanced ruling that hinges on the nature of the items and whether forced division is possible. In this lesson, we will examine the ruling from the matn of Quduri, its expansion in Al-Hidayah, and the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is a bequest of one-third of specific items (e.g., clothes, slaves, houses). The base ruling from the matn: if two-thirds are lost, the legatee gets only one-third of the remaining items. However, if the items are of the same genus (e.g., all cotton clothes), they are treated like dirhams, and the legatee gets the entire remaining item(s).
This is the starting point before the dispute is introduced.
2
Understand the basis: analogy to dirhams
The text analogizes clothes, measurable, and weighable items to dirhams because forced division (qisma jabr) is possible in all these cases. This qiyas (analogy) is the core reasoning behind the ruling for same-genus items.
The effective cause (illa) is the ability to force division among co-owners.
3
Explore the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Hanifa does not permit forced division in non-fungible items like slaves and houses, so even if the items are of the same genus, he rules that the legatee gets only one-third of the remaining. The Sahibayn permit forced division in such items, so they would give the legatee the entire remaining item(s).
The dispute hinges on whether qisma jabr applies to non-fungibles.
4
Evaluate the tarjih
The author (Al-Marghinani) prefers the view that the ruling is specific to Abu Hanifa (al-awwal ashbah). There is also a view that it is a consensus opinion, but that requires the qadi's ijtihad to have occurred before the loss, which is not the case here.
The preferred view leads to a practical consequence: in the absence of a qadi's judgment, the legatee takes only one-third of the remaining, even according to the Sahibayn.

Source Text

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۹
وكذلك المكيل والموزون بمنزلتها لانه يجرى فيه الجمع جبرا با
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور اگر اپنے تہائی کپڑوں کی وصیت کی نپس ان کپڑوں میں سے دو ثلث ختم ہو گئے اور ان کا ثلث باقی رو گیا اور یہ ( ثلث باقی ) اس کے مابقی مال کے ثلث سے خارج ہو جاتا ہے تو موصی لا مستحق نہ ہوگا مگر مابقی کپڑوں کے ثالث کا ۔ مشائخ نے فرمایا ہے کہ یہ اس وقت ہے جبکہ کپڑے مختلف جنس کے ہوں اور اگر کپڑے ایک جنس کے ہوں تو کپڑے دراہم کے درجہ میں ہیں اور ایسے ہی ہر کیلی اور وزنی چیز دراہم کے درجہ میں ہے اسلئے کہ اس میں ( کیلی اور وزنی چیز میں ) جمع کرنا جاری ہو جاتا ہے تقسیم کے اندر جبر کے اعتبار سے ۔
تشریح اگر موسی نے اپنے کپڑوں کے ثالث کی وصیت کی ہو اور اتفاق سے ان کپڑوں میں سے دو ثلث ختم ہو جائیں اور صرف ایک ثلث باقی رہ جائے تو موصی لہ کو مابقی کا ثلث ملے گا یا پورا مابھی ملے گا۔؟
تو اس میں تفصیل ہے اگر کپڑے مختلف الجنس ہوں تو مابقی کپڑوں کا ثث ملے گا اور اگر ایک جنس کے ہوں تو پورا مابقی ملے گا اسلئے کہ اتحاد جنس کی صورت میں کپڑے دراہم کے مثل ہو گئے اور اسی طرح ہر کیلی اور وزنی چیز بھی دراہم کے درجہ میں ہے کیونکہ جس طرح دراہم میں تقسیم پر جبر جائز ہے اسی طرح کیلی اور روز نی اشیاء میں تقسیم پر جبر جائز ہے اور جیسے دراہم وغیرہ میں جمع کرنا ممکن ہے اسی طرح کیلی اور وزنی چیز میں جمع کرنا ممکن ہے۔ موصی تین غلاموں میں ایک ثات شکایت کرے اور پھر دوغلام مر گئے اور ایک باقی رہ گیا تو
موصی لہ کو اس ایک غلام کا ثلث ملے گا اور چند مختلف گھروں میں بھی یہی حکم ہے
ولو اوصى بثلث ثلثة من رقيقه فمات اثنان لم يكن له الاثلث الباقى وكذا الدور المختلفة وقيل هذا على قول ابي حنيفة وحده لانه لا يرى الجبر على القسمة فيها وقيل هو قول الكل لان عندهما للقاضى ان يجتهد ويجمع وبدون ذلك يتعذر الجمع والاول اشبه للفقه المذكور
ترجمہ اور اگر اس نے وصیت کی اپنے تین غلاموں میں سے ثالث کی پس دو مر گئے تو نہیں ہو گا موصی لہ کیلئے ، مگر ما بقی کا ثلث اور ایسے ہی مختلف گھر اور کہا گیا ہے کہ یہ ابو حنیفہ کے قول پر ہے اسلئے کہ وہ ان میں ( دور مختلفہ اور غلاموں میں) قسمت پر جبر کو جائز نہیں قرار دیتے اور کہا گیا ہے کہ یہ سب کا قول ہے اس لئے کہ صاحبین کے نزدیک قاضی کو حق ہے کہ وہ ایسا اجتہاد کرے اور جمع کرے اور قاضی کے اجتہاد کے بغیر جمع کرنا معذ رہے اور اول (یعنی اس میں اختلاف کا ہونا ) فقہ مذکور کے زیادہ مشابہ ہے۔ تشریح اگر زید نے اپنے تین غلاموں میں سے ثلث کی وصیت کی اور پھر دو غلام مر گئے اور ایک باقی رہ گیا تو موصی لہ کو اس ایک غلام کا ثلث دیا جائے گا اور چند مختلف گھر ہوں تو اس میں بھی یہی حکم ہے۔
پھڑی یہ بات کہ اس میں اختلاف ہے یا نہیں تو اس میں مشائخ کے دو قول ہیں۔
یہ فقط امام صاحب کا قول ہے اس لئے کہ ان کے نزدیک مذکورہ اشیاء میں تقسیم پر جبر جائز نہیں تو اس کا وہ حکم ہو گا جو اختلاف جنس کی صورت میں ہوتا ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک ان میں تقسیم پر جبر جائز ہے تو یہ دراہم کے درجہ میں ہوں گے۔
اور دوسرا قول یہ ہے کہ یہ سب کا اجماعی قول ہے تو اس صورت میں صاحبین پر اعتراض وارد ہوتا ہے مگر ان کی جانب سے یہ جواب دیا گیا ہے کہ قاضی کے اجتہاد کے بغیر شرکاء میں سے کسی ایک کا حق مکان واحد یا غلام واحد میں جمع نہیں ہوسکتا اور جب دو غلام یا دو مکان تلف ہو گئے تو اس میں قاضی کا اجتہاد ابھی تک نہیں ہوا پس مابقی مال شرکت رہا تو موصی لہ کو مابقی کا صرف تہائی ملے گا اور یہی امام صاحب کا قول ہے۔ مگر مصنف نے قول اول کو ترجیح دی ہے۔
The bequest of one-third of clothes: if two-thirds are lost and one-third remains, the legatee is entitled only to one-third of the remaining clothes. The scholars said this is when the clothes are of different types. If they are of one type, clothes are like dirhams, and similarly every measurable or weighable item is like dirhams because combining them by force is possible in division. Explanation: If the clothes are of different types, he gets one-third of the remaining; if same type, he gets the entire remaining. Similarly, for three slaves: if he bequeaths one-third of three slaves and two die, he gets only one-third of the remaining slave, and similarly for different houses. It is said this is only the opinion of Abu Hanifa because he does not permit forced division. It is also said it is the consensus opinion because according to the two companions, the judge may exercise ijtihad and combine, and without that combination is difficult. The first view is more appropriate.
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of a ruling from Quduri's matn with an intra-Hanafi dispute. The ruling: if someone bequeaths one-third of specific items (clothes, slaves, houses) and part of those items are destroyed before distribution, the legatee's entitlement depends on whether the items are of the same genus. If different genera, he gets one-third of the remaining items only. If same genus (e.g., all cotton clothes, all male slaves), he gets the entire remaining item(s) because they are treated like dirhams—forced division (jabr) is possible to allocate the legacy. The dispute: Is this ruling specific to Abu Hanifa or agreed upon? Abu Hanifa does not allow forced division in such items, so the legatee gets only one-third of the remaining. The Sahibayn allow forced division, so for them the legatee would get the entire remaining. However, some scholars argue that even for the Sahibayn, since the judge's ijtihad has not yet occurred at the time of destruction (the two items are gone before distribution), the remaining item remains a shared property, so the legatee gets only one-third. The author (Marghinani) prefers the first view that it is only Abu Hanifa's position.

Key Terms
ثلث (thuluth): One-third of the estate or of a specific bequeathed item.
جبر (jabr): Forced division of joint property by a qadi to allocate shares.
قسمة (qisma): Division of shared property among co-owners.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The entire remaining slave
B) One-third of the remaining slave
C) One-half of the remaining slave
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
The legatee's entitlement after partial loss of bequeathed items depends on the genus of the items and the permissibility of forced division, with a key intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Bequest of a Fixed Sum When Estate Includes Cash and Debts
Ruling on distribution of a fixed bequest from mixed assets of cash and debts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling for distributing a fixed bequest when the estate consists of both cash and debts, and explain the rationale based on partnership and the nature of debt.

Core Idea
The legatee is a partner; both cash and debts are shared proportionally to avoid harming heirs.

This passage from Quduri's matn and its commentary addresses a practical scenario: a testator bequeaths a fixed sum (1000 dirhams) but leaves an estate with both cash and outstanding debts. How should the bequest be paid? The Hanafi ruling balances the rights of the legatee and the heirs by treating the legatee as a partner and recognizing that debt is not wealth until collected. In this lesson, you will work through the rule step by step and understand its equitable reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the estate components
Determine the cash ('ayn) and debts (dayn) in the estate. Note that debts are not yet collected.
Cash includes dirhams on hand; debts are amounts owed to the estate.
2
Compare bequest to one-third of cash
If one-third of the cash is equal to or exceeds the bequest amount, pay the full bequest from the cash. This is possible without prejudice to the heirs because the legatee's share of the cash is sufficient.
The one-third limit is from the total estate, but here we only consider cash for this step.
3
Proportional distribution when cash insufficient
If one-third of the cash is less than the bequest, the legatee receives one-third of the cash immediately. Then, as each debt is collected, the legatee takes one-third of that collected amount until the full bequest is satisfied.
The legatee does not get all the cash; the heirs share proportionally.
4
Understand the rationale
The legatee is a partner (sharik) with the heirs in the estate up to the bequest value. Giving only cash would harm the heirs because cash is readily available and debts are uncertain. Debt is not absolute wealth until collected, so both must share in both types of assets.
This prevents injustice (bakhs) against the heirs.

Source Text

قال و من اوصى لرجل بالف درهم وله مال عين ودين فان خرج الالف من ثلث العين دفع الى الموصى له لانه امکن ايفاء كل ذي حق حقه من غير بخس فيصار اليه وان لم يخرج دفع اليه ثلث العين وكل ما خرج شئى من الدين اخد ثلثه حتى يستوفى الالف لان الموصى له شریک الوارث وفی تخصیصه بالعين بخس في حق الورثة لان للعين فضلا على الدين ولان الدين ليس بمال فى مطلق الحال وانما يصير ما لا عند الاستيفاء فانما يعتدل النظر بما ذكرناه
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جس نے کسی شخص کیلئے ہزار درہم کی وصیت کی اور اس کیلئے نقد مال ہے اور قرض ہے پس اگر ہزار نکل جائیں نقد کے ثلث سے تو ہزار موصی لا کو دئیے جائیں گے اسلئے کہ ہر حق والے کو اس کا حق دینا ممکن ہے بغیر کسی کمی کے تو اس کی جانب رجوع کیا جائے گا اور اگر ہزار ثلث سے نہ نکلیں تو موصی لہ کو نقد مال کا ثث دیا جائے گا اور جو مقدار قرض کی وصول ہوتی رہے گی اس میں سے ٹکٹ لیتا رہے گا یہاں تک کہ وہ ( موصی لۂ ) ہزار کو وصول کرے اسلئے کہ موصی لہ وارث کا شریک ہے اور موصی لہ کو خاص کر دینے میں نقد مال کے ساتھ ورثہ کے حق میں کمی کرنا ہے اسلئے کہ نقد مال کو قرض پر فضیلت ہے اور اسلئے کہ قرض مطلق حال میں مال نہیں ہے وہ وصول کر لینے کے وقت مال بنتا ہے تو ( موصی لہ اور ورثا کے درمیان ) نظر کا اعتدال اس صورت میں ہے جس کو ہم نے ذکر کیا ہے۔
تشریح زید نے وصیت کی کہ میرے مال میں سے ہزار روپے بکر کو دیدئے جائیں تو وصیت درست ہے۔
لیکن زید نے کچھ مال تو نقد چھوڑا ہے اور کچھ مال وہ ہے جو لوگوں پر قرض ہے تو بکر کو جو ہزار روپے دئیے جائیں گے یہ نقد میں سے دیئے جائیں گے یا قرض میں سے تو اس کا جواب دیا کہ اگر نقد مال اتنا ہو کہ جس کا ثلث ہزار ہوتا ہومثلا تین ہزار یا اس سے زیادہ نقد مال موجود ہے تو بکر کو ہزار روپے اس نقد مال سے دیدئے جائیں گے یہ
را گر نقد مال اتنا نہیں ہے بلکہ کم ہے مثلا کل ہزار روپے نقد میں اور باقی مال لوگوں پر قرض ہے۔
تو بکر کو ہزار کا ثلث تو نقد میں سے دیا جائے گا اور باقی حصہ اس کو قرض میں سے ملے گا جس کی صورت یہ ہوگی کہ جتنا قرض وصول ہوتا جائے اس کی تنہائی بکر کو دیدی جائے یہاں تک کہ اس کا حق پورا ہو جائے یعنی ہزار روپے پورے ہو جائیں۔ طریقہ اختیار کرنے کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ موصی لڈ اور در تاتر کہ میں دونوں شریک ہیں اس کے باوجود اگر نقد مال فقط موصی لیہ کو دے دیا
He said: And whoever bequeaths to a man one thousand dirhams, and he has property in cash and debt, if the thousand comes out of one-third of the cash, it is given to the legatee because it is possible to give every right-holder his right without diminution, so it is followed. If it does not come out, he is given one-third of the cash, and whatever comes out of the debt, he takes one-third of it until the thousand is satisfied, because the legatee is a partner of the heir, and specifying him with cash is a diminution of the heirs' right because cash has superiority over debt, and because debt is not wealth in the absolute sense but becomes wealth upon collection. So the consideration is balanced by what we mentioned.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage from Quduri's matn, expanded by the commentator, explains the ruling when a bequest of a fixed sum (1000 dirhams) is made and the estate includes both cash ('ayn) and debts (dayn). The ruling: First, check if one-third of the cash alone equals or exceeds 1000 dirhams. If so, pay the entire bequest from the cash, because this satisfies all claimants without prejudice. If not, the legatee receives one-third of the cash (since the bequest is limited to one-third of the estate, but here the total estate includes debts). Then, as debts are collected, the legatee takes one-third of each collected amount until his 1000 is complete. The reason: The legatee is a partner of the heirs in the estate. Giving him only cash would harm the heirs because cash is more accessible and valuable than debt. Debt is not considered wealth until actually collected. Therefore, the equitable method is to allocate proportionally from both cash and debts.

Key Terms
عين (‘ayn): Tangible, present wealth (cash, goods on hand).
دين (dayn): Debt owed to the estate by others, not yet collected.
شريك (sharik): Partner; here, the legatee is a partner of the heirs in the estate up to the value of the bequest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 1000 dirhams
B) 600 dirhams
C) 200 dirhams
D) 400 dirhams

Key Takeaway
When a fixed bequest exceeds one-third of the cash, the legatee shares proportionally in both cash and debts to ensure fairness to heirs.

Wasiyyah — Bequest

6 min
Fulfilling a Bequest of 1000 Dirhams from Cash and Debts
Ruling on satisfying a bequest from mixed cash and debt assets

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on paying a bequest from an estate with both cash and debt, and explain the reasoning behind proportional distribution.

Core Idea
A bequest is paid proportionally from cash and debt when cash is insufficient because cash is superior and the legatee and heirs are partners.

This lesson examines a classic Hanafi ruling on executing a bequest when the estate contains both cash ('ayn) and debts (dayn). The ruling balances the rights of the legatee and the heirs, ensuring that neither party is disadvantaged by the quality of assets they receive. Understanding this principle is essential for correctly distributing bequests in mixed estates.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two asset types in the estate
Determine whether the testator left 'ayn (cash) and dayn (debt), and their amounts. This sets the stage for applying the ruling.
2
Classify the case based on cash sufficiency
Check if the bequest (1000 dirhams) can be covered by one-third of the cash alone. If the cash is at least 3000 dirhams, the bequest is paid entirely from cash. Otherwise, proceed to proportional distribution.
One-third of the cash is the maximum that can be allocated from cash without harming heirs.
3
Calculate the proportional payment
If cash is insufficient, the legatee receives one-third of the cash immediately. Then, as debts are collected, the legatee receives one-third of each collection until the total bequest is fulfilled.
This ensures the legatee gets a share of both asset types proportionate to the estate.
4
Explain the rationale of equity
The legatee is a partner with the heirs; cash is superior to debt because debt is not immediately disposable property. Exclusive cash would harm heirs, so proportional distribution maintains fairness.
The reasoning is based on the principle that no one should be unduly burdened.

Source Text

قال و من اوصى لرجل بالف درهم وله مال عين ودين فان خرج الالف من ثلث العين دفع الى الموصى له لانه امکن ايفاء كل ذي حق حقه من غير بخس فيصار اليه وان لم يخرج دفع اليه ثلث العين وكل ما خرج شئى من الدين اخد ثلثه حتى يستوفى الالف لان الموصى له شریک الوارث وفی تخصیصه بالعين بخس في حق الورثة لان للعين فضلا على الدين ولان الدين ليس بمال فى مطلق الحال وانما يصير ما لا عند الاستيفاء فانما يعتدل النظر بما ذكرناه
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جس نے کسی شخص کیلئے ہزار درہم کی وصیت کی اور اس کیلئے نقد مال ہے اور قرض ہے پس اگر ہزار نکل جائیں نقد کے ثلث سے تو ہزار موصی لا کو دئیے جائیں گے اسلئے کہ ہر حق والے کو اس کا حق دینا ممکن ہے بغیر کسی کمی کے تو اس کی جانب رجوع کیا جائے گا اور اگر ہزار ثلث سے نہ نکلیں تو موصی لہ کو نقد مال کا ثث دیا جائے گا اور جو مقدار قرض کی وصول ہوتی رہے گی اس میں سے ٹکٹ لیتا رہے گا یہاں تک کہ وہ ( موصی لۂ ) ہزار کو وصول کرے اسلئے کہ موصی لہ وارث کا شریک ہے اور موصی لہ کو خاص کر دینے میں نقد مال کے ساتھ ورثہ کے حق میں کمی کرنا ہے اسلئے کہ نقد مال کو قرض پر فضیلت ہے اور اسلئے کہ قرض مطلق حال میں مال نہیں ہے وہ وصول کر لینے کے وقت مال بنتا ہے تو ( موصی لہ اور ورثا کے درمیان ) نظر کا اعتدال اس صورت میں ہے جس کو ہم نے ذکر کیا ہے۔
تشریح زید نے وصیت کی کہ میرے مال میں سے ہزار روپے بکر کو دیدئے جائیں تو وصیت درست ہے۔
لیکن زید نے کچھ مال تو نقد چھوڑا ہے اور کچھ مال وہ ہے جو لوگوں پر قرض ہے تو بکر کو جو ہزار روپے دئیے جائیں گے یہ نقد میں سے دیئے جائیں گے یا قرض میں سے تو اس کا جواب دیا کہ اگر نقد مال اتنا ہو کہ جس کا ثلث ہزار ہوتا ہومثلا تین ہزار یا اس سے زیادہ نقد مال موجود ہے تو بکر کو ہزار روپے اس نقد مال سے دیدئے جائیں گے یہ
را گر نقد مال اتنا نہیں ہے بلکہ کم ہے مثلا کل ہزار روپے نقد میں اور باقی مال لوگوں پر قرض ہے۔
تو بکر کو ہزار کا ثلث تو نقد میں سے دیا جائے گا اور باقی حصہ اس کو قرض میں سے ملے گا جس کی صورت یہ ہوگی کہ جتنا قرض وصول ہوتا جائے اس کی تنہائی بکر کو دیدی جائے یہاں تک کہ اس کا حق پورا ہو جائے یعنی ہزار روپے پورے ہو جائیں۔ طریقہ اختیار کرنے کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ موصی لڈ اور در تاتر کہ میں دونوں شریک ہیں اس کے باوجود اگر نقد مال فقط موصی لیہ کو دے دیا
جائے تو ورثہ کے حق میں کمی کر نالا زم آتا ہے اور کمی اسلئے لازم آئے گی کہ موصی لیہ کو نقد مال مل گیا اور ورثا کو وہ ملا جولوگوں پر قرض ہے حالانکہ نفقد مال قرض سے عمدہ اور افضل ہوتا ہے کیونکہ قرض فی الحال مال نہیں بلکہ وصولیابی کے بعد مال ہوگا، تو موصی لڈ اور ورثا کے درمیان اعتدال اس صورت میں برقرار رہے گا جس کو ہم نے بیان کیا ہے۔
He (al-Quduri) said: Whoever makes a bequest to a man of one thousand dirhams, while he has both ready cash (ayn) and debt (dayn) assets: if the thousand comes out of one-third of the cash, it is given to the legatee, because it is possible to give every right-holder his right without reduction, so one proceeds to that. If it does not come out, then one-third of the cash is given to him, and from every portion of the debt that is collected, he takes one-third of it until the thousand is fully paid, because the legatee is a partner of the heir; and giving him exclusively cash would be a reduction of the heirs' right, because cash has superiority over debt, and because debt is not property in an absolute sense; it only becomes property upon collection. So the equitable consideration is as we have mentioned.
Translation: Al-Quduri said: He who bequeaths one thousand dirhams to someone, and he has cash and debt: if the thousand comes out of one-third of the cash, the thousand is given to the legatee, because it is possible to give everyone his right without deficiency, so this is resorted to. If the thousand does not come out of one-third, then one-third of the cash is given to the legatee, and from every amount of debt that is collected, he takes a third until he receives the full thousand, because the legatee is a partner of the heir, and specifying him with cash alone causes deficiency in the heirs' right, because cash is superior to debt, and because debt is not property in an absolute sense; it only becomes property upon collection. So equity between (legatee and heirs) is as we have described.
Explanation: Zayd bequeathed that one thousand rupees be given to Bakr from his property. The bequest is valid. But Zayd left some cash and some debt owed by people. How should the bequest to Bakr be satisfied—from cash or debt? The answer: If the cash is enough such that its one-third equals one thousand (e.g., cash is three thousand or more), then the thousand is given entirely from cash. If the cash is not enough, e.g., only one thousand cash and the rest is debt, then one-third of the thousand is given from cash, and the remainder from the debt: as debt is collected, its one-third is given to Bakr until his right is fulfilled (one thousand rupees). The reason: the legatee and the heirs are partners. If only cash were given to the legatee, it would prejudice the heirs, because cash is better than debt, as debt is not property currently but becomes property only upon collection. So equity between legatee and heirs is maintained by this method.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from Al-Quduri's matn on how to satisfy a bequest of a fixed sum (1000 dirhams) when the testator's estate consists of both cash ('ayn) and debts (dayn) owed to him. The ruling, which is the relied-upon Hanafi position (mufta bihi), distinguishes two scenarios: (1) If the bequest can be completely paid from one-third of the cash alone (i.e., the cash is at least 3000 dirhams), it is given entirely from cash, because this fulfills the right without harming anyone. (2) If the cash is insufficient (less than 3000 dirhams), the legatee receives one-third of whatever cash exists, and as debts are collected, he receives one-third of each collection until his total reaches 1000. The reasoning is that the legatee and the heirs are partners in the estate. Giving the legatee only cash would unfairly deprive the heirs of the superior quality of cash over debt, since debt is not immediately disposable property. This ruling ensures equitable distribution between the legatee and the heirs.

Key Terms
عين ('ayn): Ready cash or tangible property present in the estate.
دين (dayn): Debts owed to the testator, i.e., receivables.
ثلث (thuluth): One-third of the estate, the maximum fraction that can be bequeathed to non-heirs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a testator leaves 1000 dirhams in cash and 3000 dirhams in debts, and bequeaths 1000 dirhams to a legatee, how should the bequest be paid?
A) Entirely from cash because cash is easier.
B) Entirely from debts because cash is for heirs.
C) One-third from cash (333.33 dirhams) and the rest from debts as collected.
D) 500 dirhams from cash and 500 from debts.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling ensures equity by proportionally distributing the bequest from cash and debt, recognising cash's superiority and the partnership between legatee and heirs.

Wasiyyah — Bequest

8 min
Bequest to a Deceased Person: The Entire Third Goes to the Survivor
Ruling on a bequest to two where one predeceases the testator

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a bequest is made to two persons, one predeceased, and distinguish Abu Hanifa's view from Abu Yusuf's view with its practical consequence.

Core Idea
A dead person cannot own property; a bequest to a deceased legatee is void, and the surviving legatee takes the entire share.

When a testator bequeaths one-third of his estate to two individuals, but one is already dead, a question arises: does the survivor take the whole share or only half? Al-Quduri's matn gives the ruling that the dead person lacks capacity, so the survivor takes all. However, Abu Yusuf introduces a nuance based on the testator's knowledge. This lesson unpacks the ruling and the internal Hanafi debate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and legal issue
The testator bequeaths one-third of his property to Zayd and 'Amr. At the time of the bequest, 'Amr is already dead. The issue is: what share does Zayd receive?
The bequest is made in the present tense, so the legatees must be alive at the moment of the statement.
2
Extract the ruling from the matn (Abu Hanifa's position)
Al-Quduri states: 'The entire third is for Zayd, because the dead person is not eligible for a bequest.' This is the relied-upon position in the school.
The matn is considered authoritative and reflects Abu Hanifa's view.
3
Understand the dalil: lack of capacity (ahliyyah)
A dead person lacks legal capacity to own property. Therefore, the bequest to 'Amr is void ab initio. The testator's intent to give to 'Amr is irrelevant because the recipient is incapable.
The analogy to a wall (which also lacks capacity) reinforces the principle.
4
Examine Abu Yusuf's distinction
Abu Yusuf differentiates based on the testator's knowledge. If the testator was unaware of 'Amr's death, he intended to give half to each, so Zayd gets half. If aware, the bequest to 'Amr is futile, so Zayd gets the whole.
Abu Yusuf's reasoning is based on honoring the testator's presumed intent.
5
Compare the two positions and identify the mufta bihi
The matn and later Hanafi authorities prefer Abu Hanifa's view, making it the operative ruling for fatwa regardless of the testator's knowledge.
The practical difference: under Abu Hanifa, Zayd always gets the full third; under Abu Yusuf, he gets half if the testator was ignorant of the death.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ومن اوصى لزيد و عمر و بثث ماله فاذا عمروميت فالثلث كله لزيد لان الميت ليس باهل للوصية فلا لــحــــى الـــــذى هــــو مـــــن كما اذا اوم می نزید و جدار
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جس نے وصیت کی زید اور عمر د کیلئے اپنے مال کے ثلث کی پس عمرومیت ہے پس ثلث کل کا کل زید کیلئے ہو گا، اسلئے کہ میت وصیت کا اہل نہیں ہے تو میت اس زید کا مزاحم نہ ہوگا جو کہ وصیت کا اہل ہے جیسا کہ جبکہ اس نے وصیت کی وہ زید اور دیوار کیلئے۔
تشریح بکرنے زید اور عمرو دونوں کیلئے اپنے تہائی مال کی وصیت کی لیکن عمر وزندہ نہیں ہے بلکہ وہ وصیت کرنے سے پہلے ہی مر چکا ہے تو پوراثت زید کو ملے گا کیونکہ میت وصیت کا اہل نہیں ہے اور زید چونکہ زندہ ہے اور وصیت کا اہل ہے تو عمر و عدم اہلیت کی وجہ سے زید کا مزائم نہ ہوگا اور اس کو ٹکٹ دیئے جانے سے مانع نہ ہوگا۔
جیسے اگر مہر نے زید اور دیوار کیلئے ثلث مال کی وصیت کی تو پورا ثلث زید کو ملے گا، کیونکہ دیوار میں اہلیت نہیں ہے کہ اس کو بھی دیا جاسکے تو عمر بھی دیوار کے درجہ میں ہے اور دونوں صورتوں میں زید کو پورا ثلث ملے گا۔
امام ابو یوسف کا مذکورہ مسئلہ میں نقطہ نظر
وعن ابى يوسف انه اذا لم يعلم بموته فله نصف الثلث لأن الوصية عنده صحيحة لعمر وفلم يرض للحي الانصف الثلث بخلاف ما اذا علم بموته لان الوصية للميت لغو فكان راضيا بكل الثلث للحي ترجمہ اور ابو یوسف سے منقول ہے کہ جب موسی عمرو کی موت سے واقف نہ ہو تو زید کیلئے ٹکٹ کا نصف ہے اسلئے کہ موصی کے نزدیک (اس کے گمان میں ) عمرہ کیلئے وصیت صحیح ہے تو وہ راضی نہیں زندہ کیلئے مگر ٹکٹ کے نصف سے بخلاف اس صورت کے جبکہ وہ اس کی موت سے واقف ہو اسلئے کہ میت کیلئے وصیت کرنا لغو ہے تو وہ پورے ثلث سے زندہ کے حق میں راضی ہو گیا۔ تشریح ماقبل والے مسئلہ کی امام ابو یوسف نے یہ تفصیل بیان فرمائی ہے کہ اگر موسی کو معلوم ہے کہ عمر وزندہ ہے حالانکہ وہ مر چکا ہے تو موسی اپنے گمان میں زید کو صرف ثالث کا نصف دے رہا ہے لہذا ثلث کا نصف ہی زید کو ملے گا۔ اور اگر موسی کو معلوم ہے کہ عمر و مر چکا ہے پھر بھی وہ ان الفاظ میں وصیت کر رہا ہے تو عمرہ کیلئے وصیت کرنا سراسر لغو ہے اور اس صورت میں پورانہ زید کو ملے گا۔
He said: Whoever makes a bequest to Zayd and 'Amr of one-third of his property, and 'Amr is dead, then the entire third is for Zayd, because the dead person is not eligible for bequest, so he does not compete with the living one who is eligible, just as if he made a bequest to Zayd and a wall.
Translation: Al-Quduri said: He who bequeaths to Zayd and 'Amr one-third of his property, and 'Amr is dead, then the entire third belongs to Zayd, because the dead is not eligible for bequest, so the dead does not compete with Zayd who is eligible, just as if he made a bequest to Zayd and a wall.
Explanation: Bakr made a bequest of one-third of his property to both Zayd and 'Amr, but 'Amr is not alive; he died before the bequest. Then the entire third goes to Zayd, because the dead is not eligible for bequest, and Zayd is alive and eligible, so 'Amr, due to lack of eligibility, does not compete with Zayd and does not prevent giving the portion to him.
Just as if someone bequeathed one-third to Zayd and a wall, the entire third goes to Zayd, because the wall lacks capacity to receive. 'Amr is like the wall; in both cases Zayd gets the whole third.
Imam Abu Yusuf's view on this issue:
And from Abu Yusuf: If he (the testator) was unaware of his ('Amr's) death, then for Zayd is half of the third, because according to him (the testator's assumption) the bequest to 'Amr is valid, and he was not pleased to give the living only half of the third; unlike when he knew of his death, because the bequest for the dead is futile, so he was pleased with the entire third for the living.
Translation: And it is narrated from Abu Yusuf that when the testator is not aware of 'Amr's death, then Zayd gets half of the third, because in the testator's estimation the bequest to 'Amr is valid, so he was not pleased for the living (Zayd) to receive more than half of the third; unlike when he is aware of 'Amr's death, because the bequest for the dead is futile, so he was pleased with the entire third for the living.
Explanation: Imam Abu Yusuf explains the previous issue with this detail: If the testator thinks 'Amr is alive when he is actually dead, then in his assumption he is giving only half of the third to Zayd, so Zayd receives half. If the testator knows 'Amr is dead but still makes the bequest in those words, then the bequest to 'Amr is entirely futile, and in that case Zayd receives the entire third.
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage addresses a situation where a testator bequeaths one-third of his estate to two individuals, Zayd and 'Amr, but 'Amr is already deceased at the time of the bequest. The main ruling from Al-Quduri (based on Abu Hanifa's view) is that the entire third goes to Zayd alone, because a dead person is not legally capable of receiving a bequest. 'Amr is like a wall—incapable—so he does not compete with Zayd. The commentator then presents a differing view from Imam Abu Yusuf, who distinguishes based on the testator's knowledge: if the testator was unaware of 'Amr's death and thought he was alive, then the bequest was intended to be shared, so Zayd receives only half of the third (as the testator's intent is honored). If the testator knew 'Amr was dead, then the bequest to 'Amr is void, and Zayd gets the entire third. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Hanifa (and the matn) that Zayd gets the full third regardless of the testator's knowledge, because the dead person's incapacity is objective, not dependent on the testator's awareness.

Key Terms
وصية (wasiyyah): A bequest or testamentary disposition of property.
أهلية (ahliyyah): Legal capacity; the ability to own property. A dead person lacks this.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a testator bequeaths one-third of his estate to Zayd and 'Amr, but 'Amr died before the testator made the will, what is the Hanafi ruling according to the matn (Abu Hanifa)?
A) The bequest is invalid entirely because the condition is not met.
B) Zayd receives half of the third, and the other half goes to 'Amr's heirs.
C) Zayd receives the entire third.
D) The third is divided among the legal heirs.

Key Takeaway
When a legatee predeceases the testator, the bequest to him is void, and the surviving legatee receives the entire share, per the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Bequest to Two Persons, One Predeceased
Ruling on a bequest to two when one is already dead

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a legatee predeceases the testator, distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and apply the rule that a dead legatee does not compete.

Core Idea
A dead legatee cannot receive; the entire bequest goes to the surviving co-legatee.

When a testator bequeaths a portion of his wealth to two named individuals, and one of them has already died, questions arise about how the share should be distributed. This passage from Al-Quduri addresses this scenario, presenting the primary Hanafi ruling that the entire third passes to the living legatee. However, Imam Abu Yusuf offers a nuanced view depending on the testator's knowledge. Understanding this dispute sharpens our ability to apply the principles of eligibility (ahliyyah) and intention in Islamic inheritance law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case and the ruling
Recognize that the testator bequeaths one-third of his property to Zayd and Amr. Amr is dead at the time of the will (or before the testator's death). The ruling in the primary text: the entire third goes to Zayd.
The source uses the analogy of bequeathing to Zayd and a wall.
2
Understand the legal reasoning (ta'lil)
The dead person (Amr) is not eligible (ahliyyah) to receive a bequest. Therefore, he does not compete (yuzahim) with the eligible living legatee (Zayd). The share is not split; the entire third becomes Zayd's.
Eligibility is the key condition for receiving a will.
3
Note Abu Yusuf's position
Imam Abu Yusuf distinguishes two scenarios: if the testator knew of Amr's death, the will for Amr is void (laghw) and Zayd gets the whole third. If the testator did not know, then the testator's intention was to give half to each, so Zayd only gets half of the third (one-sixth of the estate).
Abu Yusuf considers the testator's assumed intention based on knowledge.
4
Determine the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa: Zayd receives the entire third regardless of the testator's knowledge. This is the position in zahir al-riwayah and followed by later Hanafi authorities like al-Marghinani.
Tarjih is based on the principle that a dead legatee is never eligible.
5
Apply the rule to analogous cases
If the testator bequeaths to a person and an inanimate object (like a wall), the object cannot receive, so the entire share goes to the person. Similarly, a dead legatee is treated as legally non-existent.
This analogy reinforces the principle of eligibility.

He said: Whoever bequeaths one-third of his property to Zayd and Amr, and Amr is dead, then the entire third is for Zayd, because the dead person is not eligible for a will, so he does not compete with the one who is eligible, just as if he bequeathed to Zayd and a wall. Commentary: [Detailed explanation in Urdu] And from Abu Yusuf: when he (the testator) does not know of his (Amr's) death, then he (Zayd) gets half of the third, because in his estimation the will is valid for Amr, so he is not satisfied for the living person except with half of the third. Contrary to the case when he knows of his death, because making a will for a dead person is meaningless, so he is satisfied with the entire third for the living.
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage states a ruling from Al-Quduri: if a testator bequeaths one-third of his property to Zayd and Amr, but Amr had already died before the will (or before the testator's death), the entire one-third goes to Zayd. The reason is that a dead person is not a valid recipient of a will; thus, Amr does not 'compete' (yuzahim) with Zayd, who is eligible. The author gives an analogy: if one bequeaths to Zayd and a wall, the entire third goes to Zayd, as a wall cannot own property. Then Imam Abu Yusuf is reported to have a detailed view: if the testator was unaware of Amr's death (i.e., he thought Amr was alive when making the will), then Zayd only receives half of the one-third, because the testator's intention was to give half to each, but since Amr is dead, only the share intended for a living person remains; if the testator knew of the death, the will for Amr is void from the start, and the testator's intention would be to give the whole to Zayd. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the ruling of Abu Hanifa (full third to Zayd) regardless of knowledge, as reflected in the primary text.

Key Terms
موصى له (mūṣā lahu): The person for whom a bequest is made (legatee).
مزاحم (muzāḥim): One who competes or contests for a share; here, a dead legatee does not 'compete' with a living one.
أهلية (ahliyyah): Legal capacity or eligibility. Here, the capacity to receive a bequest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Yusuf, what is the ruling if a testator bequeaths one-third to Zayd and Amr, and Amr is dead, but the testator was unaware of Amr's death?
A) Zayd receives the entire one-third
B) Zayd receives half of the one-third (one-sixth of the estate)
C) The bequest is void because Amr is dead
D) Zayd receives nothing because the testator's intention was incomplete

Key Takeaway
A dead legatee is ineligible to receive a bequest, so the entire bequeathed share passes to the surviving co-legatee, a principle upheld by the Hanafi school regardless of the testator's knowledge.

Bequest Using 'Bayna' with a Dead Legatee
Ruling on bequest wording with 'bayna' and deceased legatee

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a bequest uses 'bayna' (between) and one legatee is dead, and distinguish it from the ruling using 'li' (for).

Core Idea
When the testator says 'between', the dead legatee's share lapses; the survivor does not take the whole third.

In Hanafi wasiyyah, the wording of a bequest matters. The word 'bayna' (between) implies equal division among the named recipients. This lesson examines what happens when one of those recipients dies before the testator, and why the survivor does not automatically get the entire bequest.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Key Wording
Determine whether the testator used 'bayna' (between) or 'li' (for). In this case, 'bayna' indicates distribution.
2
Understand the Implication of 'Bayna'
In Hanafi fiqh, 'bayna' implies that each named person receives an equal share of the bequeathed portion.
Contrast with 'li', which gives the entire portion to the named person.
3
Apply to the Scenario
If one legatee (Zayd) is dead, his share lapses. The surviving legatee (Amr) only receives his own share—half of the bequeathed third.
The dead legatee's share does not transfer to the survivor.
4
Contrast with 'Li' Wording
If the testator had used 'li' (e.g., 'one-third for Zayd'), and Zayd is dead, the bequest would be void and the third reverts to the heirs. But if the testator says 'one-third for Zayd and Amr', the survivor takes all.
The key is that 'bayna' fixes separate shares, whereas 'li' can imply joint ownership or a single gift.
5
State the Ruling
When 'bayna' is used and one legatee predeceases, the surviving legatee receives half of the designated third (i.e., one-sixth of the estate).
This ruling is consistent across the Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
