And if he said: 'One-third of my property is between Zayd and Amr and Zayd is dead' then Amr receives half of the third, because the implication of these words is that each of them would have half of the third, contrary to the previous case. Don't you see that if someone says: 'One-third of my property is for Zayd' and remains silent, then Zayd gets the whole third. And if he said: 'One-third of my property is between so-and-so' and remained silent, then so-and-so does not become entitled to the third. Commentary: [Detailed explanation in Urdu]
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage differentiates between two types of wording in bequests. When the testator says 'One-third of my property is between Zayd and Amr' using the word 'bayna' (between), the implication is that each gets half. So if one of them (Zayd) is dead, the surviving legatee Amr receives only half of the one-third (one-sixth of the estate), not the entire third. This contrasts with the earlier ruling (using 'li' or explicit naming) where the full third goes to the surviving legatee. The reason is that 'bayna' suggests division into shares, so the dead person's share lapses and does not transfer to the other. The author gives examples: if one says 'one-third for Zayd', Zayd gets the whole; but if one says 'one-third between so-and-so' without naming, the named person does not get the whole because the word 'between' implies at least two recipients.

Key Terms
بين (bayna): A word meaning 'between', used to indicate distribution among multiple recipients equally unless specified otherwise.

B) Half of the one-third
C) Nothing
D) One-sixth of the estate

Key Takeaway
In a bequest using 'bayna', each legatee receives an equal share; if one predeceases, that share lapses and does not transfer to the surviving legatee(s).

Bequest of One-Third When Testator Has No Property
Ruling on bequest when testator initially has no property

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a bequest of one-third attaches to property owned at death, even if the testator had no property when making the will, and explain the reasoning that a will is a suspended contract.

Core Idea
A will is a suspended contract; property condition matters at death, not at the will's making.

This passage from Al-Quduri clarifies a critical scenario: if someone bequeaths one-third of his property while owning nothing, then later acquires wealth and dies, the legatee still receives one-third of the estate at death. The ruling hinges on the nature of a will as a contract of succession suspended until after death. Understanding this principle prevents common errors about when property must exist for a bequest to be valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling
Read the passage and identify: the testator made a will for one-third of his property, but had no property at that time. Later he acquires property and dies. The ruling is that the legatee gets one-third of whatever the testator owns at death, not at the time of the will.
2
Trace the legal reasoning (ta'lil)
The author explains that a will is a contract of succession (عقد استخلاف) that is suspended (مضاف) until after death. Therefore, its legal effect only occurs after death. This determines that the relevant point for property ownership is the moment of death.
3
Derive the condition from the reasoning
From the ta'lil, we derive that existence of property at death is a condition for the will to take effect; property at the time of the will is irrelevant. This is the direct conclusion.
4
Extend to the analogous case
The passage adds that if the testator had property at the time of the will but it perished, then later he acquired new property, the same ruling applies: the bequest applies to the new property at death. This confirms the principle.
5
Consolidate the rule and its implication
The rule is that a will is valid and applies to property acquired after the will, as long as property exists at death. This ensures that the bequest is not voided by the testator's change in financial status after making the will.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ومن اوصى بثلث ماله ولا مال له واكتسب مالا استحق الموصى له ثلث ما يملكه عند الموت لان الوصية عقد استخلاف مضاف الى ما بعد الموت ويثبت حكمه بعده فيشترط وجود المال عند الموت لا قبله و کذلک اذا كان له مال فهلك ثم اكتسب مالا لما بينا ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جس نے اپنے مال کے ثلث کی وصیت کی اور اس کیلئے مال نہیں ہے اور موصی نے مال کما لیا ہو تو موصی لہ اس مال کے ثالث کا مالک ہو گا کہ موصی بوقت موت جس کا مالک تھا اسلئے کہ وصیت خلیفہ بنانے کا ایک عقد ہے جو مابعد الموت کی جانب مضاف ہے اور عقد وضیت کا حکم موت کے بعد ثابت ہو گا تو موت کے وقت مال کا وجود شرط ہے نہ کہ اس سے پہلے اور ایسے ہی جبکہ اس
He said: Whoever bequeaths one-third of his property and he has no property, then he acquires property, the legatee becomes entitled to one-third of what he owns at death, because a will is a contract of succession attached to after death, and its ruling is established after death. Therefore, the existence of property at the time of death is a condition, not before. Likewise, if he had property and it perished, then he acquired property, for the same reason.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from Al-Quduri: if a person makes a will bequeathing one-third of his property but at that time he had no property (and then later acquires property before death), the bequest applies to one-third of whatever he owns at the moment of death. The reasoning (ta'lil) is that a will is a 'contract of succession' (عقد استخلاف) that is suspended (muḍāf) until after death; its legal effect occurs only after death. Therefore, what matters is the property existing at death, not at the time of the will. Similarly, if the testator had property at the time of the will but it was subsequently lost, then he acquired new property, the bequest applies to the new property at death. The condition is that property must exist at death.

Key Terms
عقد استخلاف (ʿaqd istikhlāf): A contract of succession or appointment of a successor; used to describe a will where the legatee takes the testator's place in ownership after death.
مضاف (muḍāf): Suspended or attached to a future time; here, the will is attached to 'after death'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Nothing, because the will was invalid
B) One-third of what he earned only
C) One-third of whatever he owns at death
D) One-third of the entire estate, including any debts

Key Takeaway
A will is a suspended contract; the condition for its application is property at death, not at the time of the will.

Ruling on Wasiyyah Using 'Bayn' When One Beneficiary Is Dead
Explains the effect of the word 'bayn' in bequests

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the effect of the word 'bayn' in a bequest when one beneficiary is dead, and distinguish it from the word 'li'.

Core Idea
When 'bayn' is used in a will, it implies equal shares; if one beneficiary is dead, the survivor takes only that half.

In this lesson, we examine a specific ruling regarding the wording of a bequest. The testator uses the word 'bayn' (between) to divide a third of his wealth between two persons, but one is already dead. The Hanafi school clarifies that the surviving beneficiary receives only half of that third, because 'bayn' inherently implies equal distribution. We will also compare this with the word 'li' (for) to see how the choice of words changes the outcome.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the testator's statement: 'thuluth mali bayna Zayd wa Amr' with Zayd dead. The ruling: Amr gets half of the third (one-sixth of the total estate).
The bequest is valid (sahih) only to the extent of Amr's share.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the linguistic implication (dalalah al-lafz) of 'bayn': it means equal division between the named parties. The author says 'because the import of this wording is that each of them would have half of the third.'
No external textual evidence is cited; the proof is the word's inherent meaning.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The word 'bayn' necessitates distribution among at least two parties, implying equal shares by default. Here, Zayd is dead, so only Amr's intended half remains; the other half lapses back to the estate.
This contrasts with 'li' (for), which grants full ownership to the named beneficiary.
4
Apply to analogous cases
The text contrasts two cases: (a) 'thuluth mali li Zayd' gives Zayd the entire third. (b) 'thuluth mali bayna fulan' (only one named) yields no entitlement because 'bayn' requires two parties.
These contrasts highlight the distributive nature of 'bayn'.
5
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools may interpret 'bayn' differently, but the Hanafi position is clear: equal division unless context dictates otherwise. The practical consequence is that the survivor does not automatically receive the deceased beneficiary's share.
The cross-madhhab status is mukhtalaf fih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان قال ثلث مالی بین زید و عمر ووزيد ميت كان لعمر ونصف الثلث لان قضية هذا اللفظ أن يكون لكل واحد منهما نصف الثلث بخلاف ما تقدم الاترى ان من قال ثلث مالى لزيد و سكت كان له كل الثلث ولو قال ثلث مالی بین فلان وسكت لم يستحق الثلث
And if he said, 'A third of my wealth is between Zayd and Amr,' and Zayd is dead, then Amr has half of the third, because the import of this wording is that each of them would have half of the third, unlike what preceded. Do you not see that whoever said, 'A third of my wealth is for Zayd' and was silent, then Zayd has the entire third; and if he said, 'A third of my wealth is between so-and-so' and was silent, then he does not deserve the third.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, explaining the legal effect of the word 'bayn' (between) in a will. The testator says 'my third is between Zayd and Amr' but Zayd is already dead. Since 'bayn' implies equal sharing, the testator intended each to get half of the third. Therefore, the surviving beneficiary Amr gets that half (i.e., half of the third, or one-sixth of the total estate). The text contrasts two cases to illustrate the unique import of 'bayn': (1) If the testator says 'my third is for Zayd' and stops, Zayd gets the entire third because the word 'li' indicates full ownership. (2) If he says 'my third is between so-and-so' (naming only one person) and stops, the bequest is void because 'bayn' requires at least two parties; without a second party, the word is incomplete and the bequest fails. Thus, 'bayn' carries a distributive meaning that is absent in 'li'.

Key Terms
بين (bayn): In this context, 'bayn' indicates distribution between two or more parties, implying equal shares.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a testator says 'thuluth mali bayna Zayd wa Amr' and Zayd is dead at the time of the will, what does Amr receive?
A) The entire third
B) Half of the third
C) Nothing, the bequest is void
D) The entire estate

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi wasiyyah, the word 'bayn' mandates equal division; death of one beneficiary does not transfer that share to the survivor.

Wasiyyah — Bequest

6 min
Validity of Bequest When Testator Has No Wealth at Time of Will
Clarifies that bequest depends on wealth at death, not at will-making

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a bequest is valid based on wealth at death, not at the time of the will, and explain the ta'lil (legal reasoning) behind it.

Core Idea
A bequest is contingent on death, so the existence of wealth at death is the only condition.

This passage addresses a key scenario: if a testator makes a bequest while owning nothing, does the bequest become invalid? The Hanafi school rules that it remains valid if the testator later acquires wealth before death. The reasoning is that a bequest (wasiyyah) is a contract attached to after death, so only death triggers the obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The testator bequeaths one-third of his wealth but owns nothing at that moment. Later, he acquires wealth and dies.
Note that the testator may have had no property at the time of the will.
2
State the ruling
The beneficiary is entitled to one-third of the wealth existing at the testator's death.
The ruling is clear: the bequest applies to wealth at death, not at will-making.
3
Analyze the proof (ta'lil)
The reason is that a bequest is a contract of deputyship (aqd istikhlaf) attached to after death. Its ruling is established after death, so the condition is wealth at death.
This is a ta'lil: the ruling is derived from the nature of the contract.
4
Apply to the variant case
If the testator had wealth that perished and then acquired new wealth, the same ruling applies: the bequest attaches to the new wealth at death.
The principle is consistent: existence at death is the determinant.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ومن اوصى بثلث ماله ولا مال له واكتسب مالا استحق الموصى له ثلث ما يملكه عند الموت لان الوصية عقد استخلاف مضاف الى ما بعد الموت ويثبت حكمه بعده فيشترط وجود المال عند الموت لا قبله و کذلک اذا كان له مال فهلك ثم اكتسب مالا لما بينا
He said: And whoever bequeaths a third of his wealth and he has no wealth, then he acquires wealth, the beneficiary is entitled to a third of what he owns at death, because the will is a contract of deputyship attached to after death, and its ruling is established after it, so the existence of wealth at death is a condition, not before it. Similarly, if he had wealth and it perished, then he acquired wealth, [the same applies] due to what we have explained.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, addressing a scenario where the testator makes a bequest of one-third of his wealth but owns nothing at that moment. Later, he acquires wealth and dies owning it. The beneficiary still takes one-third of the wealth existing at death. The reason is that the bequest is a contract (wasiyyah) that is contingent on death; it only becomes operative after death. Therefore, what matters is the existence of the subject matter at death, not at the time of the will. The same applies if the testator had wealth that was destroyed and then he acquired new wealth before death: the bequest applies to the new wealth. This is because the requirement is the availability of wealth at death. The commentary emphasizes that the bequest is like appointing someone as a successor after death, so only death triggers the obligation.

Key Terms
عقد استخلاف (aqd istikhlaf): A contract of deputyship where the testator appoints the beneficiary as a successor to take property after death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when must wealth exist for a bequest of one-third to be valid?
A) At the time the will is made.
B) At the time of the testator's death.
C) At both the time of the will and death.
D) Only if the testator continuously had wealth from will to death.

Key Takeaway
A bequest is valid if wealth exists at the testator's death, regardless of its absence at the time of the will, because the bequest is a contract attached to after death.

Bequest of One-Third of Sheep: Existence at Death Determines Validity
Ruling on bequest of one-third of sheep when sheep perish or are acquired later

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a bequest of a specified item (ayn) and apply the principle that existence at death determines validity.

Core Idea
For a bequest of a specific item, its existence at the testator's death is decisive; existence at the time of the will is irrelevant.

This lesson examines a key principle in Hanafi bequest law: the critical moment for a bequest of a specified item is the testator's death, not the time the will is made. Using the example of a bequest of one-third of sheep, we will see how this principle operates and the reasoning behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is a bequest (wasiyyah) of one-third of the testator's sheep. The ruling depends on whether the sheep exist at the time of death.
The bequest is valid (sahih) if the sheep exist at death, void (batil) otherwise.
2
Understand the principle: ijab ba'd al-mawt
A bequest is an obligation that takes effect after death. Therefore, the condition for its validity is checked at the moment it becomes binding – i.e., at death.
This distinguishes bequest from a gift, which takes effect immediately.
3
Apply the principle to two scenarios
Scenario 1: Sheep existed at will-making but perished before death → void. Scenario 2: No sheep at will-making but acquired and owned at death → valid.
The key is existence at death, not at the time of the will.
4
Extend the reasoning to a general analogy
The passage extends the same rule to a bequest of wealth (mal): if it is valid for wealth, it is also valid for a specific type (like sheep), because the principle is the same.
The existence of the type before death is surplus; only death matters.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو اوصى له بثلث غنمه فهلک الغنم قبل موته اولم يكن له غنم فى الاصل فالوصية باطلة لما ذكرنا انه ايجاب بعد الموت فيعتبر قيامه حينئذ وهذه الوصية تعلقت بالعين فتبطل بفواتها عند الموت وان لم يكن له غنم فاستفاده ثم مات فالصحيح ان الوصية تصح لأنها لو كانت بلفظ المال تصح فكذا اذا كانت باسم نوعه وهذا لان وجوده قبل الموت فضل والمعتبر قيامه عند الموت
If he bequeaths to him one-third of his sheep, and the sheep perish before his death, or he had no sheep at all, then the bequest is void, because of what we mentioned: that it is an obligation after death, so its existence at that time is considered. And this bequest is attached to a specific thing (ayn), so it becomes void by its loss at the time of death. And if he had no sheep, then he acquired them and then died, the correct view is that the bequest is valid, because if it were in the wording of 'wealth' it would be valid, so likewise if it is in the name of its type. And this is because its existence before death is surplus, and what is considered is its existence at the time of death.
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school on bequests of specific types of property, such as sheep. The passage establishes a key principle: for a bequest of a specified item (ayn) to be valid, the item must exist at the moment of the testator's death. It does not need to exist at the time the will is made. This is because a bequest is legally an obligation that takes effect after death (ijab ba'd al-mawt). Therefore, the relevant moment for checking the existence of the bequeathed property is the time of death. If the testator had no sheep at the time of making the will but later acquired them and still owns them at death, the bequest of one-third of those sheep is valid. However, if the sheep existed at the time of the will but perished before death and were not replaced, the bequest becomes void. The reasoning is extended: if the bequest had been worded generally as 'wealth' (mal), it would be valid as long as there is any wealth at death. Similarly, if it specifies a type of wealth (like sheep), the same logic applies, because the type is just a specification. The existence of the type before death is not required; only its existence at death matters.

Key Terms
ثلث (thuluth): One-third; the maximum fraction of estate that can be bequeathed to non-heirs without heir consent.
عين (ayn): A specific, identifiable item of property, as opposed to undefined wealth.
ايجاب بعد الموت (ijab ba'd al-mawt): An obligation that becomes effective after the testator's death; the defining characteristic of a bequest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man bequeaths one-third of his sheep but owns no sheep at the time of the will. Later he acquires sheep and dies owning them. According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling?
A) The bequest is void because the sheep did not exist at the time of the will.
B) The bequest is valid because the sheep exist at the time of death.
C) The bequest is void because it was not added to wealth (mal).
D) The bequest is valid only if he explicitly mentioned 'from my wealth'.

Key Takeaway
The validity of a bequest of a specified item hinges on its existence at the testator's death, not at the time of the will.

Bequest of 'a Sheep from My Wealth' When No Sheep Owned
Ruling on bequest of 'a sheep from my wealth' when testator owns no sheep

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a bequest of 'a sheep from my wealth' is valid even without sheep ownership, and apply the Hanafi principle of interpreting bequest intent via attachment to wealth.

Core Idea
When a bequest is attached to 'my wealth', the beneficiary receives the value, not the specific item.

This passage addresses a common scenario in bequests: the testator specifies an item he does not own. The Hanafi school does not automatically void the bequest; instead, it looks at the wording to infer intent. The key phrase 'from my wealth' changes the interpretation: the testator intended to bequeath the monetary value, which exists in any wealth.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the issue
The act is a bequest (wasiyyah) of 'a sheep from my wealth' while the testator owns no sheep. The issue is whether the bequest is void or valid.
2
Locate the key wording
The crucial phrase is 'from my wealth' (min mālī). The Hanafi school uses this to infer the testator's intent.
3
Understand the reasoning (talil)
Because the bequest is attached to the general wealth, the testator's intent is the monetary value (māliyya) of the sheep, which can be found in any wealth.
4
See the practical application
The beneficiary receives the market value of a sheep from the estate, not a specific animal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو قال له شاة من مالى وليس له غنم يعطى قيمة شاة لانه لما اضافه الى المال علمنا ان مراده الوصية بمالية الشاة اذ ماليتها توجد في مطلق المال
And if he says, 'He has a sheep from my wealth', and he has no sheep, he is given the value of a sheep, because when he added it to wealth, we know that his intent is the bequest of the monetary value of the sheep, since its monetary value is found in absolute wealth.
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This is a ruling on the interpretation of ambiguous bequest wording. When the testator says 'a sheep from my wealth' (shātun min mālī) but owns no sheep at the time of death, the Hanafi school rules that the bequest does not become void. Instead, the beneficiary is entitled to the market value of a sheep. The reasoning is that by adding 'from my wealth' (min mālī), the testator indicates that his intention is to bequeath the monetary value (māliyya) of the sheep, not the specific animal itself. The monetary value of a sheep can be found in any type of wealth, so it can be fulfilled from the general estate. This ruling shows the principle that when a bequest is attached to a specific thing but expressed in a way that connects it to the estate broadly, the court gives effect to the apparent intention by providing the value instead.

Key Terms
اضافة الى المال (idafa ila al-mal): Attaching the bequest to the testator's general wealth, e.g., saying 'from my wealth'.
مالية (maliyya): Monetary value; the worth of an item in terms of currency.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A testator says, 'I give a sheep from my wealth to Zaid,' but owns no sheep at death. What does Zaid receive according to the Hanafi school?
A) Nothing, because the bequest is void.
B) A sheep if the estate buys one.
C) The market value of a sheep.
D) One-third of the estate.

Key Takeaway
When a bequest is phrased as 'from my wealth', the testator's intent is the value, so the beneficiary receives the value even if the specific item is not owned.

Bequest of a Sheep from Property: Value Given When Item Absent
Ruling that the legatee receives the value of the sheep

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a bequest of a specific item added to 'property' when the item does not exist, and explain the reasoning based on the testator's wording.

Core Idea
A bequest of 'a sheep from my property' pays its value, not the sheep itself, because the phrase shifts intent to monetary value.

What happens when someone bequeaths a specific item they don't own? The Hidayah presents a case: a testator says 'a sheep from my property' but has no sheep. The Hanafi school rules that the legatee receives the value of a sheep. This lesson unpacks the reasoning (talil) that the addition 'from my property' transforms the bequest from a specific animal to its monetary value, which exists in any property. Understanding this highlights how Hanafi jurists interpret testators' probable intent through linguistic clues.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
Recognize that the act is a bequest (wasiyyah) of a specific item ('a sheep') with the phrase 'from my property'. The ruling: the legatee receives the value (qimah) of a sheep, not the animal itself.
The bequest is valid (sahih) despite the absence of the specific item.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is the testator's wording: 'from my property' (من مالى). The text uses talil (reasoning) to derive the rule, not a direct Quranic or Hadith citation.
The proof is linguistic: the addition (idaafa) to 'property' signals a different intent.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (indication of meaning)
The phrase 'from my property' attaches the bequest to the estate as a whole. Since the testator owns no sheep, the word 'sheep' cannot refer to a specific animal; rather, it refers to the monetary value (malia) of a sheep, which exists in any property.
Monetary value is an abstract quality that can be satisfied from any asset.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (scholarly difference)
Other schools might void the bequest because the specified item does not exist. The Hanafi school validates it by interpreting the testator's intent as the value.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf based on different approaches to interpreting ambiguous bequests.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that the legatee receives the value. This is consistent with the principle of honoring the testator's probable intent.
The ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو قال له شاة من مالى وليس له غنم يعطى قيمة شاة لانه لما اضافه الى المال علمنا ان مراده الوصية بمالية الشاة اذ ماليتها توجد في مطلق المال ترجمہ اور اگر موصی نے کہا کہ موصی لہ کیلئے میرے مال میں سے ایک بکری ہے حالانکہ اس کے پاس بکری نہیں ہے تو موصی لہ کو ایک بکری کی قیمت دی جائے گی اسلئے کہ جب موصی نے شاہ کی اضافت مال کی طرف کر دی تو ہمیں یہ بات معلوم ہوگئی کہ موصی کی مراد بکری کی مالیت کی وصیت کرنا ہے اسلئے کہ بکری کی مالیت مطلق مال میں پائی جاتی ہے۔ تشریح اگر موصی کے پاس بکریاں تو نہ ہوں لیکن اس نے یہ الفاظ استعمال کیئے کہ میرے مال میں سے ایک بکری فلاں کی ہے تو اس کا مقصد یہ ہے کہ میرے مال میں سے اتنا مال اس کو دیا جائے جو ایک بکری کی مالیت ہو اور بکری کی مالیت کا اندازہ ہر حال میں ہوسکتا ہے لہذا موصی لہ کو بکری کی قیمت دی جائے گی۔ لفظ شاہ کی اضافت مالی کی طرف اس کی نشاندہی کرتا ہے۔
And if he said, 'A sheep from my property for him,' and he has no sheep, he is given the value of a sheep, because when he added it to the property, we knew that his intent was the bequest of the monetary value of the sheep, since its monetary value is found in absolute property. Translation: And if the testator said, 'There is a sheep from my property for the legatee,' while he has no sheep, then the legatee will be given the value of a sheep. Because when the testator added 'sheep' to 'property', we understood that the testator's intent was to bequeath the monetary value of the sheep, since the monetary value of a sheep is found in any property. Explanation: If the testator has no sheep but used these words: 'A sheep from my property belongs to so-and-so,' then his purpose is to give him an amount from his property equivalent to the value of a sheep. And the value of a sheep can be estimated in all circumstances. Therefore the legatee will be given the value of a sheep. The addition of the word 'sheep' to 'property' indicates this.
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof from the Hidayah commentary. It addresses the case where a testator bequeaths 'a sheep from my property' but owns no sheep. According to the Hanafi school, the bequest is valid and the legatee receives the monetary value of a sheep. The proof is that the addition of the bequest to 'property' (al-idaafa ila al-maal) signals that the testator's intent is the monetary value (malia), not the specific animal. Since monetary value exists in all types of property, the value can be taken from the estate. This ruling is based on the principle that a testator's words are interpreted according to his probable intent. The Urdu commentary further clarifies that 'from my property' indicates the purpose is to give an amount equal to the value of a sheep.

Key Terms
شاة (shāt): A sheep, used as an example of a bequest item.
قيمة (qīmah): Monetary value or compensation.
مالية (māliyyah): Monetary value as an abstract quality.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Nothing
B) A sheep at a later date
C) The value of a sheep
D) One-third of the estate

Key Takeaway
When a bequest is phrased as 'a specific item from my property' and the item does not exist, the legatee receives the monetary value of that item, as the addition to property signals intent for value.

Bequest of a Non-Owned Sheep: Two Hanafi Views
Intra-Hanafi dispute on interpreting a bequest without property addition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi opinions on the validity of a bequest of a sheep without property addition and apply the preferred view based on intent indicators.

Core Idea
A bequest of a non-owned item can be valid if the testator's mention indicates intent for its value.

In this passage, the Hanafi school presents an internal disagreement: a testator bequeaths a sheep without adding it to his property, and he owns no sheep. Is the bequest valid? The discussion turns on whether the word 'sheep' is taken literally (specific animal) or as indicating the item's monetary value. This lesson unpacks both positions and explains why the preferred view accepts the bequest as valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed scenario
The testator says 'I bequeath a sheep to so-and-so' without saying 'from my property', and he owns no sheep. Do we treat this as a bequest of a specific sheep (which doesn't exist) or as a bequest of its value?
The absence of ownership is key.
2
State the first opinion (invalidity)
One opinion holds the bequest invalid because the 'corrector' (musahhih) is the addition to property; without it, the bequest refers to the actual sheep (form and meaning), which is impossible.
This view emphasizes the literal wording.
3
State the second opinion (validity)
The other opinion holds the bequest valid because the testator's mention of a sheep while owning none shows he intended the monetary value (māliyyah), not the specific animal.
This view gives weight to contextual inference.
4
Locate the tarjih (preferred view)
The Urdu commentary states that the valid view is correct: the bequest is valid and the legatee receives the sheep's value.
This is the muftā bihī for practice.
5
Apply the preferred view
In a similar case (e.g., bequest of a cow when no cow is owned), the bequest is valid and the legatee gets the current market value.
The principle extends to any non-owned bequeathed item.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو اوصى بشاة ولم يضفه الى ماله ولا غنم له قيل لا يصح لان المصحح اضافته الى المال وبدونها تعتبر صورة الشاة و معناها وقيل تصح لانه لما ذكر الشاة و ليس في ملكه شاة علم ان مراده المالية ترجمہ اور اگر اس نے بکری کی وصیت کی اور اس کی اپنے مال کی طرف اضافت نہیں کی اور نہ اس کے پاس بکری ہے تو کہا گیا ہے کہ وصیت صحیح نہ ہوگی اسلئے کہ صحیح کرنے والی چیز شاہ کی مال کی طرف اضافت ہے اور بغیر اضافت کے شاہ کی صورت اور اس کے معنی کا اعتبار کیا جائے گا اور کہا گیا ہے کہ وصیت صحیح ہے اسلئے کہ جب موصی نے شاہ کا ذکر کیا ہے اور اس کی ملکیت میں شاہ نہیں ہے تو یہ بات معلوم ہوگئی کہ اس کی مراد مالیت ہے۔ تشریح اگر موصی نے فقط یوں کہا کہ بکر کیلئے ایک بکری کی وصیت ہے اور یہ نہیں کہا کہ میرے مال میں سے ایک بکری کی الخ حالانکہ اس کے پاس بکریاں نہیں ہیں تو وصیت صحیح ہے یا نہیں تو اس میں دو قول ہیں۔ وصیت صحیح نہیں ہے اسلئے کہ وصیت تو اسی وقت صحیح ہوتی جبکہ مال کی طرف اس کی اضافت کر دی جاتی ورنہ جب مال کی طرف شاہ کی اضافت نہ کی جائے تو وہاں عین بکری محوط و مقصود ہوتی ہے اس کی مالیت مقصود نہیں ہوتی مین بکری بتانے کیلئے ”صورة الشاة و معناها “ کہا ہے۔  كتاب الوصايا اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۹ وسیت صحیح ہے کیونکہ جب اس نے اپنے کلام میں لفظ شاہ ذکر کیا ہے حالانکہ اس کی ملکیت میں شا ہ نہیں ہے تو یہ اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ موسی کی مراد مالیت ہے نہ کہ میں جگر کی۔
And if he bequeathed a sheep, without adding it to his property, and he has no goats, it is said it is not valid because the corrector is the addition to property, and without it the form and meaning of the sheep are considered. And it is said it is valid, because when he mentioned the sheep and he does not own a sheep, it is known that his intent is the monetary value. Translation: And if he bequeathed a sheep and did not add it to his property, and he has no sheep, then it is said that the bequest is not valid because the corrector is the addition of the sheep to property, and without addition the form and meaning of the sheep are considered. And it is said it is valid because when the testator mentioned 'sheep' and he does not have a sheep in his ownership, it became known that his intent is the monetary value. Explanation: If the testator only said 'There is a bequest of a sheep for so-and-so' and did not say 'from my property', even though he has no sheep, then is the bequest valid or not? There are two opinions. The bequest is not valid because a bequest is only valid when it is added to property; otherwise when the sheep is not added to property, the actual sheep is meant and intended, not its monetary value. For indicating the actual sheep, it is said 'the form and meaning of the sheep'. [Page 137] Book of Wills, Ashraf al-Hidaya Urdu commentary vol 19: The bequest is valid because when the testator mentioned the word 'sheep' while he owns no sheep, this is evidence that his intent is the monetary value, not the specific sheep.
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This is a disputed ruling within the Hanafi school. The text presents two views (qīla): one view holds the bequest invalid because the correct factor (musahhih) is the addition to property; without it, the bequest is considered as a specific sheep (form and meaning) which is non-existent. The other view holds it valid because mentioning a sheep when none is owned indicates the intent is the monetary value. The Urdu commentary explains both views but then states that the correct opinion (sahih) is that it is valid, as the testator's mention of a sheep without owning one implies his intent is the value. This is an application of the principle that words are interpreted according to what is commonly understood.

Key Terms
شاة (shāt): Sheep, the bequeathed item.
مالية (māliyyah): Monetary value.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view in this passage, what is the ruling when a testator bequeaths a sheep without adding it to property and has no sheep?
A) The bequest is void
B) The bequest is valid and the legatee gets nothing
C) The bequest is valid and the legatee gets the value
D) The bequest is suspended

Key Takeaway
When a testator bequeaths an item he does not own, Hanafi law infers his intent is the item's value, making the bequest valid.

Bequest of a Sheep from Goats When No Goats Exist
Ruling that the bequest is void when added to a specific category

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a bequest added to a specific category (e.g., 'from my goats') is void if that category does not exist, and distinguish it from a bequest added to property.

Core Idea
Addition to a category specifies the actual item; absence makes the bequest void.

This passage from the Hanafi fiqh on bequests (wasiyyah) illustrates a critical principle: the wording of a bequest determines whether the testator intended a specific item or its value. When a bequest is added to a specific category like 'my goats', the testator is referring to a particular animal as part of that herd. If the herd does not exist, the bequest fails because the subject matter is non-existent at both the time of will and death. This contrasts with a bequest added to 'property', where the value is intended and the bequest may still be valid even if no specific item exists.

Guided Path
1
Identify the wording of the bequest
Examine the exact phrase used: 'a sheep from my goats' (shaatan min ghanami). The addition 'min ghanami' is crucial.
2
Determine the effect of addition to ghanam
Adding to 'goats' indicates the testator intends a specific animal as part of a defined category, not just its value. The Arabic grammar ties the sheep to the goats.
Contrast with addition to 'mal' (property).
3
Apply the existence condition
Since the testator has no goats, the category is non-existent. Therefore, the specific sheep referred to is also non-existent at the time of will and at death.
Hanafi law requires the subject matter to exist at both times for a bequest to be valid.
4
Distinguish from addition to mal
If the bequest were added to 'property' (mal), the testator's intent would be the value, which can be satisfied even if no specific sheep exists. Hence, the bequest would be valid and the value given.
This principle governs many similar cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولوقال شاة من غنمى ولا غنم له فالوصية باطلة لانه لما اضافه الى الغنم علمنا ان مراده عين الشاة حيث جعلها جزء من الغنم بخلاف ما اذا اضافها الى المال وعلى هذا يخرج كثير من المسائل ترجمہ اور اگر موسی نے کیا ہو کہ میری بکریوں میں سے ایک بکری اور اس کیلئے بکریاں نہیں ہیں تو وصیت باطل ہے اسلئے کہ جب موسی نے شاہ کی اضافت منم کی طرف کر دی تو ہمیں یہ بات معلوم ہوگئی کہ موصی کی مراد متین بکری ہے اس حیثیت سے کہ موصی نے شاہ کو ختم کا ایک جز قرار دیا ہے بخلاف اس صورت کے جبکہ موصی نے شاہ کی اضافت مال کی طرف کی ہو اور اس قاعدہ پر بہت سے مسائل کی تو ہی ہوتی ہے۔ تشریح اگر موصی نے بوقت وصیت یہ الفاظ استعمال کئے کہ فلاں کیلئے میر کی بکریوں میں سے ایک بکری ہے، حالانکہ موصی کے پاس بکریاں نہیں ہیں تو اب و نیست باطل ہو جائے گی کیونکہ موصی نے لفظ شاہ کی اضافت غنم کی جانب کر کے یہ واضح کر دیا کہ میری مراد مالیت نہیں بلکہ مین بکری ہے کیونکہ اس نے شاہ کو فلم کا ایک جز قرار دیتے ہوئے کہا ہے " نشاة من علمي " تو بیشی معدوم کیلئے وصیت ہوئی جو وقت وصیت اور بوقت موت دونوں صورتوں میں معدوم ہے لہذا، سیت باطل ہو جائے گی ۔ البتہ اگر مال کی طرف شاہ کی اضافت کی جائے تو وہاں مالیت مقصود ہوتی ہے اس پر مصنف فرماتے ہیں کہ یہ ایسا جنرال پوائنگ ہے ں پر بہت سے مسائل متفرع ہوتے ہیں ان میں سے کچھ حواشی و شروح میں مذکور ہیں۔
And if he said, 'A sheep from my goats,' and he has no goats, then the bequest is void, because when he added it to the goats, we knew that his intent is the specific sheep, since he made it a part of the goats, contrary to when he adds it to property. And upon this many issues arise. Translation: And if the testator said, 'A sheep from my goats for him,' and he has no goats, then the bequest is void because when the testator added 'sheep' to 'goats', we understood that the testator's intent is the specific sheep, in the sense that the testator made the sheep a part of the goats, contrary to the case when the testator added the sheep to property. And upon this principle many issues are derived. Explanation: If the testator at the time of the will used these words: 'There is a sheep from my goats for so-and-so,' even though the testator has no goats, then the bequest will be void because the testator added the word 'sheep' to 'goats' making it clear that his intent is not the monetary value but the specific sheep, because he said 'a sheep from my goats,' making the sheep a part of the goats. So the bequest is for a non-existent item, which is non-existent at the time of the will and at the time of death, therefore the bequest is void. However, if the sheep is added to property, then the monetary value is intended. The author says this is a general rule upon which many issues branch, some of which are mentioned in the commentaries and glosses.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof and a general principle (qa'ida). When a testator says 'a sheep from my goats', the addition to 'goats' (ghanam) indicates that he intends the actual animal as part of a specific herd. Since he has no goats, the bequest is for a non-existent item and is thus void. This is contrasted with addition to 'property' (mal), where value is given. The text states that this principle applies to many other similar cases. The Urdu commentary clarifies that the bequest is void because it is for a non-existent item at both the time of will and death. The author (possibly al-Quduri or the commentator) notes this as a foundational rule (qa'ida) for many branched issues.

Key Terms
غنم (ghanam): Goats or sheep collectively; a category of livestock.
عين (ayn): The specific entity or object.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a testator says 'I give him a sheep from my goats' but has no goats?
A) The bequest is valid and he receives the value
B) The bequest is void
C) The bequest is valid and he receives a sheep at a later date
D) The bequest is valid only if the testator intended value

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a bequest added to a specific category requires that category to exist; otherwise, the bequest is void because the subject matter is non-existent.

Distribution of One-Third to Ummahat Awlad and the Poor: Shaykhan vs. Muhammad
Intra-Hanafi dispute on share allocation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between the Shaykhan and Imam Muhammad regarding the distribution of a bequest and apply the thamarah al-khilaf to a similar case.

Core Idea
When bequeathing to ummahat awlad and both groups of the poor, Shaykhan count fuqara and masakin as one; Muhammad treats them separately.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: when a testator bequeaths one-third of his estate to his three ummahat awlad (mothers of his children) and also to the poor (fuqara) and needy (masakin), how should the one-third be divided? The Shaykhan (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) divide it into five shares, while Imam Muhammad divides it into seven. The difference hinges on whether fuqara and masakin are treated as one category or two.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and each position
Note that the Shaykhan (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold one view, and Imam Muhammad holds another. Both are within the Hanafi school.
The Shaykhan are the two primary founders; Muhammad is the foremost student.
2
State the share distribution under each
Under Shaykhan: total 5 shares – mothers get 3, poor+needy get 2. Under Muhammad: total 7 shares – mothers get 3, poor get 2, needy get 2.
3
Identify the basis for Muhammad's view
Muhammad relies on the Zakat classification where fuqara and masakin are distinct categories (jinsan). The text says 'we have explained them in the book of Zakat'.
The Shaykhan's basis is not given; they may consider the wording as implying one group.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: in Shaykhan's view, the combined group gets 2/5 of the one-third; in Muhammad's view, each subgroup gets 2/7, so they receive more separately.
This affects the amount each individual poor/needy person receives.
5
Consider the tarjih (preferred view)
The text does not explicitly give tarjih, but in the Hanafi school, the view of Abu Hanifa (Shaykhan) is usually preferred unless overridden. Many later authorities adopt the Shaykhan's view.
Check later fatwa works for the mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال و من اوصى بثلث ماله لا مهات أولاده وهن ثلث وللفقراء والمساكين فلهن ثلثة اسهم من خمسة اسهم قال الله عنه وهذا عند ابي حنيفة وابي يوسف وعن محمد انه يقسم على سبعة اسهم لهن ثلثة ولكل فريق رضی سهمان واصله ان الوصية لامهات الاولاد جائزة والفقراء والمساكين جنسان وفسرنا هما في الزكوة ترجمه قدوری نے فرمایا اور جس نے ایک ثلث مال کی وصیت کی اپنی امہات اولاد کیلئے حالانکہ وہ تین ہیں اور فقراء ومساکین کیلئے تو امہات اولاد کیلئے پانچ حصوں میں سے تین حصے ہوں گے مصنف رضی اللہ عنہ نے فرمایا اور یہ شیخین کے نزدیک ہے اور امام محمد سے منقول ہے کہ ثالث کو سات حصوں پر تقسیم کیا جائے گا امہات اولاد کیلئے تین حصے ہوں گے اور ہر فریق کیلئے دو دو حصے اور اس کی اصل یہ ہے کہ امہات اولاد کیلئے وصیت جائز ہے اور فقرا ، اور مساکین دو جنسیں ہیں اور ہم ان دونوں کی کتاب الزکوۃ میں تقسیم کر چکے ہیں۔ تشرق ایک شخص کی تین ام ولد ہیں تو اب وہ ان الفاظ میں وصیت کرتا ہے کہ میرے مال کا نت میری امہات اولا دکواور مساکین اور فتراء نگیر کتب میں اما کو دے دیا جائے تو اب تک کی تقسیم کس طرح ہوگی اس میں شیخین اور امامحمد کا اختلاف ہے۔ جامع صغیر کے علاوہ مودی محمد نے فرمایا ہے کہ ثلاث کو سات حصوں پر تقسیم کیا جائے ان میں سے تین امہات اولاد کیلئے ہوں گے یعنی ہر ایک کا ایک اور چار مساکین
He said: And whoever makes a bequest of one-third of his property for the mothers of his children, and they are three, and for the poor and needy, then they (the mothers) get three shares out of five. The author (may Allah be pleased with him) said: And this is according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. And from Muhammad: that it is divided into seven shares: they get three, and each group gets two shares. And the origin is that a bequest for mothers of children is valid, and the poor and needy are two different classes, and we have explained them in the chapter of Zakat. Translation: Quduri said: And whoever makes a bequest of one-third of his property for his ummahat awlad, and they are three, and for the poor and needy, then the ummahat awlad get three shares out of five. The author (may Allah be pleased with him) said: And this is according to the two Shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). And from Imam Muhammad that the one-third is divided into seven shares: the ummahat awlad get three shares, and each group gets two shares. And its basis is that the bequest for ummahat awlad is valid, and the poor and needy are two distinct categories, and we have explained them in the book of Zakat. Explanation: A person has three umm walads. He makes a bequest with these words: 'One-third of my property for my ummahat awlad and also for the masakin and fuqara from my estate...' How will the distribution be? There is a difference between the two Shaykhs and Imam Muhammad. In al-Jami' al-Saghir, Imam Muhammad said that the one-third is divided into seven shares: among them three for the ummahat awlad (one each) and four for the masakin.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute between the Shaykhan (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) and Imam Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani regarding the distribution of a bequest of one-third of the estate to three ummahat awlad (mothers of the testator's children, i.e., his former slave concubines who bore his children) and to the poor (fuqara) and needy (masakin). According to the Shaykhan, the one-third is divided into five shares: the three ummahat awlad receive three shares (one each), and the poor and needy collectively receive two shares (the text does not specify how these two are split between the two groups, but presumably one each or they share equally). According to Imam Muhammad, the one-third is divided into seven shares: the three ummahat awlad receive three shares, the poor receive two shares, and the needy receive two shares. The basis for Muhammad's view is that fuqara and masakin are two distinct categories (jinsān), as explained in the Zakat chapter, so they should be treated separately. The commentary notes that this difference is recorded in the books, and that Imam Muhammad's view is in al-Jami' al-Saghir. The Hanafi school typically follows the Shaykhan on many issues, but the commentary does not explicitly state which is mufta bihi here.

Key Terms
أمهات أولاد (ummahāt awlād): Mothers of children; female slaves who have borne a child to their master.
فقراء (fuqarāʾ): The poor; those who have insufficient means.
مساكين (masākīn): The needy; those in need.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 1 share
B) 2 shares
C) 3 shares
D) 4 shares

Key Takeaway
The intra-Hanafi dispute over whether fuqara and masakin are one or two categories affects the distribution of a bequest, with Shaykhan counting five shares and Muhammad counting seven.

Bequest to Named and Poor: Shaykhayn vs Imam Muhammad
Intra-Hanafi dispute on division of one-third bequest between a named person and the poor

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) and Imam Muhammad regarding the division of a bequest between a named person and the poor, and explain the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) in the number of poor recipients.

Core Idea
Shaykhayn divide the bequest equally; Imam Muhammad gives the poor double the named person's share and requires at least two poor recipients.

When a testator bequeaths one-third of their estate to a named individual and to 'the poor,' how should the bequest be divided? This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) and Imam Muhammad. The disagreement covers both the proportional split and the minimum number of poor recipients, reflecting different interpretations of the testator's intent and the meaning of 'the poor' (masākīn).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two disputes
The passage contains two related disputes: (1) how to divide the one-third when the bequest is to a named person and the poor; (2) if the bequest is only to the poor, how many poor persons must receive it.
Both disputes stem from the same qāʿida about the category 'the poor'.
2
State the Shaykhayn's position
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that the named person receives half of the one-third, the poor receive the other half. If the bequest is only to the poor, the testator may confine it to one poor person.
They treat the poor as a flexible category that can be satisfied by one.
3
State Imam Muhammad's position
Imam Muhammad holds that the named person receives one-third of the one-third, and the poor receive two-thirds. If the bequest is only to the poor, it must be distributed to at least two poor persons.
He treats 'the poor' as a plural requiring at least two individuals.
4
Identify the underlying principle
The disagreement hinges on the interpretation of 'masākīn': whether it can be satisfied by one (Shaykhayn) or requires at least two (Muhammad). This principle also affects the proportional division.
The passage references a previously explained principle (qāʿida).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under Shaykhayn, the named person gets half of the bequest (1/6 of total estate) and the poor get half (1/6); under Muhammad, the named gets 1/3 of the bequest (1/9) and the poor get 2/3 (2/9). Also, the minimum poor recipients differ (one vs. two).
This affects actual distribution in estate administration.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمہ امام حمد نے فرمایا اور اگر اپنے تہائی مال کی وصیت فلاں اور مساکین کیلئے کی تو اس کا نصف فلاں کیلئے اور اس کا نصف مساکین کیلئے شیخین کے نزدیک اور محمد کے نزدیک اس کا ثلث فلاں کیلئے اور اس کے دو ثلث مساکین کیلئے ہوں گے اور اگر اس نے مساکین کیلئے وصیت کی تو شیخین کے نزدیک موصی کو حق ہے ایک مسکین پر صرف کرنے کا اور محمد کے نزدیک صرف نہیں کیا جائے گا مگر دو مسکینوں پر اس قاعدہ پر بناء کرتے ہوئے جس کو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں۔ تشریح اس عبارت کا مطلب ترجمہ سے ظاہر ہے فتدبر
Imam Muhammad said: And if he makes a bequest of his one-third of property to so-and-so and to the poor, then half of it is for so-and-so and half for the poor according to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). According to Muhammad, one-third is for so-and-so and two-thirds for the poor. And if he makes a bequest for the poor, according to the two shaykhs, the testator has the right to spend it on one poor person, while according to Muhammad, it will not be spent except on two poor persons, based on the principle we have already explained. Explanation: The meaning of this phrase is apparent from the translation, so ponder.
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the two shaykhs) on one side and Imam Muhammad on the other regarding the distribution of a bequest of one-third of the estate when it is directed to a named individual and to the poor collectively. The two shaykhs hold that the named person receives half of the one-third and the poor receive the other half, treating them as equal shares. Imam Muhammad holds that the named person receives one-third of the one-third (i.e., one-ninth of the total estate) and the poor receive two-thirds of the one-third (i.e., two-ninths), giving the poor a larger share because of their collective need. Additionally, if the bequest is only for the poor without naming a specific number, the two shaykhs allow the testator to confine it to one poor person, while Imam Muhammad requires that it be distributed to at least two poor persons. This is based on the principle (qā‘ida) that the poor are not a single entity but a category, and the minimum to fulfill the category is two. The commentary ends with a note that the meaning is clear from the translation.

Key Terms
وصیت (waṣiyyah): Bequest or will directing distribution of up to one-third of the estate after death.
مساکین (masākīn): The poor, as a category of recipients in a bequest.
شیخین (shaykhayn): Refers to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf together.
ثلث (thulth): One-third; the maximum portion that can be bequeathed in a will without heirs' consent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One-third of the one-third
B) Half of the one-third
C) Two-thirds of the one-third
D) The entire one-third

Key Takeaway
The Shaykhayn and Imam Muhammad differ on both the proportional division of a bequest to a named person and the poor, and on the minimum number of poor recipients, based on their interpretation of 'masākīn'.

Joint Bequests: The Principle of Equality in Partnership Language
Muhammad's ruling on distribution when a testator includes a third person as partner in bequests

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the Hanafi school distributes a bequest when a third person is included as a partner, distinguishing between equal and unequal initial amounts, and apply the principle of linguistic interpretation (shirkah implies equality) to derive the shares.

Core Idea
Partnership (shirkah) linguistically implies equality; implemented as far as possible, halving where full equality is impossible.

This lesson examines a specific case from Imam Muhammad in Al-Hidayah regarding joint bequests. When a testator includes a third person as a partner in a bequest already made to two others, how are the shares calculated? The answer turns on the linguistic meaning of 'shirkah' (partnership) and the principle that the testator's wording must be honoured to the extent possible. Through two scenarios—equal and unequal initial amounts—we see the Hanafi method of balancing textual fidelity with equitable results.

Guided Path
1
Determine the testator's intent from his wording
The wording 'I have made you a partner' indicates an intention of equal sharing among all beneficiaries.
2
Identify the linguistic principle
In Arabic, 'shirkah' (partnership) linguistically entails equality (musāwāh). This is the primary proof for the ruling.
This principle is stated explicitly in the passage: 'الشركة للمساواة لغة'.
3
Apply the principle when equality is possible
When the two original bequests are equal (e.g., both 100 dirhams), the third partner takes one-third of each, achieving equality among all three.
Each of the three ends with 66.66 dirhams.
4
Apply when equality is impossible
When amounts differ (e.g., 400 and 200 dirhams), full equality cannot be achieved, so the third partner takes half of each, honouring the wording as much as possible.
The third gets 200 from the first and 100 from the second, totalling 300, while the original beneficiaries are left with 200 and 100 respectively.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ومن اوصى لرجل بمائة درهم ولأخر بمائة ثم قال لاخر قد اشركتك معهما فله ثلث كل مائة لان الشركة للمساواة لغة وقد امكن اثباته بين الكل بما قلناه لا تحاد المال لانه يصيب كل واحد منهم ثلثا مائة بخلاف ما اذا اوصى لرجل باربع مائة ولاخر بمائتين ثم كان الاشراك لانه لا يمكن تحقيق المساواة بين الكل التفاوت المالين فحملناه على مساواته كل واحد بتنصيف نصيبه عملا باللفظ بقدر الامكان
He (Muhammad) said: Whoever makes a bequest to a man of one hundred dirhams, and to another of one hundred dirhams, then says to a third: I have made you a partner with them, then he gets one-third of each hundred, because partnership linguistically means equality, and we have been able to establish equality among all by what we said due to the unity of the amount, so each one of them gets two-thirds of a hundred. Contrary to the case where he makes a bequest to a man of four hundred and to another of two hundred, then he makes a partnership, because equality cannot be achieved among all due to the disparity of the two amounts, so we interpreted it as making him equal to each of them by halving his share, acting upon the wording as much as possible.
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage from Imam Muhammad explains two scenarios of joining a third person as a partner in a bequest. In the first scenario, the testator bequeaths equal amounts (100 dirhams each) to two people, then says to a third person 'I have made you a partner with them.' Since partnership (shirkah) linguistically implies equality, the third person shares in each of the two bequests equally taking one-third of each, totalling 66.66 dirhams. Thus each of the three ends with 66.66 dirhams. In the second scenario, the bequests are unequal: 400 and 200 dirhams. Including a third person to make equality impossible because the amounts differ. So to salvage the meaning of partnership, Imam Muhammad rules that the third person takes half of each beneficiary's share: from the first (400) he takes 200, from the second (200) he takes 100, so he gets 300 total, while the first gets 200 and the second gets 100, achieving some level of equality through proportional reduction. The principle is to implement the wording (sharikat) as much as possible even if absolute equality is not possible.

Key Terms
شرکت (shirkah): Partnership or sharing; here used in the context of including a third person in a bequest.
مساوات (musāwāh): Equality of shares among partners.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the first scenario where a testator bequeaths 100 dirhams to each of two persons, then says to a third 'I make you a partner with them', what total amount does the third person receive?
A) 33.33 dirhams
B) 66.66 dirhams
C) 100 dirhams
D) 133.33 dirhams

Key Takeaway
When a testator uses partnership language, the Hanafi school enforces equality of shares as much as possible, and when full equality is impossible, the third partner takes half of each existing share.

Istihsan Overrides Qiyas: Deathbed Acknowledgment of an Unknown Debt
Istihsan vs qiyas on validity of dying person's acknowledgment of a debt without specifying amount

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school applies istihsan to validate a dying person's acknowledgment of an unspecified debt and state the resulting ruling (up to one-third).

Core Idea
Istihsan transforms a deathbed acknowledgment of an unspecified debt into a valid bequest up to one-third of the estate.

This lesson examines a classic Hanafi ruling where a dying person instructs his heirs to affirm a debt without specifying the amount. Strict analogical reasoning (qiyas) would reject this due to the unknown amount and lack of evidence. However, the Hanafi school invokes istihsan (juristic preference) to honor the testator's intention, treating the acknowledgment as a bequest limited to one-third. Understanding this case reveals how Hanafi usul balances textual principles with equitable outcomes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Read the passage and identify the act being ruled upon: the dying person's statement to his heirs that someone has a debt against him without specifying the amount. Then note the ruling: 'he is affirmed up to one-third' — meaning the acknowledgment is valid but limited.
The act is an iqrar (acknowledgment) made during death illness (marad al-mawt).
2
State the qiyas position and its reasoning
The passage states that according to qiyas, the acknowledgment would not be affirmed. Extract the reasons: (1) acknowledgment of an unknown amount cannot be adjudicated without clarification, and (2) the instruction to affirm without evidence contradicts Shari'ah, as a plaintiff must bring proof.
Qiyas here is based on the general rule that iqrar of an unknown amount is valid but cannot be executed until specified.
3
Explain the istihsan position and its wajh
The istihsan reasoning (wajh) is provided: the testator's intention is to prefer the claimant over heirs, and this can be realized through the rules of bequest (wasiyya). The acknowledgment is thus treated as a bequest, allowing the claimant to determine the amount up to one-third of the estate.
This istihsan overrides the strict qiyas by prioritizing intention and practical feasibility.
4
Summarize the practical consequence
The final ruling: the claimant is believed up to one-third of the estate, but not more. Any claim exceeding one-third is disregarded.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ومن قال لفلان على دين فصدقوه معناه قال ذلك لورثته فانه يصدق الى الثلث وهذا استحسان وفي القياس لا يصدق لان الاقرار بالمجهول وان كان صحيحا لكنه لا يحكم به الا بالبيان وقوله فصدقوه صدر مخالفا للشرع لأن المدعى لا يصدق الا بحجة فتعذر اثباته اقرار امطلقا فلا يعتبر وجه الاستحسان انا نعلم ان من قصده تقديمه على الورثة وقد امكن تنفيذ قصده بطريق الوصية وقد يحتاج الـيـه مـن يعمل باصل الحق عليه دون مقداره سعيا[؟]منه في تفريغ ذمنه فيجعلها وصية جعل التقدير فيها الى الموصى له كانه قال اذا جاءكم فلان وادعى شيئا فاعطوه من مالى ما شاء هذه معتبرة من الثلث فلهذا يصدق على الثلث دون الزيادة
He (Muhammad) said: And whoever says 'So-and-so has a debt against me, so affirm him' meaning he said that to his heirs, then he is affirmed up to one-third. This is istihsan (juristic preference). And in qiyas (analogy) he is not affirmed, because acknowledgment of an unknown amount, though valid, is not adjudicated except with clarification. And his saying 'so affirm him' occurred contrary to Shari'ah, because a plaintiff is not affirmed except with evidence. So establishing this as an absolute acknowledgment is not possible, so it is not considered. The wajh (reason) of istihsan is: we know that his intention is to prefer him over the heirs, and it is possible to implement his intention through the way of bequest. And he may need, by acting on the principle of the right against him without its amount, striving to discharge his responsibility. So we make it a bequest, and we make the determination of amount up to the legatee, as if he said: When so-and-so comes to you and claims something, give him from my wealth whatever he wishes. This is taken into account from the one-third. Therefore he is affirmed up to one-third, not more.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage deals with a scenario where a dying person (moribund) tells his heirs that someone (e.g., Khālid) has a debt against him, but does not specify the amount, and tells them to affirm him (i.e., acknowledge the debt) when he comes. According to qiyas (analogy), such an acknowledgment cannot be executed because the amount is unknown and the instruction to affirm without evidence contradicts the Shari'ah requirement that a claimant must provide proof. However, the Hanafi school applies istihsan (juristic preference) to override qiyas: the testator's intention is to prefer the claimant over the heirs, and this can be achieved by treating the statement as a bequest (wasiyya) limited to one-third of the estate. The amount is left to the claimant's own statement, similar to a bequest where the testator says 'give him whatever he asks.' Therefore, the claimant is believed up to one-third of the estate, but not more. This illustrates the Hanafi principle of using istihsan to honor the testator's intent while protecting the heirs' rights.

Key Terms
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference that overrides strict qiyas in favor of a more equitable result based on intention and custom.
قیاس (qiyās): Analogical reasoning; the ruling derived by analogy from a primary case.
اقرار (iqrār): Acknowledgment of a right or debt; a legal declaration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because acknowledgment of an unknown quantity is invalid
B) Because the instruction contradicts Shari'ah which requires evidence for a claim
C) Because the testator cannot prefer one heir over others
D) Both A and B

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uses istihsan to validate a deathbed acknowledgment of an unspecified debt, treating it as a bequest up to one-third of the estate.

Will with Unknown Amount and Its Priority Over Other Wills
Explains Hanafi ruling on a will delegating amount and distribution with other wills.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a will where the testator delegates the amount to the beneficiary, and apply the rule that known wills take priority over an unknown will when distributing the estate's one-third.

Core Idea
A will delegating the amount is valid but capped at one-third; known wills are satisfied first.

This lesson examines two connected rulings from Al-Hidayah on wills. First, when a testator says 'give my creditor whatever he claims', this is treated as a will (not an acknowledgment) and limited to one-third. Second, when there are multiple wills, the known ones are separated first, and the unknown claimant can only take from the remaining portion. We will trace the Hanafi use of istihsan and the principle that the unknown does not compete with the known.

Guided Path
1
Identify the testator's statement
Recognize that the testator's instruction 'give him whatever he claims' is a statement delegating the amount to the beneficiary.
This is not a simple acknowledgment (iqrar) but a will because it relates to a third party's right.
2
Classify the statement as a will
Under Hanafi istihsan, this statement is treated as a will, not an acknowledgment, to limit its effect to one-third of the estate.
The testator's intention is to clear his conscience, analogous to a will with delegated authority.
3
Apply the one-third limitation
The will is valid but its maximum execution is one-third of the estate. The claimant's statement is confirmed up to one-third.
If the claimant demands more than one-third, he only gets one-third.
4
Introduce other known wills
If the testator also made other specific bequests, those known wills take priority. First, set aside one-third for the known wills and two-thirds for the heirs.
The unknown will does not compete with known ones because it is ambiguous (majhul).
5
Determine the unknown claimant's recovery
After separation, each group (known will beneficiaries and heirs) can acknowledge the claim within their share. Their acknowledgments are binding proportionally, and each group must swear an oath if the claimant seeks more than acknowledged.
The total paid to the unknown claimant from both groups is limited to the one-third share (after known wills are taken).

Source Text

کے طریقہ پر اور کبھی اس اقرار کی جانب وہ شخص محتاج ہوتا ہے جو اپنے اوپر اصل حق کو جانتا ہے نہ کہ اس کی مقدار کو اپنی جانب سے اپنے ذمہ کی تفریغ میں کوشش کرتے ہوئے تو وہ اس کو ایسی وصیت قرار دیتا ہے جس میں تقدیر موصی لہ کی جانب محول ہو گویا کہ موصی نے یوں کہا کہ جب تمہارے پاس فلاں شخص آئے اور میرے مال میں سے کچھ کا دعوی کرے تو میرے مال میں سے اس کو اتنادے دینا جتنا ہو چاہے اور یہ وصیت تہائی سے معتبر ہوتی ہے اسی وجہ سے فلاں کی تہائی تک تصدیق کی جائے گی نہ کہ زیادہ میں ۔ تشریح یہ استحسان کی دلیل ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ یہاں زید کا مقصد یہ ہے کہ خالد کو درخا پر مقدم رکھا جائے اور یہاں اس کے ارادہ کونا فذ کیا جا سکتا ہے جس کا طریقہ یہ ہوگا کہ اس کو وصیت قرار دیا جائے۔ اس لئے کہ کبھی ایسا ہو جاتا ہے کہ ایک شخص پر کسی کا حق ہے لیکن وہ اس کی مقدار سے واقف نہیں ہے پس اتنا جانتا ہے کہ خالد کا میرے او پر حق ہے تو ایسی صورت میں زید محتاج ہو گا کہ وہ اس قسم کی وصیت کرے جس سے وہ حق اتر جائے جو اس کے ذمہ ہے لیکن اس کی مقدار سے زید واقف نہیں اسلئے وہ مجبوراً کہتا ہے کہ خالد جو کہے اس کی تصدیق کر دینا تو یہ ایسی وصیت کی ہو گئی جس میں موصی یہ کی تعداد بیان کرنے کا اختیار خود موصی لیہ کو ہو تو وہ وصیت درست ہے اور موصی لہ کو یہ اختیار نہ ہوگا بلکہ اس کو صرف ثلث ملے گا۔ تو یہاں زید کی وصیت کا حاصل یہ ہوا کہ جب تمہارے پاس خالد آئے اور مجھ پر اپنا مالی دعوی کرے تو جتنا وہ چاہے اتنا ہی اس کو میرے مال میں سے دے دینا تو یہ وصیت صحیح ہے اور معتبر ہے لیکن تہائی تک معتبر ہے زیادہ میں نہیں لہذا صورت مذکورہ میں خالد کی تصدیق فقط ثلث تک کی جائے گی اس سے زیادہ میں نہیں کی جائے گی۔

اصحاب الوصایا کا ثلث الگ کیا جائے اور ورثا کا دو ٹکٹ الگ کیا جائے۔

تشریح یعنی معلوم اور مجہول کا تقاضہ بھی یہ تھا کہ مجہول معلوم کا مزاحم نہ ہو اور معلوم کو جدا کر لیا جائے اور ساتھ ہی ساتھ جدا کرنے میں اور بھی فائدہ ہے اور وہ یہ کہ ہو سکتا ہے کہ ایک فریق خالد کے حق کے متعلق زیادہ معلومات اور زیادہ بصیرت رکھتا ہو اور دوسرا فریق دیدہ دانستہ جھگڑالو، یعنی جب خالد آکر دعویٰ کرے کہ میرے تین سو روپے تھے تو ایک فریق تو کہہ دے کہ ہاں سچ کہتا ہے، اتنا ہی تھا اور دوسرا فریق کہے کہ جھوٹ کہتا ہے اس کے تو پچاس روپے تھے خواہ مخواہ تین سو بتاتا ہے۔
لیکن جب ہر فریق کا حصہ الگ کر دیا گیا تو ہر فریق اپنے اقرار میں ماخوذ ہوگا اور کوئی منازعت اور جھگڑے کی صورت سامنے نہ آئے گی ، خیر تو اب کیا طریقہ اختیار کیا جائے گا اس کو مصنف نے اگلی عبارت میں پیش کیا ہے۔
ہر فریق اصحاب الوصایا اور ورثا میں سے اپنے اقرار کے مطابق ماخوذ ہوگا
واذا عزل يقال لا صحاب الوصايا صدقوه فيما شئتم ويقال للورثة صدقوه فيما شئتم لان هذا دين في حق المستحق وصية في حق التنفيذ فاذا اقر كل فريق بشئى ظهران فى التركة دينا شائعا في النصيبين فيؤخذ اصحاب الثلث بثلث ما اقروا والورثة بثلثى ما اقرو اتنفيذ الاقرار كل فريق فى قدر حقه وعلى كل فريق منهما اليمين على العلم ان ادعى المقرله زيادة على ذالك لانه يحلف على ما جرى بينه وبين غيره ترجمہ اور جب الگ کر لیا گیا تو اصحاب الوصایا سے کہا جائے گا کہ تم اس کی تصدیق کر جتنی مقدار میں چاہو اور ورثا سے کہا جائے گا کہ تم اس کی تصدیق کرو جتنی مقدار میں تم چاہو اس لئے کہ یہ سحق کے حق میں قرض ہے تحفیذ کے حق میں وصیت ہے پس جب کہ اقرار کر لیا ہر فریق نے کسی مقدار کا تو یہ بات ظاہر ہوگئی کہ ترکہ میں دین شائع ہے دونوں حصوں میں تو اصحاب الثلث ( موضی ہم ) اپنے اقرار کے ثلث میں ماخوذ ہوں گے اور ورڑنا اپنے اقرار کے دو ثلث میں ماخوذ ہوں گے ہر فریق کے اقرار کو نافذ کرتے ہوئے اس کے حق کی مقدار میں اور ان دونوں میں سے ہر فریق پر علم پر قسم کھانا ہے اگر مقر لہ اس اقرار سے زیادہ کا دعوی کرے اس لئے کہ فریق سے قسم لی جارہی ہے اس فعل پر جو اس کے اور اس کے غیر کے درمیان جاری ہوا ہے۔ تشریح جب پورے ترکہ کے تین سہام کر کے ایک تہائی اصحاب الوصایا الگ کر دی گئی اور ورثا کے دو ٹکٹ الگ کر دیے گئے تو
Book of Wills. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary on al-Hidayah, volume 16. ... (the complete passage is too long to translate here; see commentary). The meaning: this is the proof of istihsan, the gist of which is that Zayd's purpose is to prioritize Khalid over others, and his intention can be executed by considering this a will. Because sometimes a person owes a right but does not know its exact amount, so he makes a will delegating the amount to the beneficiary. This will is valid up to one-third, so Khalid's claim is confirmed only up to one-third, not more. Commentary: This is the proof of istihsan... (continues). Then: Imam Muhammad said: If he made other wills besides this, one-third is set aside for the beneficiaries of those wills and two-thirds for the heirs, because their inheritance is known and these wills are known, while this one is unknown, so the unknown does not compete with the known, and the known is separated first. Commentary: The previous ruling applies when there are no other wills; if there are other wills, the procedure is different. First, set aside one-third for the known wills and two-thirds for the heirs. Then, each group can confirm the claimant's statement within their share, and upon separation, each group's acknowledgment is valid for their portion, and if the claimant demands more, each group must take an oath.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage addresses two scenarios related to wills. First, when a testator says: 'If someone claims a right against me, give him whatever he asks.' Under Hanafi istihsan, this is treated as a valid will, but limited to one-third of the estate. The rationale is that the testator knows a debt exists but not the amount, so he effectively delegates the determination to the claimant. Second, if there are other known wills (e.g., specific bequests to named individuals), those known wills take priority. The estate is divided: one-third for the known will beneficiaries, two-thirds for the heirs. The claimant with the unknown amount can only recover from whatever remains after the known wills are fulfilled, up to the one-third share. After separation, each group (the known will beneficiaries and the heirs) can acknowledge the claimant's right within their portion, and each must swear an oath if the claimant seeks more than they acknowledge. This prevents disputes between groups with conflicting interests.

Key Terms
وصیت (wasiyyah): A testamentary disposition of property made by the testator to take effect after death, valid up to one-third of the estate.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; a method of reasoning that departs from strict analogy (qiyas) in favor of a more equitable outcome based on custom, necessity, or hidden analogy.
اقرار (iqrar): Acknowledgment or confession of a right against oneself; here, the testator's statement is treated as a will rather than an acknowledgment because it involves declaration about a third party's right.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When a testator says 'give Khalid whatever he claims' and there are no other wills, how much can Khalid receive?
A) The entire estate because the testator agreed to it.
B) Up to one-third of the estate because it is a will.
C) Only what the testator's heirs agree to.
D) Nothing, because the statement is invalid.

Key Takeaway
A will delegating the amount to the beneficiary is valid but capped at one-third, and known wills take priority over it when distributing the estate.

Wasiyyah — Bequest
intermediate
8 min
Effect of Acknowledgment After Segregation of the Third
a ruling statement with commentary explaining the effect of acknowledgment after segregation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on acknowledgment of a debt by legatees and heirs after the third is segregated, and calculate the amounts each party must pay.

Core Idea
After segregation, each party's acknowledgment binds only their share: legatees pay 1/3, heirs pay 2/3.

In estate administration, a debt claimed against the deceased may be acknowledged differently by legatees and heirs. This lesson explains the Hanafi ruling on how such acknowledgments are handled once the third (thulth) for bequests is separated from the heirs' shares. Understanding this prevents disputes and ensures each party is bound only to the extent of their portion.

Guided Path
1
Understand the benefit of segregation
Segregation separates the legatees' one-third from the heirs' two-thirds. This prevents disputes because each party acknowledges only what belongs to their share.
The unknown (disputed amount) does not interfere with the known (segregated shares).
2
Identify the dual nature of the claim
From the claimant's perspective, it is a debt. From the execution perspective, it is treated like a bequest. Therefore, execution is limited to the third, but the debt is spread over the entire estate proportionally.
This dual nature explains why both legatees and heirs are involved, not just legatees.
3
Apply the ruling on acknowledgment
After segregation, each party's acknowledgment is binding on them. Legatees pay one-third of what they acknowledge; heirs pay two-thirds. One party is not bound by the other's acknowledgment.
Example: Legatees acknowledge 300, heirs acknowledge 600 → legatees pay 100, heirs pay 400.
4
Recognize the oath requirement
If the claimant demands more than the acknowledged amount, each party must swear an oath based on knowledge (yamin 'ala al-'ilm) because the transaction occurred between the claimant and the testator, not the parties.
The oath is not one of certainty, as the parties did not directly witness the transaction.
