كتاب الوصايا
جس حصہ کا مالک ہے اس میں اس کی وصیت نافذ ہو جائے گی اور جس کا مالک بکر ہے اس میں وصیت نافذ نہ ہوگی بلکہ وہ بکر کی اجازت پر موقوف ہے اگر اجازت دیدے تو اس میں بھی نافذ ہوگی ورنہ نہیں۔ سوال زید اگرچہ بوقت وصیت اس پورے کمرہ کا مالک نہیں تھا لیکن اب بعد قسمت تو زید اس پورے کمرہ کا مالک ہو گیا ہے لہذا پورے کمرہ میں وصیت نافذ ہونی چاہئے؟
جواب اگر کوئی شخص دوسرے کی چیز کسی کو وصیت کر دے اور پھر موصی اس چیز کو خرید لے تو وصیت صحیح نہ ہوگی اسی طرح یہاں زید بوقت وصیت پورے کمرہ کا مالک نہیں ہے اور پورا کمرہ زید کی ملکیت میں بعد قسمت آیا ہے اور قسمت کی حقیقت مبادلہ ہے جیسے شرا، تو یہاں بھی پہلی وصیت نافذ ہوگی۔
لہذا خلاصہ کلام یہ ہوا کہ جب گھر تقسیم کیا گیا اور یہ کمرہ زید کے حصہ میں آگیا تو جو وصیت ہے اس میں وصیت نافذ ہوگی اور موصی بہ اس کمرہ کا نصف ہے۔ اور اگر وہ کمرہ بکر کے حصہ میں آیا ہو تو اب خالد کو موصی بہ کا بدل ملے گا یعنی جتنی جگہ اس کمرہ کی ہے اس سے آدھی خالد کو اس زمین میں سے دی جائے گی جو زید کے حصہ میں آئی ہے۔
موصی بہ فوت ہو جائے تو اس کا بدل قائم مقام بن جاتا ہے
كالجارية الموصى بها اذا قتلت خطا تنفذ الوصية فى بدلها بخلاف ما اذا بيع العبد الموصى به حيث لا تتعلق الوصية بثمنه لأن الوصية تبطل بالاقدام على البيع على مابيناه ولا تبطل بالقسمة
ترجمہ جیسے وہ باندی جس کی وصیت کر دی گئی جب کہ اس کو خطا قتل کر دیا ہو تو اس کے بدل میں وصیت نافذ ہو جائے گی بخلاف اس صورت کے جب کہ موصی بہ غلام کو بیچا گیا ہو اس حیثیت سے کہ وصیت اس کے ثمن سے متعلق نہ ہوگی اس لئے کہ وصیت باطل ہو جائے گی بیچ پر اقدام کی وجہ سے اس تفصیل کے مطابق جس کو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں اور وصیت تقسیم سے باطل نہ ہوگی ۔ تشریح جب موصی بہ فوت ہو جائے تو اس کا بدل اس کا قائم مقام ہو جاتا ہے اس کی ایک مثال پیش کی گئی ہے کہ جب زید نے اپنی باندی کی وصیت کسی شخص کے لئے کر دی اور کسی نے خطأ اس باندی کو قتل کر دیا تو اب موصی لیہ کو بجائے باندی کے اس کا بدل ملے گا۔ سوال اگر موصی نے غلام موصی بہ فروخت کر دیا تو یہاں بھی ثمن میں وصیت جاری ہوگی ؟ جواب نہیں ، اس لئے کہ موصی کا بیچ پر اقدام کرنا اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ وہ وصیت سے رجوع کر رہا ہے لہذا یہاں وصیت ہی باطل ہو جائے گی اور چونکہ تقسیم کرنا رجوع کرنے کی دلیل نہیں ہے لہذا تقسیم سے وصیت باطل نہ ہوگی یہ امام محمد کی دلیل ہے آگے شیخین کی دلیل آ رہی ہے۔
شیخین کی دلیل
ولهما انه اوصى بما يستقر ملكه فيه بالقسمة لان الظاهر انه يقصد الايصا بملک منتفع به من كل و ذالک يكون بالقسمة لان الانتفاع بالمشاع قاصر وقد استقر ملكه في جميع البيت اذا وقع في نصيبه فتنفذ الوصية فيه ومعنى المبادلة فى هذه القسمة تابع وانما المقصود الافراز تكميلا للمنفعة ولهذا يجبر على فيه وعلى اعتبار الافراز يصير كان البيت ملكه من الابتداء
ترجمہ اور شیخین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ موصی نے اس چیز کی وصیت کی ہے جس میں تقسیم سے اس کی ملکیت ثابت ہو جائے گی اس لئے کہ ظاہر یہی ہے کہ موصی نے ایسی ملک کے ایصاء کا قصد کیا ہے جس سے ہر اعتبار سے نفع حاصل ہو سکے اور یہ ( پورا انتفاع ) تقسیم سے ہوسکتا ہے اس لئے کہ مشاع کے ذریعہ انتفاع قاصر ہے اور جب کمرہ موصی کے حصہ میں آگیا تو پورے کمرہ میں اس کی ملک جم گئی تو اس میں وصیت نافذ ہوگی اور اس تقسیم میں مبادلہ کے معنی تابع ہیں اور مقصود افراز ہے گویا کہ شروع ہی سے کمرہ موصی کی ملکیت ہے۔ تشریح یہ حضرات شیخین کی دلیل فرماتے ہیں کہ بوقت وصیت اگرچہ پورے کمرہ میں زید کی ملکیت نہیں تھی لیکن یہ احتمال اس میں سے موجود ہے کہ بٹوارہ کے ذریعہ اس میں زید کی ملکیت ثابت ہو جائے ، اور جب بکر کو معلوم ہے کہ ساتھی نے اس کمرہ کی وصیت کر رکھی ہے وہ بھی اس کی رعایت رکھے گا کیونکہ ایسے مقامات پر رعایت کرنے کی عادت جاری ہے۔
اور جو چیز مشترک ہوتی ہے اس سے کما حقہ انتفاع حاصل نہیں ہو پاتا بلکہ اس سے انتفاع قاصر ہوتا ہے، تو زید کا منشاء پہلے سے یہ ہے کہ بعد قسمت یہ کمرہ خالد کے حوالہ کر دیا جائے گا کیونکہ زید کا مقصد یہی ہے کہ خالد کو اس کمرہ سے پورا نفع حاصل ہو اور یہ تقسیم کے بغیر ممکن نہیں ہے، بہر حال جب پہلے سے یہ مقصد تھا اور اب تقسیم ہو کر پورا کمرہ زید کی ملکیت میں آگیا تو وصیت نافذ کر دی جائے گی اور پورا کمرہ خالد کے حوالہ کر دیا جائے گا۔
رہا امام محمد کا یہ فرمان کہ قسمت میں مبادلہ کے معنی ہیں جو شراء کے درجہ میں ہے تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ قسمت میں مبادلہ اور افراز دونوں پہلو ہوتے ہیں اور حیوانات و عروض میں مبادلہ کے معنی غالب ہوتے ہیں اور جنس واحد میں افراز کے معنی غالب ہوتے ہیں تو یہاں جنس واحد ہے جس میں افراز کے معنی اصل ہیں اور مبادلہ کے معنی مغلوب ہیں اور تابع ہیں ، اور چونکہ یہاں افراز کے معنی غالب ہیں اس وجہ سے قسمت پر جبر جائز ہے ورنہ جہاں مبادلہ کے معنی غالب ہوں قاضی کا جبر جائز نہیں ہے ( جس کا تفصیلی بیان کتاب القسمۃ میں گزر چکا ہے)۔ بہر حال جب یہاں افراز کے معنی غالب ہیں تو اس سے یہ بات واضح ہو گئی کہ گویا شروع ہی سے یہ کمرہ زید کی ملکیت ہے لہذا وصیت اس میں نافذ ہوگی۔
مذکورہ مسئلہ کی مزید وضاحت
وان وقع فى نصيب الآخر تنفذ في قدر ذرعان جميع مما وقع فى نصيبه اما لانه عوضه كما ذكرناه اولان مراد الموصى من ذكر البيت التقدير به تحصيلا لمقصوده ما امكن الا انه يتعين البيت اذا وقع في نصيبه جمعا بين الجهتين التقدير والتمليك وان وقع فى نصيب الاخر عملنا بالتقدير اولانه اراد التقدير على اعتبار احد الوجهين والتمليك بعينه على اعتبار الوجه الاخر
Book of Wills. In whatever portion he owns, his bequest will be effective, and in whatever portion Bakr owns, the bequest will not be effective; rather it is suspended on Bakr's permission. If he permits, then it will be effective in that portion too, otherwise not. Question: Zayd, although at the time of bequest he was not the owner of the entire room, but now after division, Zayd has become the owner of the entire room; therefore the bequest should be effective in the entire room? Answer: If a person bequeaths another's property to someone, and then the testator purchases that property, the bequest is not valid. Similarly here, Zayd at the time of bequest is not the owner of the entire room, and the entire room came into Zayd's ownership after division, and the reality of division is exchange like purchase; so here too the first bequest will be effective. Therefore the summary is that when the house was divided and this room came into Zayd's share, then the bequest will be effective in that room, and the bequeathed property is half of that room. And if that room came into Bakr's share, then Khalid will receive the substitute of the bequeathed property, i.e., half the area of that room will be given to Khalid from the land that came into Zayd's share. If the bequeathed property dies, its substitute takes its place. Like the slave-girl who was bequeathed, if she is killed accidentally, the bequest is executed in her substitute, unlike the case when the bequeathed slave is sold, where the bequest does not attach to his price, because the bequest is nullified by proceeding with the sale, as we have explained, and it is not nullified by division. Translation: For example, the slave-girl who was bequeathed, when she is accidentally killed, the bequest is executed in her substitute, contrary to the case when the bequeathed slave is sold, in which the bequest does not attach to his price, because the bequest becomes void due to proceeding with the sale, according to the detail we have explained, and the bequest does not become void due to division. Explanation: When the bequeathed property dies, its substitute takes its place. One example is given: when Zayd bequeaths his slave-girl to someone, and someone accidentally kills that slave-girl, then the legatee will receive her substitute in place of the slave-girl. Question: If the testator sold the bequeathed slave, then will the bequest apply to its price? Answer: No, because the testator's proceeding with the sale is evidence that he is retracting the bequest; therefore here the bequest itself becomes void. And since division is not evidence of retraction, the bequest does not become void by division. This is Imam Muhammad's proof; the proof of the two Shaykhs comes next. The proof of the two Shaykhs: And they argue that he bequeathed something in which his ownership becomes established through division, because the apparent meaning is that he intended to bequeath property from which benefit can be obtained in every aspect, and that can only happen through division, because benefit from shared property is limited. And when the room falls in his share, his ownership is established in the entire room, so the bequest is effective in it. The meaning of exchange in this division is subsidiary; rather the purpose is segregation to complete the benefit, and therefore he is compelled to accept it. And considering segregation, it is as if the room was his property from the beginning. Translation: And the proof of the two Shaykhs is that the testator bequeathed that property in which his ownership will be established through division, because it is apparent that the testator intended to bequeath property from which benefit can be obtained in every respect, and this (complete benefit) can only be through division, because benefit from shared property is limited. And when the room comes into the testator's share, his ownership becomes established in the entire room, so the bequest is effective in it. In this division, the meaning of exchange is subsidiary; the purpose is segregation, as if the room was the testator's property from the beginning. Explanation: The two Shaykhs argue that at the time of bequest, although Zayd did not own the entire room, there existed the possibility that through division his ownership in it would be established. And when Bakr knows that his partner has made a bequest of this room, he will also take it into consideration, because in such matters it is customary to take care. And from a shared property, full benefit cannot be obtained; rather benefit from it is limited. So Zayd's intention from the beginning was that after division this room would be handed over to Khalid, because Zayd's aim is that Khalid should obtain full benefit from this room, and this is not possible without division. In any case, when this was the intention from the beginning, and now after division the entire room has come into Zayd's ownership, the bequest will be executed and the entire room will be handed over to Khalid. As for Imam Muhammad's statement that in division there is the meaning of exchange which is like purchase, the answer is that in division both aspects of exchange and segregation exist. In animals and movables, the meaning of exchange predominates, while in a single genus, the meaning of segregation predominates. Here it is a single genus, so the meaning of segregation is primary, and the meaning of exchange is subdued and subsidiary. And because the meaning of segregation predominates here, compulsion in division is permissible; otherwise, where the meaning of exchange predominates, the judge's compulsion is not permissible (as has been detailed in the Book of Division). In any case, when the meaning of segregation predominates here, it becomes clear that it is as if this room was Zayd's property from the beginning; therefore the bequest will be effective in it. Further clarification of the mentioned issue: And if it falls in the other's share, it is executed in the amount of the entire dimensions that fell in his share, either because it is his substitute as we mentioned, or because the testator's intention in mentioning the house was to estimate by it to achieve his purpose as much as possible, except that the house is determined when it falls in his share, combining both aspects of estimation and ownership. And if it falls in the other's share, we act on estimation, either because he intended estimation on one consideration and ownership of the same on the other consideration.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of a bequest made in a shared property (musha') that later becomes exclusively owned by the testator through division (qismah). The passage opens with a ruling: if a testator bequeaths a shared room, and the room ends up in his share after division, the bequest is effective for his half (since at the time of bequest he only owned his share). If it falls in the other co-owner's share, the legatee (Khalid) gets a substitute from the testator's separate property. The main debate is between Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani and the two Shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). Imam Muhammad views division as resembling an exchange (mubadalah) akin to purchase; thus, just as selling the bequeathed property invalidates the bequest, division should also invalidate it unless the original co-owner (Bakr) permits. The two Shaykhs argue that division, especially of real estate of a single genus, is fundamentally segregation (ifraz) to complete benefit, not an exchange. The meaning of exchange is subsidiary. Therefore, the bequest is effective if the room falls in the testator's share, as if he owned it from the start. The text then provides an analogy: if a bequeathed slave-girl is accidentally killed, the substitute (compensation) inherits the bequest, but if the testator sells the slave, the bequest is void because sale indicates retraction; division does not indicate retraction. The commentary explains that in division of a single genus, segregation predominates, so the testator's intention to give full benefit to the legatee is realized. The final Arabic portion clarifies that if the room goes to the other co-owner, the legatee gets substitute property from the testator's share.

Key Terms
قسمت (qismah): Division of jointly owned property, either by mutual agreement or by court order.
مبادلہ (mubadalah): Exchange; in division, the aspect of exchanging shares.
افراز (ifraz): Segregation; separating shares without implying exchange.
مشاع (musha'): Undivided share in joint property; property owned in common without physical division.
موصی بہ (musa bihi): The specific property or asset that is bequeathed in a will.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (the two Shaykhs), what happens if a testator bequeaths a room in a jointly owned house, and after division the room falls in the testator's share?
A) The bequest becomes void because division is like a sale.
B) The bequest is effective for the entire room because division is segregation, as if the room was his from the start.
C) The bequest requires the co-owner's permission to be valid.
D) The bequest is only valid if the testator repurchases the room.

Key Takeaway
Division of a single genus property is segregation, so a bequest of a musha' share remains valid if the item falls in the testator's share.

Wasiyyah — Bequest
intermediate
10 min
Bequest of a Specific Room in Joint Property: Rulings and Dispute
Explains the validity of a bequest of a specific room after partition and the intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the validity of a bequest of a specific room in joint property and identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference) between the Shaykhain and Imam Muhammad.

Core Idea
The bequest of a room in joint property is valid retroactively if the room falls into the testator's share after partition (Shaykhain's view).

Bequeathing a specific item that you partially own raises questions of validity and execution. This lesson examines a classic case: a testator bequeaths a room in a house he owns jointly with a partner. After his death, the house is partitioned. What happens if the bequeathed room falls into his share or into his partner's share? The Hanafi school is divided on this, and understanding the reasoning behind each position sharpens your ability to handle wills involving joint property.

Guided Path
1
State the Issue
The testator bequeaths a specific room in a jointly owned house. At the time of bequest, he owned an undivided share, not the room itself. After his death, the house is partitioned. Determine the validity and execution of the bequest.
2
Identify the Two Positions
The Shaykhain (Imam Abu Hanifa & Abu Yusuf) hold that partition is primarily segregation (ifraz) with subsidiary exchange; it gives retroactive ownership, so if the room falls into the testator's share, the bequest is valid for the exact room. Imam Muhammad holds that partition is an exchange (mubadala) akin to purchase, so the bequest becomes effective only after partition and only from the testator's share.
3
Analyze Each Position's Proof (Dalil)
Shaykhain: The usufruct of joint property is limited; the testator intended full benefit. The exchange in partition is subsidiary; the main purpose is segregation. Imam Muhammad: Partition is a mutual exchange, so ownership transfers only upon partition, not retroactively.
Both sides use the same event but differ on its legal nature.
4
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
If the room falls into the testator's share: Shaykhain give the exact room; Imam Muhammad would also execute the bequest from the testator's share but not necessarily the same room (if the room falls into the partner's share, compensation based on measure). If the room falls into the partner's share: Shaykhain act on estimation (taqdir) and give compensation; Imam Muhammad also gives compensation but sees it as the only option.
The practical difference is whether the exact room is delivered or not.
5
Evaluate the Relied-Upon Position (Mufta Bihi)
The text elaborates the Shaykhain's view and provides responses, indicating their opinion is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi madhhab.
The passage uses analogical reasoning (talil) to defend the Shaykhain's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و ذالک يكون بالقسمة لان الانتفاع بالمشاع قاصر وقد استقر ملكه في جميع البيت اذا وقع في نصيبه فتنفذ الوصية فيه ومعنى المبادلة فى هذه القسمة تابع وانما المقصود الافراز تكميلا للمنفعة ولهذا يجبر على فيه وعلى اعتبار الافراز يصير كان البيت ملكه من الابتداء وان وقع فى نصيب الآخر تنفذ في قدر ذرعان جميعه مما وقع فى نصيبه اما لانه عوضه كما ذكرناه اولان مراد الموصى من ذكر البيت التقدير به تحصيلا لمقصوده ما امكن الا انه يتعين البيت اذا وقع في نصيبه جمعابين الجهتين التقدير والتمليك وان وقع فى نصيب الاخر عملنا بالتقدير اولانه اراد التقدير على اعتبار احد الوجهين والتمليك بعينه على اعتبار الوجه الاخر كما اذا علق عتق الولد وطلاق المراة باول ولد تلده امته فالمراد فى جزاء الطلاق مطلق الولد وفي العتق ولد حى
And that is through partition because the usufruct of the joint property is limited, and his ownership has become established in the entire house when it falls into his share, so the bequest is executed in it. And the meaning of exchange in this partition is subsidiary; the intended purpose is only segregation to complete the benefit, and for this reason he is compelled upon it. And upon considering segregation, it becomes as if the house was his property from the beginning. And if it falls into the share of the other, it is executed according to the measure of the entire [room] from what fell into his share; either because it is its equivalent as we mentioned, or because the intention of the testator in mentioning the room is estimation by it to achieve his objective as much as possible. But the room is determined when it falls into his share, combining both aspects of estimation and ownership. And if it falls into the share of the other, we act upon estimation; either because he intended estimation according to one of the two aspects, and actual ownership according to the other aspect. Just as when he suspended the freeing of a child and the divorce of a woman upon the first child his slave woman gives birth to, then the intention regarding the penalty of divorce is an absolute child, and regarding freeing, a living child.
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from Ashraf al-Hidaya on a ruling from Al-Hidayah concerning the bequest of a specific room in a jointly owned house. It presents the position of the Shaykhain (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) and contrasts it with the view of Imam Muhammad. The Shaykhain argue that partition (qismah) is primarily a segregation (ifraz) to complete the benefit, and it establishes the testator's ownership retroactively. Therefore, if the room falls into the testator's share, the bequest is valid for the entire room. Imam Muhammad considers partition as an exchange (mubadala) akin to purchase, so the bequest becomes effective only after partition, and if the room falls into the other partner's share, the bequest is executed according to the measure of the room from the testator's share, either as an equivalent or based on the testator's intention of estimation (taqdir). The passage then provides an analogy: when a man suspends the freeing of a child and the divorce of his wife upon the first child born to his slave woman, for divorce the intention is an absolute child (alive or dead), but for freeing it must be a live child. This illustrates the principle of interpreting the testator's intention to combine both possibilities when possible, and to prioritize one when not. The commentary follows the author's order and emphasizes the reasoning behind the Shaykhain's view.

Key Terms
مشاع (mushā‘): Jointly owned undivided property where each co-owner has a share in the entirety without specific demarcation.
افراز (ifrāz): Segregation or partition that separates the shares of co-owners, making each share specific.
مبادلة (mubādala): Exchange; in the context of partition, the transfer of one share for another to achieve equality.
تقدير (taqdīr): Estimation; in this context, the testator's mention of the room is considered as an estimation of value rather than specific designation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Shaykhain (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), if a person bequeaths a specific room in a jointly owned house and the room falls into the testator's share after partition, what is the ruling?
A) The bequest is invalid because the testator did not own the room at the time of bequest.
B) The bequest is valid for the entire room, as if the testator owned it from the beginning.
C) The bequest is valid only to the extent of the testator's share in the room.
D) The bequest is treated as a general bequest of value, not the specific room.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi madhhab (on the Shaykhain's view) validates a bequest of a specific room in joint property if that room falls into the testator's share upon partition, due to the principle that partition perfects ownership retroactively.

Wasiyyah — Bequest
intermediate
8 min
Analogy and Division Method for Bequest of Room in Partner's Share
Analogy and division calculation for bequest of room.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply Imam Muhammad's division method to a bequest of a room in jointly owned property and explain the analogy from conditional emancipation/divorce.

Core Idea
A single expression can bear different meanings in different contexts, affecting legal outcomes.

In this lesson, we explore a nuanced ruling from the Hanafi school regarding a bequest of a specific room that may fall into the partner's share rather than the testator's. The author uses an analogy from conditional emancipation and divorce to illustrate how context determines the intended meaning of a testator's words. We then examine Imam Muhammad's precise division method to calculate the legatee's and heirs' shares.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Analogy from Conditional Emancipation/Divorce
Consider a man who says: 'When my slave-girl gives birth to her first child, that child is free and my wife is divorced.' For divorce, any child (live or stillborn) triggers it; for emancipation, only a live child triggers freedom. The same expression 'first child' has different meanings in different contexts.
This shows that a single phrase can be interpreted differently based on the legal consequence.
2
Identify the Parallel with the Bequest Case
Similarly, a testator says: 'I bequeath this room to X.' If the room falls in his share, the specific room is given. If it falls in the partner's share, an equivalent place is given. The words 'this room' refer to the physical room if possible, otherwise to a substitute.
The analogy clarifies that intention may shift depending on circumstances.
3
Recognize the Division Problem
When the room (10 cubits) falls in the partner's share, the testator's half of the house (50 cubits) must be divided between the legatee and the testator's heirs. The legatee is entitled to half the room's area (5 cubits) as substitute.
The division only concerns the testator's share, not the entire house.
4
Apply Imam Muhammad's Calculation
Imam Muhammad: The testator's share (50 cubits) is divided into 10 shares of 5 cubits each. The legatee gets 1 share (5 cubits = half the room), and the heirs get 9 shares (45 cubits).
This method ensures the legatee receives exactly half the room's area.
5
Note the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
The text presents only Imam Muhammad's view. It is known that Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf may have different methods. The practical difference lies in the legatee's share amount.
This is a manqul ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school, not fully detailed here.

دس حصوں پر
تقسیم کا طریقہ
ثم اذا وقع البيت فى نصيب غير الموصى والدار مائة ذراع والبيت عشرة اذرع يقسم نصيبه بين الموصى له و بين الورثة على عشرة اسهم تسعة منها للورثة وسهم للموصى له وهذا عند محمد فيضرب الموصى له بخمسة اذرع نصف البيت ولهم بنصف الدار سوى البيت وهو خمسة واربعون فيجعل كل خمسة سهما فيصير عشرة ترجمہ پھر جب کہ کمرہ غیر موصی کے حصہ میں آئے اور حویلی سوگز ہو اور کمرہ دس گز ہوتو موصی کا حصہ موضی لڈ اور ورثا کے درمیان ت تقسیم کیا جائے گا ان میں سے نو ورثا کے لئے اور ایک حصہ موضی لا کے لئے ہے اور یہ محمد کے نزدیک ہے پس موصی لۂ نصف بیت کے تناسب سے پانچ گزلے گا اور ورثا کے لئے آدھی حویلی ہے کمرہ کے علاوہ اور وہ ( کمرہ کے علاوہ آدھی حویلی ) پینتالیس گز ہیں تو ہر پانچ گز کو ایک حصہ قرار دیا جائے گا تو دس حصے ہو جائیں گے۔ تشریح جب یہ معلوم ہو چکا ہے کہ اگر وہ کمرہ زید کے حصہ میں نہ آئے تو اس کے برابر زمین خالد کو دی جائے گی تو اس تقسیم کا کیا طریقہ ہوگا اگر چہ مسئلہ خود واضح تھا مگر مصنف نے اس کو بیان کیا ہے۔ فرمایا ہے کہ امام محمد کے نزدیک موصی لیہ کو کمرہ کے نصف کا عوض دیا جائیگا لہذا اگر پورا گھر سو گز ہے اور کمرہ دس گز ہے تو موضعی لن کو پانچ گرملیں گے یعنی زید کے حصہ میں دار کے پچاس گز آگئے اور کمرہ کا نصف پانچ گز ہے لہذا پانچ گز زمین زید کو دی جائے گی اور باقی پینتالیس گز زید کے ورثہ کے لئے ہوں گے۔
اس کو بالفاظ دیگر یوں کہ لیجئے کہ زید کے پورے ترکہ کے دس سہام کر کے ان میں سے نو زید کے ورثا کو اور ایک موصی لۂ کو دیا جائے گا کیونکہ پچاس میں سے پینتالیس (2) ہے اور پچاس میں سے پانچ ہے ہے، یہ تفصیل امام محمد کے نزدیک ہوگی کہ بنوارہ دس سہام پر ہوگا اور ہر پانچ گز کو ایک سہم قرار دیا جائے گا۔
Analogy of the issue:
Just as when he suspends the emancipation of a child and the divorce of his wife on the condition of the first child born to his slave-girl, then the meaning in the context of divorce is absolute child, and in emancipation is a living child.
Translation: Like when he suspends the emancipation of the child and the divorce of the wife on the first child born to his slave-girl, then the meaning in the penalty of divorce is absolute child, and in emancipation is a living child.
Explanation: This last answer given is that it is possible that the testator's intention from the beginning is that if this room comes into my share, this same is given; and if it does not come into my share, an equivalent place is given. Here the author presents its analogy. For example, Zaid has a slave-girl married to Khalid, and Zaid has a wife. Zaid says: When my slave-girl gives birth to her first child, that child is free and my wife is divorced. So when the child is born, it will be free and Zaid's wife will be divorced. But divorce and emancipation have separate meanings: for the occurrence of divorce, absolute child is intended, meaning whether born alive or dead, in both cases divorce occurs; and for emancipation, a living child is intended, meaning if she gives birth to a living child, the child is free, otherwise if stillborn, it is not free. Thus it is understood that Zaid intended absolute child for divorce and living child for emancipation. Similarly, here if the room comes into my share, this room is intended; if not, an equivalent place is intended.
On ten shares:
Method of division: Then when the room falls in the share of someone other than the testator, and the house is one hundred cubits and the room is ten cubits, his share is divided between the legatee and the heirs into ten shares: nine for the heirs and one for the legatee. This is according to Muhammad. So the legatee receives five cubits, half of the room, and they (the heirs) receive half the house excluding the room, which is forty-five cubits. Then every five cubits is made one share, so it becomes ten.
Translation: Then when the room falls in the share of someone other than the testator, and the house is one hundred cubits and the room is ten cubits, the testator's share is divided between the legatee and the heirs into ten shares: nine for the heirs and one for the legatee. This is according to Muhammad. So the legatee gets five cubits (half of the room), and the heirs get half the house excluding the room, which is forty-five cubits. Then every five cubits is considered one share, making ten shares.
Explanation: When it is established that if the room does not fall in Zaid's share, land equal to it is given to Khalid, what is the method of division? Although the issue is clear, the author has explained it. He said: According to Imam Muhammad, the legatee is given the substitute of half the room. So if the entire house is one hundred cubits and the room is ten cubits, the legatee receives five cubits. That is, from Zaid's share of the house (fifty cubits), half the room is five cubits, so five cubits of land are given to Zaid (the legatee? Actually it says 'Zaid ko di jayegi' but Zaid is the testator; the legatee is Khalid. The text says 'panch gaz zameen Zaid ko di jayegi' but it likely means the legatee, as Zaid is the testator. I will correct in commentary. The remaining forty-five cubits go to Zaid's heirs. In other words, make Zaid's entire estate into ten shares: nine for Zaid's heirs and one for the legatee. This is because fifty cubits (Zaid's half) minus five cubits (half the room) leaves forty-five cubits, which is nine parts of five cubits each. This detail is according to Imam Muhammad: the division is into ten shares, each share being five cubits.
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah provides an analogy (nazir) and a calculation method (taqseem ka tareeqa) for the bequest of a room in jointly owned property. The passage type is intra-Hanafi dispute (mentioning Imam Muhammad's view specifically). First, the author gives an analogy from the case of conditional emancipation and divorce: if a man says, 'When my slave-girl gives birth to her first child, the child is free and my wife is divorced,' then for divorce any child (live or stillborn) counts, but for emancipation only a live child counts. This illustrates that a single expression can have different intended meanings depending on context. Similarly, in the bequest case, the testator's mentioning of 'this room' may mean the specific room if it falls in his share, or an equivalent if it does not. Then the author explains the division method according to Imam Muhammad. If the house is 100 cubits and the room is 10 cubits, and the room falls in the partner's share, then from the testator's share (50 cubits) the legatee gets half the room's area (5 cubits) and the heirs get the remaining 45 cubits. The total testator's share is divided into 10 parts of 5 cubits each: 9 parts for heirs, 1 for legatee. This is Imam Muhammad's position. The text does not mention the views of Abu Hanifa or Abu Yusuf, but it is known that they may have different methods. The ruling is from the Hidayah commentary, and Imam Muhammad's view is presented as the operative method here.

Key Terms
نظیر (nazir): Analogy or parallel case used to illustrate a ruling.
عتق (itq): Emancipation of a slave; setting free.
سہم (sahm): Share or portion in division of property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, if the house is 100 cubits, the room is 10 cubits, and the room falls in the partner's share, how many shares of the testator's inheritance does the legatee receive?
A) 1 share
B) 5 shares
C) 9 shares
D) 10 shares

Key Takeaway
When a bequeathed room falls in the partner's share, Imam Muhammad calculates the legatee's substitute as half the room's area, taken from the testator's share divided into ten parts.
